Proof from Challenge to Wish for Death
Maturidi argues from the Qur'anic challenge to the Jews to wish for death, with objection and refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two-fold rational proof for Muhammad's prophethood based on the Qur'anic challenge to the Jews and the mubahala with Christians, and how Maturidi refutes a skeptical objection.

Core Idea
The Jews' failure to wish for death proves Muhammad's prophethood despite its ease.

Maturidi uses a powerful Qur'anic challenge to demonstrate the truth of Muhammad's prophethood. By analyzing the Jews' response to the call to 'wish for death' and the mubahala with Christians, he builds a compelling argument. This lesson unpacks the proof and addresses a sophisticated objection.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic passage once, then its English translation. Note the two main parts: the proof and the objection-response.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the two aspects of the proof
Maturidi presents two aspects from 'Wish for death' and the mubahala. Find them and understand how each supports prophethood.
The first aspect is the promised death; the second is the impossibility of them wishing.
3
Understand al-Warraq's objection
The objector raises two points: the wish might be only in the heart, and the Jews already had knowledge from earlier prophets like astrology.
Al-Warraq is a known skeptic.
4
Trace the refutation
Follow Maturidi's responses: the mubahala context requires a genuine wish, and the Jews would have challenged other prophecies if they had such knowledge.
Notice how he uses Quranic verses about entering the mosque and prevailing religion.
5
Reflect on the jurist's addition
The jurist adds that the Prophet's challenge was effective precisely because he knew they would not wish. This reinforces the strength of the proof.
This shows the argument is based on known psychology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واحتج في إثبات رسالة محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم مع ما بينا بقوله لليهود: فَتَمَنَّوُا الْمَوْتَ، بوجهين: أحدهما الوعد بأنهم لو تمنوا الموت لماتوا، والثاني أنهم لا يتمنون أبدا، ولا شيء أيسر عليهم من تمنى ذلك، وبمباهلة النصارى والإخبار بوقوع اللعن، ثبت أنه معلوم النعت في كتبهم. فأدخل الوراق أنهم لو تمنوا باللسان لقيل إنما أريد به القلب، والثاني أنهم قد آمنوا بموسى وعيسى، وقد أخبراهم بذلك كما يخبر المنجمة. فجواب الأول أن المباهلة لا تحتمل ذلك، وأيضا إنهم أهل بصر، إذا لو ردوا لقابلوا بأنهم فعلوا ذلك أيضا بقلوبهم والحرف الثاني لو كان كذلك ما امتنعوا عن مقابلته عند قوله: لَتَدْخُلُنَّ الْمَسْجِدَ الْحَرَامَ وقوله: لِيُظْهِرَهُ عَلَى الدِّينِ كُلِّهِ، ولو كان بذلك كان التصديق لما احتمل المقابلة بأعز الأشياء وهى الأنفس والأموال. قال الفقيه رحمه الله: وأيضا أنه لو كان بالذي ذكر لم يكن خير رسول الله لن يتمنوه بذلك، بل كان بالذي يعلم أنهم لا يفعلون ولا قوة إلا بالله، وطعن، ولو كان على حكم قول المنجمة لما تقرر عندهم حتى يتحرجوا الإجابة، لم يكن الذي جاء به رسول الله بدون ذلك لم يتحرجوا عما خوفهم فيسلموا ولا قوة إلا بالله.
And he argued for establishing the message of Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, along with what we have explained, by His saying to the Jews: 'Then wish for death' in two ways: one is the promise that if they wished for death they would die, and the second is that they will never wish for it, and nothing is easier for them than that wish; and by the imprecation of the Christians and the announcement of the occurrence of the curse, it is established that he is described in their books. So al-Warraq objected that if they wished with the tongue, it might be said that the heart was intended; and secondly, that they already believed in Moses and Jesus, and they informed them of that as astrologers inform. The answer to the first is that the imprecation does not admit that; also, they are people of insight; if they had replied they would have said that they did that also with their hearts. As for the second point, if it were so, they would not have refrained from confronting Him when He said: 'You will surely enter the Sacred Mosque' and His saying: 'That He may make it prevail over all religion'; and if that were so, the affirmation would not have allowed confrontation with the most precious things, namely lives and wealth. The jurist, may God have mercy on him, said: And also, if it were as mentioned, the goodness of the Messenger of God would not have been that they would not wish for it; rather it would have been that He knows they do not do it—and there is no power except through God—and he objected. And if it were according to the rule of astrologers, it would not have been settled among them until they were reluctant to answer; what the Messenger of God brought would not have been without that; they would not have been reluctant regarding what He threatened them with to surrender, and there is no power except through God.
Source pages p. 794

Commentary
This passage is a detailed argument for Muhammad's prophethood using the Quranic challenge to the Jews (Quran 2:94) and the mubahala (imprecation) with Christians. Maturidi explains two aspects of the proof: first, the Jews would have died if they wished for death, and second, they will never wish for it even though it is easy for them. This, combined with the mubahala with Christians, shows that Muhammad's description is in their scriptures. Then an objection from 'al-Warraq' (Ibn al-Rawandi) is presented: the wish might be only in the heart, and the Jews already believed in Moses and Jesus who informed them like astrologers. The answer refutes both points: the mubahala context requires actual wish, and the Jews are insightful; if they had wished in their hearts they would have said so. Regarding the second objection, Maturidi points out that the Jews did not confront the Prophet on other clear challenges (like entering the Sacred Mosque or the religion prevailing), which they would have done if they had such astrological knowledge. The jurist adds that the Prophet's challenge was effective precisely because he knew they would not wish for death, and if it were like astrology, they would not have been threatened to the point of surrender.

Key Terms
المباهلة
الوراق
المنجمة
التمني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the proof only works if the Jews actually wished with the tongue; Maturidi clarifies the mubahala context makes the outward wish necessary.
Correction: The mubahala context requires a genuine outward wish, not just a heart intention, so the objection fails.

Checkpoint
What is the second aspect of the proof from 'Wish for death' according to Maturidi?
A) The Jews will never wish for death even though it is easy.
B) The Jews actually wished for death and died.
C) The Jews were afraid to die.
D) The Jews were commanded to fight.

Key Takeaway
The Jews' persistent refusal to wish for death, despite its ease, combined with the mubahala, provides a compelling rational proof for Muhammad's prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Jews could not bring themselves to wish for death even though it was 'easier than anything' for them. What is the one simple act of obedience that you keep avoiding, knowing it would prove or strengthen your faith? Will you do it today?
?
Al-Warraq objected that the wish could be in the heart, but Maturidi says the mubahala requires outward action. Is your faith merely internal, or does it manifest in visible deeds that others can challenge? What outward step have you been hiding behind an 'inner intention'?
?
If you knew that a single sincere declaration could expose the truth of your beliefs, would you make it? The Jews' silence condemned them. What silence in your life condemns you, and what would it cost to break it?

Refutation of the Memorization Objection
Maturidi refutes the objection that memorization replaces a book.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's refutation of the claim that the Prophet's illiteracy could be negated by memorization, and the importance of empirical testimony in confirming miracles.

Core Idea
Memorization proves recitation; absence of prior recitation proves illiteracy.

In this passage, Maturidi addresses an objection to the miracle of the Prophet's illiteracy (ummiyya). The objector suggests that memorization could serve as a book, implying the Prophet might have learned from previous scriptures. Maturidi refutes this by highlighting the dependency of memorization on recitation and the public witness of the Prophet's community.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Notice the objection and the immediate refutation.
The objector's claim is that memorization can substitute for a book.
2
Identify the two refutations
Maturidi gives two arguments: the logical (memorization requires recitation) and the empirical (the Prophet's known life). Find both.
The second argument relies on the testimony of the Prophet's own people.
3
Connect to the broader theme
Reflect on how this refutation strengthens the miracle of the Quran and the Prophet's prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وطعن في قوله: وَمَا كُنْتَ تَتْلُوا مِنْ قَبْلِهِ مِنْ كِتَابٍ، إن الحفظ يقوم مقام الكتاب، وأحال؛ لأن الحفظ يكون عن تلاوة، وما بالإلقاء عليه فهو عن كتاب يقرأ. وبعد، فإنما ذلك إنما يكون بمن يظهر اختلافه عند من يعرف به، ومعلوم بين أظهرهم، لم يعرف في شيء من ذلك، وأنه نشأ بين أظهرهم، ولولا ذلك لكان هذا القدر من المقابلة سهلا لا يعجزون عنه.
And he objected to His saying: 'And you did not recite before it any book' – that memorization takes the place of a book, and he considered it impossible; because memorization comes from recitation, and what is inspired to him is from a book that is read. And furthermore, that only occurs in someone whose difference appears to those who know him, and he was known among them, he was not known for any of that, and he grew up among them. And were it not for that, this amount of opposition would be easy and not beyond them.
Source pages p. 795

Commentary
This passage presents an objection to the verse 'You did not recite before it any book' (Quran 29:48) and its refutation. The objector claims that memorization (hifz) could substitute for reciting a book, so the Prophet might have memorized previous scriptures. Maturidi refutes by pointing out that memorization depends on prior recitation; one cannot memorize without reciting. Furthermore, the Prophet grew up among his people who knew him, and he was never known to have studied any scripture. If the objection had merit, his opponents would have easily challenged him on this point, but they did not, proving his illiteracy was genuine.

Key Terms
الحفظ
التلاوة
الأمية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some argue that oral tradition alone could make one learned, so the Prophet might have acquired knowledge without formal recitation.
Correction: Maturidi insists that memorization comes from recitation; the Prophet had no previous recitation or study.

Checkpoint
What is Maturidi's refutation of the claim that memorization replaces a book?
A) Memorization is impossible without recitation.
B) The Prophet was illiterate and could not memorize.
C) The Prophet's people confirmed he never studied.
D) Both A and C.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's illiteracy is confirmed by both logical necessity and historical testimony, making it a clear miracle.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You say you believe that the Quran is from God, but have you ever truly sat with the miracle of an illiterate man bringing a book that challenges all of humanity? If you had lived among the Prophet, would you have recognized the truth, or would you have been among those who objected?
?
The Prophet's life was an open book; every detail was known. If your own life were as closely examined, would it bear witness to your faith, or would it reveal contradictions you hide?
?
Maturidi refutes a superficial objection with clear logic. What intellectual objections do you secretly hold against revelation? Are you willing to bring them into the light and let the truth dismantle them, or do you prefer the comfort of doubt?

Ibn al-Rawandi's Objections to Tawatur
Maturidi records and refutes Ibn al-Rawandi's objections to tawatur.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ibn al-Rawandi's three objections to the tawatur of the Qur'an and prophetic reports, and Maturidi's initial refutation that the Qur'an was narrated by the entire community.

Core Idea
The Qur'an is not a solitary report; it was narrated by the entire community.

In this passage, Maturidi records Ibn al-Rawandi's challenge to the mass transmission of the Qur'an. Ibn al-Rawandi claims the Qur'an is a solitary report and casts doubt on tawatur itself, also citing the consensus of Jews and Christians. Maturidi counters that the Qur'an was transmitted by the whole community, making it mutawatir beyond doubt.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get the flow of the objection and initial refutation.
Notice that Maturidi begins with a brief rebuttal before listing Ibn al-Rawandi's points.
2
Identify the three objections
List the three specific objections Ibn al-Rawandi raises: (1) Qur'an is khabar al-ahad, (2) tawatur is unreliable due to distance/nearness, (3) consensus of Jews and Christians undermines Islamic consensus.
These objections target the reliability of transmission.
3
Analyze Maturidi's response
For each objection, see how Maturidi responds. He calls the first claim false, noting the community narrated it. He briefly refutes the second and third, but the full refutation comes later.
Maturidi's style is to state the objection and then respond succinctly.
4
Connect to the broader argument
Understand that these objections set up the need for a systematic argument about the spread of reports, which Maturidi provides next.
This lesson prepares for the foundational principle in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الفقيه رحمه الله: وأيضا أنه لو كان بالذي ذكر لم يكن خير رسول الله لن يتمنوه بذلك، بل كان بالذي يعلم أنهم لا يفعلون ولا قوة إلا بالله. وطعن في أخبار القرآن، إنه خبر الآحاد، وذلك كذب، بل رواه كافة كافة، مع وطعن التواتر بما لا تخلو الجماعة عن البعد من السمع فيحتمل الحيلة، القرب فلا يحتمل مباشرة مثله إلا اليسير. قال ابن الروندى: هذه الجهلة بالمحافل وإلا الأمر في ذلك ينتشر ما كان من ... قبل حتى لا يكاد شيء منه يخفى على الأبعدين فضلا عن الأقربين. وطعن أيضا بإجماعات اليهود والنصارى، قال ابن الروندى: إما أن يتكر الخبر البتة فيبطل مذهبه في تقليد الماني وقوله هذا، أو يجيز خبرا، لا بد إذ ذاك من الرجوع إلى إجماع أهل الحق في الأصول العقلية فيقبل أخبارهم وإجماعاتهم؛ إذ هم المتمسكون به، ونحن أولئك بحمد الله. قال الشيخ رحمه الله: والأصل في هذا أن الأخبار التي لزم في العقول قبولها لما في ذلك بطلان حكمة السمع واللسان وفيه زوال علوم المعاش والمعاد وانقطاع الأصول إلى الأغذية والأدوية التي بها حياة الأبدان. ثم كانت الأخبار تتفاقم في الانتشار على قدر الأمور التي عنها الأخبار في العظم نحو ملك لو قتل لانتشر أمره بالضرورة حتى لو أحب الناس كتمان مثله لما قدروا عليه، وكذلك الخارجة من المعارف المعتادة، وفيما يقل خطره أو يجرى على المعتاد لا يظهر ظهوره، بل لعله لا يذكر، معروف ذلك في الخلقة، وعلى ذلك انتشرت أخبار الفتوح وقهر الملوك، فعلى مثل هذا أمر الرسل؛ لأنهم جاءوا بالأمور العظام الخارجة عن الأمر المعتاد عنا عندهم، فيظهر أخبارهم فتنتشر حتى تبلغ أقاصى الدنيا وأدانيها؛ إذ هي على وجه لا يملك السامعون كتمانها، على ما ذكرت من تغاضى الخلقة في نشر مثله مع ما قد ينتشر مثل ما ذكرت مما لا منفعة فيه، فالذي الخلق جميعا معناه أحق في ذلك، وفي كل أمر منتشر عن يعود الخير إن كان على حق أو جور، فيعلم ما افتعل منه فيغير، وما صدق فيه فيقر وفي ذلك لزوم انتشار أخبار الرسل في حياتهم وظهور المفتعل من ذلك فيمحى أثره بالنهى والتغيير، فيبقى الحق الصدق منه، دليل ذلك أمر رسول الله، حتى لا تأتي ناحية نائية ولا مكانا بعيدا إلا وجدت أثره فيه ظاهرا، وبخاصة في عصره، إذ كان ينساب إليه من الآفاق ويظهر شأنه في البلاد، فإذا كان كذلك لا وجه لقوله أخباره أخبار الآحاد، ولا لما ذكر من الوجوه، بل الخبر الواحد في الأمر أو الخارج عن الأمر المعتاد ينتشر انتشارا أظهر، فكيف فيما فيه دعاء أهل الأديان، وإرسال الكتب إلى الأفق، ومجيء الوفود من كل النواحي، وامتحان أحد.
The faqih, may Allah have mercy on him, said: Also, if it were as mentioned, the goodness of the Messenger of Allah would not have been such that they desired it by that, but rather it was by that which He knows they do not do, and there is no power except with Allah. And he objected to the reports of the Qur'an, that it is a solitary report (khabar al-ahad), and that is false; rather, the entire community narrated it, along with objecting to tawatur (mass transmission) that the group is never free from the distance of hearing, so it admits of trickery, and nearness does not admit of direct like it except rarely. Ibn al-Rawandi said: These ignorant people in the assemblies, otherwise the matter in that spreads what was... before until scarcely anything of it is hidden from the furthest, let alone the nearest. And he also objected by the consensus of the Jews and Christians. Ibn al-Rawandi said: Either the report is absolutely rejected, thus his doctrine in following al-Mani and this statement of his becomes invalid, or he permits a report; then it is necessary to refer to the consensus of the people of truth in rational principles, so their reports and consensuses are accepted, for they are the adherents of it, and we are those, praise be to Allah. The Shaykh, may Allah have mercy on him, said: The foundation in this is that reports whose acceptance is necessary in intellects, because in that is the invalidation of the wisdom of hearing and speech, and in it is the loss of the sciences of livelihood and afterlife, and the cutting off of origins to foods and medicines by which is the life of bodies. Then reports increase in spread according to the magnitude of the matters about which they are reports; for example, a king if killed, his affair spreads necessarily, even if people wished to conceal something like it they would not be able to. Likewise, what is outside customary knowledge; but regarding what is of little significance or proceeds customarily, it does not appear manifestly; rather, perhaps it is not mentioned; that is known in creation. And upon that spread the reports of conquests and the subjugation of kings. So upon the like of this is the affair of the messengers, because they came with great matters outside the customary affair from us in their view, so their reports appear and spread until they reach the farthest and nearest parts of the world, for they are in a manner that the hearers cannot conceal them, as I mentioned of the natural disposition in spreading the like of it, along with what may spread like what I mentioned that has no benefit. So that which all of creation is meant by it is more worthy in that, and in every matter that spreads concerning which good returns, whether it is right or wrong, so what is fabricated from it is known and changed, and what is truthful in it is established. And in that is the necessary spread of the reports of the messengers in their lifetimes and the appearance of what is fabricated from that, so its trace is erased by prohibition and change, so the truthful truth remains from it. The proof of that is the affair of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), such that no remote region nor distant place comes except you find his trace in it manifest, especially in his era, for he was proceeding to him from the horizons and his affair appeared in the lands. So if it is like that, there is no justification for saying his reports are solitary reports, nor for what is mentioned of the aspects. Rather, the solitary report about a matter or what is outside the customary affair spreads with a more manifest spreading; how then concerning what involves the call of the people of religions, the sending of letters to the horizon, the coming of delegations from every direction, and the testing of one.
Source pages p. 795

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of Ibn al-Rawandi's objection to the tawatur (mass transmission) of the Qur'an and prophetic reports. The author begins by quoting Ibn al-Rawandi's claim that the Qur'an is only a solitary report (khabar al-ahad), which is false because it was narrated by the entire community. Ibn al-Rawandi also objects to tawatur itself, arguing that if a group is distant they may be deceived, and if near they cannot directly experience such events except rarely. He further cites the consensus of Jews and Christians as problematic. The response from the Shaykh (Maturidi) begins with the foundational principle: reports that reason must accept are necessary, because rejecting them would invalidate the wisdom of hearing and speech, leading to loss of knowledge for this life and the next, and cutting off the sources of food and medicine that sustain the body. Then he explains that the spread of reports is proportional to the greatness of the events. For example, the death of a king spreads necessarily, and people cannot conceal it. Similarly, extraordinary events spread widely, while trivial or customary matters may not. The same applies to the messengers: they came with great extraordinary matters, so their reports appear and spread universally—hearers cannot conceal them. This is supported by the natural disposition of creation, which spreads even useless news. All the more so for the prophetic mission, which involves the call to religion, sending letters, and delegations. The argument concludes that the reports of the Prophet (peace be upon him) spread even in his lifetime, reaching every distant place, so they cannot be solitary. Rather, even a solitary report about an extraordinary matter spreads more manifestly, let alone such a momentous affair.

Key Terms
خبر الآحاد
تواتر
إجماع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the Qur'an is a solitary report that could be doubted.
Correction: Maturidi argues that the Qur'an was transmitted by the entire community, making it mutawatir and beyond doubt.

Checkpoint
What is Maturidi's initial response to Ibn al-Rawandi's claim that the Qur'an is khabar al-ahad?
A) He admits it and tries to justify it.
B) He says it is false because the entire community narrated it.
C) He cites a verse from the Qur'an.
D) He ignores the claim.

Key Takeaway
Ibn al-Rawandi's objections are refuted by the fact that the Qur'an was transmitted by the entire community, making it mutawatir.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Qur'an, do you ever stop to consider that it reached you through a chain of millions of people across generations? How does that reality change your sense of responsibility to pass it on accurately to others?
?
Ibn al-Rawandi's objections represent a deep skepticism about the transmission of divine revelation. Is there any area of your faith where you harbor such skepticism? What would it take for you to surrender that doubt completely?
?
The passage emphasizes that the Qur'an was narrated by the entire community, not just a few. Are you actively part of that community's mission to transmit the Qur'an, or are you a passive recipient? What is one concrete step you will take this week to become a transmitter of Allah's word?

Prophethood
intermediate
7 min
The Spread of Prophetic News Proves Tawatur
Maturidi argues that great events cause widespread reports, proving prophetic reports are mutawatir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that great events like the prophetic mission necessarily cause widespread reports, proving tawatur.

Core Idea
Great events inevitably spread; prophetic reports are among the greatest.

Maturidi now lays out the foundational principle: reports that reason must accept are necessary for knowledge. He then argues that the spread of reports is proportional to the magnitude of the event. Since the prophetic mission is extraordinarily great, its reports spread universally and cannot be concealed, thus they are mutawatir.

Guided Path
1
Read the foundational principle
Read the opening where Maturidi states that accepting certain reports is necessary, otherwise knowledge of this world and the next is lost.
This sets the stakes: rejecting tawatur leads to skepticism.
2
Understand the proportionality argument
Maturidi explains that reports spread more widely as events are greater. Examples: a king's death, conquests, and extraordinary occurrences.
Compare trivial versus significant events.
3
Apply to the messengers
Messengers brought the greatest matters, so their reports spread to the furthest regions. Even hearers cannot conceal them, due to natural disposition.
This is the core analogy.
4
Confirm with the Prophet's example
Maturidi points to the Prophet Muhammad: his traces were found everywhere in his lifetime, with delegations and letters reaching distant lands.
This is empirical proof of the argument.
5
Draw the conclusion
Since prophetic reports spread so widely, they cannot be solitary. Therefore, Ibn al-Rawandi's objection is invalid.
The argument is complete.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

السامعون كتمانها، على ما ذكرت من تغاضى الخلقة في نشر مثله مع ما قد ينتشر مثل ما ذكرت مما لا منفعة فيه، فالذي الخلق جميعا معناه أحق في ذلك، وفي كل أمر منتشر عن يعود الخير إن كان على حق أو جور، فيعلم ما Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that prophetic reports could be solitary and unreliable because they were not directly witnessed by everyone.
Correction: Maturidi argues that the extraordinary nature of the prophetic mission ensures widespread dissemination, making them mutawatir by necessity.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what determines the extent of spread of reports?
A) The number of narrators
B) The magnitude of the event
C) The literacy of the community
D) The political power of the narrator

Key Takeaway
The prophetic mission is the greatest event, so its reports spread universally, proving tawatur and refuting the claim of khabar al-ahad.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The spread of the Prophet's message is undeniable, reaching every remote place. How have you allowed that message to spread into the hidden corners of your own heart? Or have you kept some areas sealed off from his authority? What will you do today to open those areas?
?
Maturidi says fabricated reports are known and erased. Think of the false narratives you have entertained about Islam, the Prophet, or yourself. Are you actively seeking to identify and erase them, or do you passively let them linger? Commit to one specific falsehood you will replace with the truth from this lesson.
?
If the prophetic reports are as clear as the news of a king's death, why does your action not match your knowledge? What is the missing link between your intellectual acceptance of tawatur and your daily obedience? Stop rationalizing and identify the real barrier, then resolve to remove it today.

The Principle of Necessary Reports and Spread by Magnitude
Maturidi states the principle of necessary reports and their spread by magnitude.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why reports of extraordinary events necessarily spread widely, based on the principle that the spread corresponds to the magnitude of the event.

Core Idea
Great events produce irresistible reports; prophetic missions are the greatest events.

Maturidi begins by establishing a fundamental principle: reports that are necessary for the intellect to accept are those without which the very functions of hearing and speech, and the sciences of life and afterlife, would be nullified. He then explains that the spread of reports is proportional to the significance of the event, using the example of a king's assassination spreading uncontrollably.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle
Read the first part of the passage where Maturidi states the principle: reports necessary for the intellect to accept are those without which hearing and speech and the sciences of life and afterlife would be nullified.
2
Examine the analogy of the king
Notice how Maturidi uses the example of a king's assassination to illustrate that reports of great events spread inevitably, even if people try to conceal them.
3
Apply to prophets
Understand that prophets brought matters greater than any king's death, so their reports must spread to all parts of the world.
This sets the stage for the detailed argument in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وطعن أيضا بإجماعات اليهود والنصارى ، قال ابن الروندى : إما أن يتكر الخبر البتة فيبطل مذهبه فى تقليد المانى وقوله هذا ، أو يجيز خبرا ، لا بد إذ ذاك من الرجوع إلى إجماع أهل الحق فى الأصول العقلية فيقبل أخبارهم وإجماعاتهم ؛ إذ هم المتمسكون به ، ونحن أولئك بحمد الله . قال الشيخ رحمه الله : والأصل فى هذا أن الأخبار التي لزم في العقول قبولها لما في ذلك بطلان حكمة السمع واللسان وفيه زوال علوم المعاش والمعاد وانقطاع الأصول إلى الأغذية والأدوية التي بها حياة الأبدان . ثم كانت الأخبار تتفاقم في الانتشار على قدر الأمور التي عنها الأخبار في العظم نحو ملك لو قتل لا نتشر أمره بالضرورة حتى لو أحب الناس كتمان مثله لما قدروا عليه ، وكذلك الخارجة من المعارف المعتادة ، وفيما يقل خطره أو يجرى على المعتاد لا يظهر ظهوره ، بل لعله لا يذكر ، معروف ذلك فى الخلقة ، وعلى ذلك انتشرت أخبار الفتوح وقهر الملوك ، فعلى مثل هذا أمر الرسل ؛ لأنهم جاءوا بالأمور العظام الخارجة عن الأمر المعتاد عنا عندهم ، فيظهر أخبارهم فتنتشر حتى تبلغ أقاصى الدنيا وأدانيها ؛ إذ هى على وجه لا يملك السامعون كتمانها ، على ما ذكرت من تغاضى الخلقة في نشر مثله مع ما قد ينتشر مثل ما ذكرت مما لا منفعة فيه ، فالذي الخلق جميعا معناه أحق فى ذلك ، وفى كل أمر منتشر عن يعود الخير إن كان على حق أو جور ، فيعلم ما افتعل منه فيغير ، وما صدق فيه فيقر وفى ذلك لزوم انتشار أخبار الرسل فى حياتهم وظهور المفتعل من ذلك فيمحى أثره بالنهى والتغيير ، فيبقى الحق الصدق منه ، دليل ذلك أمر رسول الله ، حتى لا تأتى ناحية نائية ولا مكانا بعيدا إلا وجدت أثره فيه ظاهرا ، وبخاصة فى عصره ، إذ كان ينساب إليه من الآفاق ويظهر شأنه فى البلاد ، فإذا كان كذلك لأوجه لقوله أخباره أخبار الآحاد ، ولا لما ذكر من الوجوه ، بل الخبر الواحد في الأمر أو الخارج عن الأمر المعتاد ينتشر انتشاراً أظهرا ، فكيف فيما فيه دعاء أهل الأديان ، وإرسال الكتب إلى الأفق ، ومجيء الوفود من كل النواحى ، وامتحان الرسل بأنواع الحجاج ، وقصد الملوك نحوهم في إطفاء نورهم ، وإشفاقا منهم ملكهم أن يذهب ويضمحل ، على ما عرفوا من ضعفهم فى أبدانهم وقلة أعوانهم ، فما ذلك الخوف إلا لعلمهم أنهم أتوا من عند القادر العليم. وعلى ذلك مما يخرج مخرج الآيات من الأمور الخطرة لن يذهب أثر ذلك ما بقى لهم تبع وبمثله احتجاج ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . وما ذكر من إجماعات اليهود والنصارى إنما ذلك أمور اختلفوا فيها على قدر ما احتمل آرائهم فانتشرت فى اتباع كل منهم ، ليس ذلك فى الآيات ولا فى الأمور الخطرة . وبعد ، فإنه متى بلغ ذلك تبديل الشرع حتى كاد أن يمحو أثره ويندرس خبره بفضل الله ومنه فى إرسال من يحيى ذلك ويظهر ما عليه الرسل بالآيات القاهرة للعقول، ليعلموا بهم التغيير والتبديل ، وعلى ذلك الانتشار . ثم من حكم الله أن يختم بمحمد عليه السلام النبوة ، وأن لا يرسل إلى أمته بعده رسولا ، جعل أمته بحيث لا يحتمل تغير الأمور الجسيمة ، ومن الله عليهم بكتاب حفظه يعلم به التغيير والتبديل فتبقى شريعته إلى فناء العالم ، وبالله التوفيق .
And he also objected by the consensus of the Jews and Christians. Ibn al-Rawandi said: Either the report is absolutely rejected, thus his doctrine in following al-Mani and this statement of his becomes invalid, or he permits a report, then necessarily one must resort to the consensus of the people of truth in rational principles, so their reports and consensuses are accepted; for they are the ones adhering to it, and we are those, praise be to God. The Shaykh (may God have mercy on him) said: The principle in this is that reports which it is necessary for the intellects to accept, because in that is the nullification of the wisdom of hearing and speech, and in it is the removal of the sciences of livelihood and the afterlife, and the severance of the foundations to food and medicine by which the life of bodies exists. Then reports increase in spread according to the magnitude of the matters about which they are reports, such as a king: if he is killed, his affair spreads necessarily such that even if people loved to conceal something like it, they would not be able to. Likewise, what is extraordinary from customary knowledge. And in what is of little consequence or occurs customarily, it does not appear clearly; rather, perhaps it is not mentioned. That is well-known in human nature. And on that basis, the reports of conquests and the subjugation of kings spread. So upon such is the affair of the messengers; because they came with great matters outside the customary order, so their reports appear and spread until they reach the farthest and nearest parts of the world; for they are in a manner that the hearers cannot conceal, as I mentioned about the tendency of human nature in spreading the like, along with what spreads of the like of what I mentioned that has no benefit. So that which all of creation is concerned with is more deserving of that. And in every matter that spreads, whether it returns to good, whether it is truth or falsehood, what is fabricated from it is known and changed, and what is true in it remains. In that is the necessity of the spread of the reports of the messengers in their lifetimes, and the appearance of the fabricated from that is erased by prohibition and change, so the true truth from it remains. Evidence of that is the matter of the Messenger of God (peace be upon him), such that no remote area or distant place comes except that his trace is found evident in it, especially in his era, as he was flowing to him from the horizons and his affair was appearing in the lands. So if that is the case, then his reports cannot be called reports of individuals, nor for the reasons mentioned. Rather, the single report about an extraordinary matter spreads more clearly. So how (about) that which includes the call of the people of religions, the sending of letters to the horizon, the coming of delegations from every direction, the testing of the messengers with various proofs, and the kings' intention towards them to extinguish their light, out of fear for their kingdom that it might go and vanish, given what they knew of their physical weakness and few helpers? That fear is only because they knew that they (the messengers) came from the Able, the Knowing. And upon that, from what emerges as miracles of dangerous matters, the trace of that will not disappear as long as they have followers and such argument. And there is no strength except with God. And what was mentioned about the consensuses of the Jews and Christians, that is only matters in which they differed according to what their opinions allowed, so they spread among the followers of each of them; that is not regarding miracles nor dangerous matters. Moreover, when that reaches the point of altering the law until it almost erases its trace and its news becomes obliterated, then by the grace and favor of God in sending someone who revives that and makes manifest what the messengers were upon with miracles overwhelming the intellects, so that through them the alteration and change may be known. And upon that is the spread. Then it is from God's decree that He sealed prophethood with Muhammad (peace be upon him), and that He will not send a messenger to his community after him. He made his community such that it cannot bear the change of grave matters, and God favored them with a book preserved by which alteration and change are known, so His law remains until the annihilation of the world. And with God is success.
Source pages p. 796

Commentary
This passage is a combination of an objection and an argument. It begins with Ibn al-Rawandi's objection: if reports are rejected entirely, the Manichaean position (taglid al-Mani) fails; if reports are accepted, one must rely on the consensus of the people of truth (ahl al-haqq) in rational principles. Al-Maturidi then presents the principle: reports that are necessary for the intellect to accept are those without which the function of hearing and speech would be nullified, and human livelihood and afterlife sciences would cease. He explains that the spread of news corresponds to the magnitude of the event. Great events, like the assassination of a king, spread necessarily and cannot be concealed. Prophets brought extraordinary matters beyond custom, so their news spreads inevitably to all parts of the world. He uses the example of the Prophet Muhammad, whose trace was evident in every remote area, especially during his lifetime. He refutes the claim that prophetic reports are isolated (akhbar al-ahad) by showing that a single report about an extraordinary matter spreads more clearly. He then addresses the consensus of Jews and Christians, explaining that their consensuses are about opinions that differ, not about miracles. Finally, he discusses God's decree to seal prophethood with Muhammad, preserving the law through the Quran so that it remains until the end of the world.

Key Terms
أخبار
رسل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the primary factor that determines whether a report spreads widely?
A) Number of narrators
B) Magnitude of the event
C) Writing in books
D) Royal endorsement

Key Takeaway
The spread of news is governed by the magnitude of the event; prophetic reports, being the greatest, spread inevitably.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The assassination of a king cannot be hidden. What does that imply about the news of the Prophet's mission that reaches you? How do you respond to its inevitable spread in your own heart—with genuine submission or with resistance?
?
Maturidi argues that the wisdom of hearing and speech is nullified if necessary reports are rejected. In what area of your faith do you selectively hear or ignore reports that demand a response? What would it cost you to truly listen and act?
?
If the spread of truth is proportional to its magnitude, what does the silence or obscurity of certain Islamic teachings in your own life say about the weight you give them? Will you let the magnitude of the prophetic message break through your indifference today?

Prophethood
intermediate
6 min
The Inevitable Spread of Prophetic Reports and Refutation of Isolated Reports
Maturidi argues for the inevitable spread of prophetic reports using the Prophet Muhammad as evidence and refutes akhbar al-ahad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the example of Prophet Muhammad to prove that prophetic reports are not isolated (akhbar al-ahad) but spread inevitably, and how the reaction of kings confirms their divine origin.

Core Idea
Prophetic reports spread like wildfire; even kings fear them, proving their extraordinary nature.

Maturidi continues by applying the principle to the Prophet Muhammad, showing that his report spread to every remote area in his lifetime. He then refutes the claim that these reports are akhbar al-ahad (isolated reports), arguing that a single report about an extraordinary matter spreads more clearly than many reports about ordinary matters. He also discusses the opposition of kings as evidence of the truth of the messengers.

Guided Path
1
Read the evidence from the Prophet's life
Notice how Maturidi uses the example of Prophet Muhammad: his trace was found in every remote area, especially in his lifetime.
2
Understand the refutation of akhbar al-ahad
Maturidi argues that a single report about an extraordinary matter spreads more clearly than many reports about ordinary matters, so prophetic reports cannot be called isolated.
3
Consider the reaction of kings
The fear of kings, despite the prophets' physical weakness, shows that they knew the prophets came from God, which is further evidence of the truth.
This reaction is a sign of the divine origin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophetic reports are weak because they are transmitted by a few individuals (akhbar al-ahad).
Correction: Maturidi argues that the extraordinary nature of the event ensures widespread dissemination, regardless of the number of transmitters.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, why did kings fear the prophets?
A) They had large armies
B) They knew the prophets came from the Able, the Knowing
C) They performed many miracles
D) They had many followers

Key Takeaway
The inevitable spread of prophetic reports, evidenced by the Prophet Muhammad and the fear of kings, proves their divine origin and refutes the claim of isolated reports.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Kings feared the message of the prophets and tried to extinguish it, yet you have access to this truth daily. Do you treat it with awe and urgency, or have you become desensitized? What will you do today to rekindle that reverence?
?
The truth of prophethood spread inevitably despite opposition. Is your life a conduit for that truth to spread, or are you hiding it out of fear of people? Name one concrete action you will take this week to make the truth more visible.
?
The prophets were physically weak yet kings feared them because they came from Allah. What are you afraid of that should pale in comparison to your connection with the Almighty? Write down one fear you will entrust to Allah today and trust Him to handle it.

Prophethood

The Consensus of Jews and Christians and the Sealing of Prophethood
Maturidi responds to the objection of Jewish/Christian consensus and concludes with the sealing of prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's response to the objection about Jewish and Christian consensus, and his explanation of God's decree to seal prophethood with Muhammad, preserving the law through the Quran.

Core Idea
Consensus among Jews and Christians is on opinions, not miracles; God sealed prophethood and preserved the Quran.

Maturidi addresses the objection that Jews and Christians have their own consensuses, which might undermine the argument. He explains that their consensus is on matters of opinion, not on miracles or dangerous matters. He then discusses God's decree to seal prophethood with Muhammad, making the community unable to bear major changes, and preserving the Shariah through the Quran until the end of the world.

Guided Path
1
Understand the distinction in consensus
Maturidi explains that the consensuses of Jews and Christians are on matters of opinion where they differed, not on miracles or dangerous matters.
2
Consider the preservation of the law
When the law is nearly altered, God sends revivers with overwhelming miracles to restore it.
3
Focus on the sealing of prophethood
God sealed prophethood with Muhammad, and preserved the Quran so that the Shariah remains unchanged until the end of the world.
This is the conclusion of Maturidi's argument.

أخبارهم وإجماعاتهم ؛ إذ هم المتمسكون به ، ونحن أولئك بحمد الله . قال الشيخ رحمه الله : والأصل فى هذا أن الأخبار التي لزم في العقول قبولها لما في ذلك بطلان حكمة السمع واللسان وفيه زوال علوم المعاش والمعاد وانقطاع الأصول إلى الأغذية والأدوية التي بها حياة الأبدان . ثم كانت الأخبار تتفاقم في الانتشار على قدر الأمور التي عنها الأخبار في العظم نحو ملك لو قتل لا نتشر أمره بالضرورة حتى لو أحب الناس كتمان مثله لما قدروا عليه ، وكذلك الخارجة من المعارف المعتادة ، وفيما يقل خطره أو يجرى على المعتاد لا يظهر ظهوره ، بل لعله لا يذكر ، معروف ذلك فى الخلقة ، وعلى ذلك انتشرت أخبار الفتوح وقهر الملوك ، فعلى مثل هذا أمر الرسل ؛ لأنهم جاءوا بالأمور العظام الخارجة عن الأمر المعتاد عنا عندهم ، فيظهر أخبارهم فتنتشر حتى تبلغ أقاصى الدنيا وأدانيها ؛ إذ هى على وجه لا يملك السامعون كتمانها ، على ما ذكرت من تغاضى الخلقة في نشر مثله مع ما قد ينتشر مثل ما ذكرت مما لا منفعة فيه ، فالذي الخلق جميعا معناه أحق فى ذلك ، وفى كل أمر منتشر عن يعود الخير إن كان على حق أو جور ، فيعلم ما افتعل منه فيغير ، وما صدق فيه فيقر وفى ذلك لزوم انتشار أخبار الرسل فى حياتهم وظهور المفتعل من ذلك فيمحى أثره بالنهى والتغيير ، فيبقى الحق الصدق منه ، دليل ذلك أمر رسول الله ، حتى لا تأتى ناحية نائية ولا مكانا بعيدا إلا وجدت أثره فيه ظاهرا ، وبخاصة فى عصره ، إذ كان ينساب إليه من الآفاق ويظهر شأنه فى البلاد ، فإذا كان كذلك لأوجه لقوله أخباره أخبار الآحاد ، ولا لما ذكر من الوجوه ، بل الخبر الواحد في الأمر أو الخارج عن الأمر المعتاد ينتشر انتشاراً أظهرا ، فكيف فيما فيه دعاء أهل الأديان ، وإرسال الكتب إلى الأفق ، ومجيء الوفود من كل النواحى ، وامتحان الرسل بأنواع الحجاج ، وقصد الملوك نحوهم في إطفاء نورهم ، وإشفاقا منهم ملكهم أن يذهب ويضمحل ، على ما عرفوا من ضعفهم فى أبدانهم وقلة أعوانهم ، فما ذلك الخوف إلا لعلمهم أنهم أتوا من عند القادر العليم. وعلى ذلك مما يخرج مخرج الآيات من الأمور الخطرة لن يذهب أثر ذلك ما بقى لهم تبع وبمثله احتجاج ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . وما ذكر من إجماعات اليهود والنصارى إنما ذلك أمور اختلفوا فيها على قدر ما احتمل آرائهم فانتشرت فى اتباع كل منهم ، ليس ذلك فى الآيات ولا فى الأمور الخطرة . وبعد ، فإنه متى بلغ ذلك تبديل الشرع حتى كاد أن يمحو أثره ويندرس خبره بفضل الله ومنه فى إرسال من يحيى ذلك ويظهر ما عليه الرسل بالآيات القاهرة للعقول، ليعلموا بهم التغيير والتبديل ، وعلى ذلك الانتشار . ثم من حكم الله أن يختم بمحمد عليه السلام النبوة ، وأن لا يرسل إلى أمته بعده رسولا ، جعل أمته بحيث لا يحتمل تغير الأمور الجسيمة ، ومن الله عليهم بكتاب حفظه يعلم به التغيير والتبديل فتبقى شريعته إلى فناء العالم ، وبالله التوفيق .
And he also objected by the consensus of the Jews and Christians. Ibn al-Rawandi said: Either the report is absolutely rejected, thus his doctrine in following al-Mani and this statement of his becomes invalid, or he permits a report, then necessarily one must resort to the consensus of the people of truth in rational principles, so their reports and consensuses are accepted; for they are the ones adhering to it, and we are those, praise be to God. The Shaykh (may God have mercy on him) said: The principle in this is that reports which it is necessary for the intellects to accept, because in that is the nullification of the wisdom of hearing and speech, and in it is the removal of the sciences of livelihood and the afterlife, and the severance of the foundations to food and medicine by which the life of bodies exists. Then reports increase in spread according to the magnitude of the matters about which they are reports, such as a king: if he is killed, his affair spreads necessarily such that even if people loved to conceal something like it, they would not be able to. Likewise, what is extraordinary from customary knowledge. And in what is of little consequence or occurs customarily, it does not appear clearly; rather, perhaps it is not mentioned. That is well-known in human nature. And on that basis, the reports of conquests and the subjugation of kings spread. So upon such is the affair of the messengers; because they came with great matters outside the customary order, so their reports appear and spread until they reach the farthest and nearest parts of the world; for they are in a manner that the hearers cannot conceal, as I mentioned about the tendency of human nature in spreading the like, along with what spreads of the like of what I mentioned that has no benefit. So that which all of creation is concerned with is more deserving of that. And in every matter that spreads, whether it returns to good, whether it is truth or falsehood, what is fabricated from it is known and changed, and what is true in it remains. In that is the necessity of the spread of the reports of the messengers in their lifetimes, and the appearance of the fabricated from that is erased by prohibition and change, so the true truth from it remains. Evidence of that is the matter of the Messenger of God (peace be upon him), such that no remote area or distant place comes except that his trace is found evident in it, especially in his era, as he was flowing to him from the horizons and his affair was appearing in the lands. So if that is the case, then his reports cannot be called reports of individuals, nor for the reasons mentioned. Rather, the single report about an extraordinary matter spreads more clearly. So how (about) that which includes the call of the people of religions, the sending of letters to the horizon, the coming of delegations from every direction, the testing of the messengers with various proofs, and the kings' intention towards them to extinguish their light, out of fear for their kingdom that it might go and vanish, given what they knew of their physical weakness and few helpers? That fear is only because they knew that they (the messengers) came from the Able, the Knowing. And upon that, from what emerges as miracles of dangerous matters, the trace of that will not disappear as long as they have followers and such argument. And there is no strength except with God. And what was mentioned about the consensuses of the Jews and Christians, that is only matters in which they differed according to what their opinions allowed, so they spread among the followers of each of them; that is not regarding miracles nor dangerous matters. Moreover, when that reaches the point of altering the law until it almost erases its trace and its news becomes obliterated, then by the grace and favor of God in sending someone who revives that and makes manifest what the messengers were upon with miracles overwhelming the intellects, so that through them the alteration and change may be known. And upon that is the spread. Then it is from God's decree that He sealed prophethood with Muhammad (peace be upon him), and that He will not send a messenger to his community after him. He made his community such that it cannot bear the change of grave matters, and God favored them with a book preserved by which alteration and change are known, so His law remains until the annihilation of the world. And with God is success.
Source pages p. 796

Commentary
This passage is a combination of an objection and an argument. It begins with Ibn al-Rawandi's objection: if reports are rejected entirely, the Manichaean position (taglid al-Mani) fails; if reports are accepted, one must rely on the consensus of the people of truth (ahl al-haqq) in rational principles. Al-Maturidi then presents the principle: reports that are necessary for the intellect to accept are those without which the function of hearing and speech would be nullified, and human livelihood and afterlife sciences would cease. He explains that the spread of news corresponds to the magnitude of the event. Great events, like the assassination of a king, spread necessarily and cannot be concealed. Prophets brought extraordinary matters beyond custom, so their news spreads inevitably to all parts of the world. He uses the example of the Prophet Muhammad, whose trace was evident in every remote area, especially during his lifetime. He refutes the claim that prophetic reports are isolated (akhbar al-ahad) by showing that a single report about an extraordinary matter spreads more clearly. He then addresses the consensus of Jews and Christians, explaining that their consensuses are about opinions that differ, not about miracles. Finally, he discusses God's decree to seal prophethood with Muhammad, preserving the law through the Quran so that it remains until the end of the world.

Key Terms
إجماع
آيات
رسل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, why does the Shariah of Prophet Muhammad remain until the end of the world?
A) Because there are many Muslims
B) Because God preserved the Quran
C) Because no one can change it
D) Because it is the best religion

Key Takeaway
The sealing of prophethood and preservation of the Quran ensure that the true prophetic reports remain unchanged until the end of time.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Quran is preserved as the criterion to know alteration and change. Do you rely on the Quran as your ultimate authority, or do you let your desires and opinions override its clear rulings? What would change if you truly submitted to its preservation?
?
If God sealed prophethood with Muhammad and made his community unable to bear major changes, then the religion is complete. Are you living as if this completion demands your full commitment, or do you treat Islam as just a part of your life? What step can you take today to realign your priorities with this final message?
?
Maturidi says Jewish and Christian consensus is on opinions, not miracles. When you hear claims from other religions or ideologies, do you critically assess whether they are built on undeniable proofs or mere opinions? How can you strengthen your conviction in the unique truth of Islam?

The True Condition for Valid Reports: Heartfelt Acceptance Beyond Numbers
Al-Rawandi refutes al-Warraq's objection and proposes a new criterion for report validity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Rawandi's refutation of the objection that prophetic proofs rely on few chains, and his alternative criterion for validating reports based on their effect on hearts and removal of doubts.

Core Idea
Valid reports are not defined by quantity but by their effect on hearts.

Al-Rawandi responds to al-Warraq's claim that the proofs of messengers are unreliable because they are transmitted through only one or two chains. He calls this a slander and points to the consensus of the community and the unimpeachable character of the Prophet. More importantly, he shifts the criterion for report validity from mere numbers to the domination over hearts and reassurance of the soul. This passage challenges a narrow view of transmission reliability and offers a profound epistemological standard rooted in human psychology and spiritual certainty.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the literal translation. Let al-Rawandi's argument come through before interpreting.
Notice that al-Rawandi begins by stating the objection before refuting it.
2
Identify the objection and refutation
Find what al-Warraq claimed and how al-Rawandi labels it ('bahat'). Then note the two refutations: consensus of the community and the Prophet's flawless character as attested even by disbelievers.
3
Understand the alternative condition
Al-Rawandi asks: if the condition were large numbers, then how is it that the real condition is domination over hearts, tranquility, and removal of doubts? Reflect on what these terms mean.
The phrase 'istila' 'ala al-qulub' is central.
4
Apply the principle to all truthful reports
Notice that al-Rawandi generalizes: 'Such is the case with the reports of the truthful, even if their number is few.' How does this principle affect the evaluation of reports?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أبو الحسين الروندى : طعن الوراق أخبار براهين الرسل من حيث وردت من طريق أو طريقين. وهذا بهت شديد ، بل أجمعت عليها أمتنا ، ثم أمر نبى الله مما توارث به الملحدون لتكلف الطعن ، والموحدون لرعاية الحق ، مع تطابق الكفرة على أن يجدوا فى خلقه ضعفا أو فى شجاعته ، أو له في شيء من المطامع رغبة ، أو إلى شيء من فنون منافع الدنيا ميلا ، فما وجدوا ذلك . فهذا لو كان شرط صحة الأخبار كثرة العدد ، فكيف وشرطه الاستيلاء على القلوب وسكونها إليه وطمأنينة النفس بالمخرج والفحوى ورفع ما يعترض من الظنون . وهكذا الأمر عند أخبار المحقين وإن قل عددهم .
Abu al-Husayn al-Rawandi said: Al-Warraq objected to the reports of the proofs of the messengers from the angle that they were transmitted via one or two chains. This is a severe slander. Rather, our community has consensus upon them. Then the matter of the Prophet of God is such that the atheists have inherited it to undertake slander, and the monotheists to observe the truth, along with the agreement of the disbelievers that they found in his character no weakness, nor in his courage, nor in him any desire for any of the ambitions, nor any inclination towards any of the types of worldly benefits. They did not find that. So if the condition for the validity of reports were multitude of number, then how (is it) when its condition is the domination over hearts, their tranquility towards it, and the reassurance of the soul by the outcome and content, and the removal of what intervenes from doubts. And such is the case with the reports of the truthful, even if their number is few.
Source pages p. 797

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer pair. Abu al-Husayn al-Rawandi reports al-Warraq's objection that the proofs (miracles) of the messengers are transmitted only through one or two chains, implying they are unreliable. Al-Rawandi refutes this strongly, calling it a slander (bahat). He points out that the Muslim community has consensus on these reports. Moreover, the character of the Prophet is so well-attested that even the disbelievers, despite their enmity, could find no weakness in his character, courage, or worldly desires. He then argues that the condition for the validity of reports is not large numbers of transmitters but rather the domination over hearts, tranquility of the soul, and removal of doubts. This is the case for reports of the truthful, even if few in number.

Key Terms
طعن
براهين
بهت
استيلاء على القلوب
طمأنينة النفس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A report is only valid if transmitted by many chains.
Correction: Al-Rawandi shows that the key is not multitude of number but the effect on hearts and removal of doubts.

Checkpoint
What does al-Rawandi say is the true condition for the validity of reports?
A) Large number of transmitters
B) Domination over hearts, tranquility of the soul, and removal of doubts
C) Agreement of the entire community
D) Written documentation from the Prophet

Key Takeaway
The validity of reports depends on their effect on the heart and soul, not merely on the number of chains.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a report about the Prophet's life, does your heart find tranquility and certainty, or do you rely solely on the number of narrators? How can you train your heart to recognize truth by its effect?
?
Think of a time you dismissed a truth because few people believed it. Could it be that the condition for truth is not the crowd but the peace it brings your soul? Examine your attachments.
?
If the disbelievers themselves could not find any flaw in the Prophet's character, why do you sometimes doubt the reports about him? What doubts intervene in your heart, and how can you remove them using al-Rawandi's criterion?

The Finality of Prophethood and Preservation of the Quran
Maturidi argues that God preserved the religion through prophets and sealed it with Muhammad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument for why God sent prophets to revive the true religion and why He sealed prophethood with Muhammad and preserved the Quran.

Core Idea
God preserves His religion by sending prophets and seals it with a preserved scripture.

In this passage, Imam Maturidi addresses how God protects His religion from corruption. He explains that whenever the true law becomes altered, God sends a prophet with clear signs to revive it. He then concludes that prophethood ended with Muhammad and the Quran is divinely preserved, ensuring the Sharia remains until the end of time.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the author's reasoning flow before interpreting.
Notice the structure: critique of previous scriptures, principle of revival, finality argument.
2
Identify Maturidi's critique of previous scriptures
Maturidi dismisses the consensus of Jews and Christians as proof because they differed among themselves. Understand why this is important for his argument.
He is clearing the ground for the need for divine intervention.
3
Understand the principle of divine intervention
Maturidi states that when the law becomes corrupted to the point of extinction, God sends a prophet to revive it with overwhelming signs. This shows God's care for His religion.
The key phrase: 'بفضل الله ومنه في إرسال من يحيي ذلك'.
4
Recognize the finality argument
Maturidi argues that God sealed prophethood with Muhammad and will not send another messenger. He made the Muslim nation unable to bear change in grave matters and preserved the Quran.
This is the culmination: the Quran is the final preserved guide.
5
Connect to overall purpose
Reflect on the entire argument: God's wisdom ensures the survival of true religion through prophets and ultimately through the preserved Quran.
This passage shows Maturidi's defense of the finality of prophethood and the preservation of scripture.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما ذكر من إجماعات اليهود والنصارى إنما ذلك أمور اختلفوا فيها على قدر ما احتمل آرائهم فانتشرت في اتباع كل منهم، ليس ذلك في الآيات ولا في الأمور الخطرة. وبعد، فإنه متى بلغ ذلك تبديل الشرع حتى كاد أن يمحو أثره ويندرس خبره بفضل الله ومنه في إرسال من يحيي ذلك ويظهر ما عليه الرسل بالآيات القاهرة العقول، ليعلموا بهم التغيير والتبديل، وعلى ذلك الانتشار. ثم من حكم الله أن يختم بمحمد عليه السلام النبوة، وأن لا يرسل إلى أمته بعده رسولا، جعل أمته بحيث لا يحتمل تغير الأمور الجسيمة، ومن عليهم بكتاب حفظه يعلم به التغيير والتبديل فتبقى شريعته إلى فناء العالم، وبالله التوفيق.
And what is mentioned of the consensus of the Jews and Christians is only that they differed in matters according to the extent of their opinions, and it spread among the followers of each of them; that is not in the signs nor in the grave matters. And moreover, when that reaches the point of alteration of the law until it nearly obliterates its trace and its report becomes extinct, by the grace of God and His favor, He sends one who revives that and manifests what the messengers brought with overwhelming signs, so that through them they may know the change and alteration, and upon that is the dissemination. Then it is from God's wisdom that He sealed prophethood with Muhammad, peace be upon him, and that He would not send after him a messenger to his nation; He made his nation such that it cannot bear the change of grave matters, and He favored them with a book which He preserved, by which change and alteration are known, so his law remains until the annihilation of the world. And with God is success.
Source pages p. 797

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument for the preservation of the true religion. Maturidi begins by dismissing the consensus of Jews and Christians as irrelevant because they themselves differed. He then argues that whenever the true law becomes corrupted to the point of extinction, God sends a prophet to revive it with clear signs. Finally, he presents the ultimate proof: God sealed prophethood with Muhammad and preserved the Quran, ensuring that the Sharia remains intact until the end of the world. This demonstrates God's care for His religion.

Key Terms
ختم النبوة
تبديل الشرع
آيات قاهرة
حفظ الكتاب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The consensus of Jews and Christians is a proof for the truth of their religions.
Correction: Maturidi clarifies that they actually disagreed among themselves, so their consensus is not a reliable proof for the preservation of their scriptures.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the purpose of God sending prophets after the corruption of the law?
A) To establish new laws
B) To revive and manifest the true religion with overwhelming signs
C) To punish the people
D) To change the religion completely

Key Takeaway
God's wisdom ensures the survival of the true religion through prophets and ultimately through the preserved Quran, sealed with Muhammad's prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe the Quran you recite today is identical to what was revealed to Muhammad, with no addition or subtraction? If so, why do you still hesitate to obey its commands without excuse?
?
Maturidi says that God made this nation such that it cannot bear major changes to the religion. But are you, in your own life, allowing small compromises that subtly shift your practice away from the original guidance?
?
If prophethood is sealed and the Quran is preserved to expose any change, then what authority remains for innovations or customs that contradict its clear text? How will you align yourself with the preserved truth starting today?

Prophethood

Maturidi's Refutation of the Objection on Few Transmitters
Ibn ar-Rawandi reports an objection about few transmitters and Maturidi refutes it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's refutation of the objection that prophetic reports are unreliable due to few transmitters, and his emphasis on the inner compelling quality of truth over mere numbers.

Core Idea
Authenticity of prophetic reports is not about numbers but about the heart's tranquility.

This passage from Maturidi's Kitab al-Tawhid addresses a key objection raised by skeptics: that the proofs of prophethood rely on reports transmitted by only one or two narrators. Maturidi refutes this by pointing to the universal acceptance of these reports and the unimpeachable character of the Prophet, then argues that the true criterion for reliability is the internal conviction they produce. As you read, notice how Maturidi turns the question from external quantity to internal quality.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Start by reading the objection as reported by Ibn ar-Rawandi: that the reports of the messengers came through one or two chains, implying they are unreliable.
Note the word 'طعن الوراق' (the Wiraq's objection).
2
Observe Maturidi's initial response
Maturidi calls it a slanderous lie and immediately appeals to the consensus of the community (أجمعت عليها أمتنا). Then he highlights that even the disbelievers could find no fault in the Prophet's character or conduct.
This shows that external agreement and character testimony matter.
3
Identify the true condition
Maturidi explicitly rejects large numbers as the condition. Instead, he states the condition is 'الاستيلاء على القلوب وسكونها إليه وطمأنينة النفس' — overwhelming of hearts, tranquility, and soul's reassurance.
This is the core of his epistemology: truth compels inner acceptance.
4
Reflect on the broader implication
Consider how Maturidi shifts the basis of knowledge from external counting to internal certainty. This has implications for how we accept prophetic reports even when transmitted by few.
The same criterion applies to truthful reports in general (أخبار المحقين).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أبو الحسين الروندى : طعن الوراق أخبار براهين الرسل من حيث وردت من طريق أو طريقين. وهذا بهت شديد، بل أجمعت عليها أمتنا، ثم أمر نبى الله مما توارث به الملحدون لتكلف الطعن، والموحدون لرعاية الحق، مع تطابق الكفرة على أن يجدوا في خلقه ضعفا أو في شجاعته، أو له في شيء من المطامع رغبة، أو إلى شيء من فنون منافع الدنيا ميلا، فما وجدوا ذلك. فهذا لو كان شرط صحة الأخبار كثرة العدد، فكيف وشرطه الاستيلاء على القلوب وسكونها إليه وطمأنينة النفس بالمخرج والفحوى ورفع ما يعترض من الظنون. وهكذا الأمر عند أخبار المحقين وإن قل عددهم.
Abu al-Husayn al-Rawandi said: The Wiraq objected to the reports of the proofs of the messengers because they came through one or two chains. And this is a slanderous lie. Rather, our community has agreed upon them. Then the matter of the Prophet of God — may the atheists inherit it in their effort to disparage, and the monotheists [inherit it] for the observance of truth — with the agreement of the disbelievers that they could not find in his character any weakness, nor in his courage, nor any desire for anything of worldly gains, nor any inclination towards any kind of worldly benefits; they did not find that. So if the condition for the validity of reports were large numbers, what then? However, the condition is the overwhelming of hearts, their tranquility towards him, and the soul's reassurance with the outcome and the content, and the removal of suspicions that arise. And such is the case with the reports of the truthful, even if their number is few.
Source pages p. 797

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its refutation. Al-Rawandi reports that the Wiraq (a heretic) objected to the prophetic reports on the grounds that they were transmitted through only one or two chains. Maturidi refutes this as a slander. He points out that the entire Muslim community has agreed on these reports. Moreover, the disbelievers themselves, despite their enmity, could not find any fault in the Prophet's character or behavior. If the criterion for accepting reports were simply large numbers, then what? But the real condition is that the report captures the hearts, brings tranquility to the soul by its content and outcome, and removes doubts. This is how truthful reports are accepted, even if few transmit them.

Key Terms
طعن الوراق
شرط صحة الأخبار
الاستيلاء على القلوب
سكون النفس
الطمأنينة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The authenticity of prophetic reports depends solely on many chains of transmission.
Correction: Maturidi argues that the real condition is not quantity but the overwhelming of hearts and tranquility of the soul, as evidenced by the community's consensus and the Prophet's unimpeachable character.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi say is the true condition for the validity of reports from the prophets?
A) Large number of narrators
B) Agreement of the disbelievers
C) The overwhelming of hearts and reassurance of the soul
D) Being transmitted through multiple generations

Key Takeaway
Maturidi argues that the reliability of prophetic reports is not based on the number of transmitters but on the inner conviction they generate in the heart, as evidenced by the unanimity of the community and the untarnished character of the Prophet.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a prophetic report, do you weigh it by the number of scholars who narrated it or by the peace it brings to your heart? Are you willing to trust a truth that comes through a single channel if it settles your soul?
?
The disbelievers agreed on the Prophet's integrity. How does your own life testify to the truthfulness of the message? If others observed your character, would they be compelled to accept what you claim to believe?
?
Maturidi says the condition is the overwhelming of hearts. Has the prophetic message overwhelmed your heart, or do you still resist its authority in some area? What would it take for you to submit completely?

Maturidi's Three Answers to the Objection on 'Ask the People of Reminder'
Maturidi presents three responses to the Wiraq's objection against the verse 'Ask the people of the Reminder'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand three arguments that Imam Maturidi gives to explain why God commands asking the People of the Book despite their hiding of truth.

Core Idea
God's command to ask the 'People of Reminder' is a sign, not a contradiction.

The verse 'Ask the people of the Reminder' has been subject to objection: how can God command us to ask those who are accused of hiding truth? Imam Maturidi responds with three distinct answers that show the wisdom behind the command. Each answer addresses a different aspect of the situation—divine compulsion, human obstinacy, and the status of believers among them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Read the passage and note the Wiraq's objection: How can God command asking people who hide truth? Understand the problem.
The objection relies on the apparent contradiction between the command and the accusation.
2
First answer: divine subjugation
Examine Maturidi's first response: God compels them to agree after clear proofs, making it a great sign. Look for the verse quoted as support.
The verse 'Is it not a sign for them...' is used as evidence.
3
Second answer: addressing obstinacy
Understand the second answer: even after proof, a stubborn person may be convinced by asking a trusted individual. This shows practical wisdom.
The term 'lajaj' (obstinacy) is key.
4
Third answer and additional note
Read the third answer that the command refers to those who became Muslim. Also note the possible alternative interpretation of 'people of the Reminder' as arbiters.
This shows the versatility of the verse's meaning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وطعن الوراق في قوله: {فاسألوا أهل الذكر} أن كيف أمر بذلك مع الشهادة عليهم بكتمان الحق؟ فأجيب بما إذ أيد الله نبوة محمد بالحجج القاهرة مالوا إلى الكتاب، فقيل لهم ذلك على أن الله يسخرهم في ذلك ويضطرهم إلى الموافقة، فيكون ذلك من جليل آياته، إذ جمع عليه الأعداء والأولياء وهو قوله: {أو لم يكن لهم آية أن يعلمه علماء بني إسرائيل}. وأيضا إن ذا على ما يعرف من لجاج الرجل بعد إقامة البرهان عليه، أن يقال: فاسأل ذلك فلانا ممن يطمع سكون قلبه إليه فيترك اللجاج. والثالث أن يكون المراد يرجع إلى من أسلم منهم، وبالله التوفيق. وجائز أن يكون المراد بأهل الذكر هم التحكيم إليهم عن الكذب، والله أعلم.
And the Wiraq objected to His saying: 'Ask the people of the Reminder' — how can He command that while testifying that they conceal the truth? So it was answered: Since God supported the prophethood of Muhammad with overwhelming proofs, they inclined to the Scripture. So they were told that, as God subjugates them in that and compels them to agreement, and that becomes among His great signs, when both enemies and allies are gathered upon it, and He says: 'Is it not a sign for them that the scholars of the Children of Israel know it?' And also that this is based on what is known of a man's obstinacy after the establishment of proof upon him, so it is said: Ask that person — so-and-so — from whom one hopes that his heart will be calm and he will abandon obstinacy. And the third is that the meaning refers back to those who became Muslims among them. And with God is success. And it is possible that the intended meaning of 'people of the Reminder' is those who refer to them for judgment against falsehood. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 797

Commentary
This passage addresses an objection to the Quranic command 'Ask the people of the Reminder' (فاسألوا أهل الذكر). The Wiraq argues: How can God command us to ask people who are accused of hiding the truth? Maturidi provides three answers. First, after God supported Muhammad with clear proofs, the People of the Book were compelled to accept the truth from the Quran, and this is a great sign. Second, sometimes a stubborn person may be convinced by asking someone he trusts, even after clear proof. Third, the command may refer to those who had already accepted Islam. Additionally, he suggests that 'people of the Reminder' might mean those who are to be referred to for judgment to avoid falsehood.

Key Terms
فاسألوا أهل الذكر
كتمان الحق
تسخير
لجاج

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse commands asking people who hide truth, which is contradictory.
Correction: Maturidi explains that the command is either to compel them to truth, or to address obstinacy through trusted sources, or refers to Muslims among them.

Checkpoint
What is the first answer Maturidi gives for why God commanded to ask the People of the Book despite their hiding of truth?
A) They were all Muslims
B) God compels them to agree with the truth after clear proofs
C) They were forced to lie
D) The command was only for the Prophet

Key Takeaway
Maturidi shows that the command to ask the People of the Book is compatible with their hiding of truth through three wise explanations.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a command of Allah that seems difficult to reconcile with the behavior of some people, do you tend to question the command itself? How can Maturidi's method of responding to objections inspire you to trust deeper wisdom instead of doubting?
?
Is there an area in your life where you have been obstinate (lujaj) even after clear proof? Who could you ask, like Maturidi suggests, to calm your heart and abandon that stubbornness?
?
Think of someone you consider an adversary. How might God be subjugating that person (tasheer) to serve as a sign for you of His power, even if they don't realize it? What would it take for you to see that as a great sign rather than a contradiction?
