Why Angels Appeared at Badr but Not at Uhud: Maturidi's Two Answers
Maturidi answers why angels were present at Badr but not at Uhud with two distinct rationales.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's two rational explanations for why angels appeared at Badr but not at Uhud, and how these answers refute the objection of inconsistency.

Core Idea
Angels at Badr were a unique sign for the first battle, not a general rule.

The Wiraq objected that if angels helped Muslims at Badr, why were they absent at Uhud? Maturidi gives two distinct answers: one based on visible evidence (severed heads without visible killers) and one based on divine wisdom (Badr was the first decisive battle). This lesson unpacks both responses and shows how they defend the reliability of prophetic reports.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the Wiraq's challenge: why did angels not appear at Uhud if they were at Badr? Note that this is a test of consistency.
2
Examine the first answer
Maturidi points to the physical evidence at Badr—heads appearing without any visible killer, and soldiers seeing unfamiliar forms. This indicates angelic involvement.
The phrase 'بلا قاتل رأوه' means they saw heads without seeing who killed them.
3
Examine the second answer
Maturidi argues that Badr was the first major battle, so God granted a clear victory to establish the truth and defeat falsehood. Thus, angelic aid was a special event, not a recurring pattern.
أول حرب means 'first battle' in the context of Islamic military history.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وطعن الوراق إخبار رسول الله بحضور الملائكة يوم بدر، قال: أين كانوا يوم أحد؟ جواب الأول ظهور رؤوس ببدر بلا قاتل رأوه، وبيان المذكور من الأعداد أنهم رأوا صورا لم يعرفوهم. وجواب الثاني أن ذلك أول حرب، فأراد الله تعالى أن ينصرهم ليظهر الحق ويبطل الباطل.
And the Wiraq objected to the report of the Messenger of God about the presence of angels on the day of Badr. He said: Where were they on the day of Uhud? The first answer: The appearance of heads at Badr without [them] seeing a killer, and the explanation of the mentioned numbers is that they saw forms they did not recognize. And the second answer: That was the first battle, so God, exalted, wanted to support them so that the truth might appear and falsehood be defeated.
Source pages p. 798

Commentary
The Wiraq questions why the angels helped the Muslims at Badr but not at Uhud. Maturidi provides two answers. First, at Badr, the angels appeared as heads (of the enemy) without the Muslims seeing who killed them, and they saw forms they did not recognize. Second, Badr was the first battle, and God wanted to give a clear victory to establish the truth and defeat falsehood. So the angels' presence was a special sign for the first battle, not a general rule for every battle.

Key Terms
الملائكة
بدر
أحد
النصر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The absence of angelic help at Uhud contradicts their presence at Badr, implying inconsistency in divine support.
Correction: Maturidi explains that Badr was unique—it was the first battle and involved visible signs of angelic intervention, whereas Uhud did not require such a display for God's wisdom.

Checkpoint
What is the second reason Maturidi gives for the angels' presence at Badr but not at Uhud?
A) The Muslims were stronger at Badr
B) God wanted to test the Muslims at Uhud
C) Badr was the first battle, so God wanted to establish the truth
D) The angels were only sent for defensive battles

Key Takeaway
Maturidi shows that the angels' appearance at Badr was a unique divine sign for the first battle, not a general rule that applies to every battle.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a new trial, do you expect God to repeat the exact same signs of help He gave you before? What in this lesson challenges that assumption?
?
Have you ever doubted God's wisdom when you didn't see obvious supernatural aid in a struggle? How does Maturidi's second answer speak to that doubt?
?
Are you content to trust that God's help comes in ways and times He chooses, even when you cannot see it? What would need to change in your heart for you to truly accept that?

Proof of Prophethood Through Intrinsic Qualities
Maturidi proves Muhammad's prophethood through his perfect physical and moral attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the physical and moral perfection of Muhammad as a proof of his prophethood.

Core Idea
Muhammad's flawless character and beauty are direct signs of his prophethood.

Imam Maturidi presents a unique argument for prophethood: not through miracles alone, but through the intrinsic qualities of the prophet himself. He argues that Muhammad's physical beauty, moral perfection, and complete freedom from defects point to his divine mission. This lesson explores that argument and its significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Maturidi begins by stating a three-fold proof structure.
2
Identify the three-fold proof
The passage opens by stating that prophethood is established by three means: essence (al-jawhar), sensory and rational signs, and the states of need. Find these in the text and note how Maturidi focuses on the first.
3
Examine the physical perfections
Maturidi lists Muhammad's physical attributes: face more beautiful than the full moon, fragrance better than musk, body softer than silk, and sweat used as perfume. Reflect on why these are considered proofs.
These attributes are presented as signs of a special divine favor.
4
Reflect on moral perfection
The passage then lists moral perfections: never lied, never erred, never fled, no evil character, no flattery, no foul language, no revenge. Notice the consistency and the final reference to Quranic rebuke showing extreme compassion.
Moral perfection here is a cumulative argument for truthfulness.
5
Connect to the bigger picture
Ask yourself: Why does Maturidi begin with intrinsic qualities rather than miracles? How does this argument fit into a rational proof of prophethood?
This passage establishes that Muhammad's very being testifies to his mission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[ إثبات نبوة الأنبياء ] وبخاصة رسالة محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم ] ثم القول في نبوة الأنبياء وبخاصة في رسالة محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم ثبت بالجوهر ثم بأيات حسية وعقلية ثم بموافقة ظهور الأحوال التي هي أحوال الحاجة إليه . فأما أمر الجوهر فقد بينا ابتداءه ، مع ما ذكر فيه أنه نظر إلى وجهه وإلى البدر فكان هو أحسن منه ، وأنه كان أطيب ريحا من المسك ، وألين من الحرير ، وكان يُؤخذ بعرقه فيُنقع به فى الطيب ، وقد وصفت خلقته بما لا يعرف أحد يوصف بمثله حسنا وجمالا ، وجل العين تراها تهيج في الحيرة بذى آفات في الخلقة ، فدل براءته عن كل الآفات ، وزينه بكل زين ، على استجابة أعلى الدرجات فى الخلق وأفضل الأقدار، ويدل على ذلك أنه لم يؤخذ عليه كذب قط، ولا عرفت منه هفوة ، ولا منه عن أعدائه فرار ، ولا في أخلاقه سوء ، بل كان على ما وصف، لا يُدارى ولا يمارى ولا يعرف فحش ولا ينتصر لنفسه ، وكان فى الإشفاق بالمحل الذى عوتب عليه بقوله : " فَلَا تَذْهَبْ نَفْسُكَ "
[Establishment of the Prophethood of the Prophets] And specifically the message of Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. Then the statement on the prophethood of the prophets and specifically the message of Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, is established by the essence, then by sensory and rational signs, then by the agreement of the emergence of states that are states of need for him. As for the matter of the essence, we have already explained its beginning, along with what was mentioned about it: he looked at his face and at the full moon, and he was more beautiful than it; and he was more fragrant than musk, and softer than silk; and his sweat was taken and soaked in perfume; and his creation was described in a way that no one is known to be described with such beauty and handsomeness. And every eye sees it [and] becomes agitated in confusion with one having defects in creation. So his being free from all defects and his being adorned with every adornment indicates the attainment of the highest degrees in creation and the best of destinies. And it also indicates that he was never caught in a lie, nor was any mistake known from him, nor flight from his enemies, nor any evil in his character. Rather, he was as described: he did not dissemble, nor dispute, nor know obscenity, nor seek vengeance for himself. And he was in compassion to the degree that he was rebuked for it in His saying: 'So do not let yourself be consumed' [Quran].
Source pages p. 801

Commentary
This passage is a proof of prophethood, specifically of Muhammad, based on his intrinsic qualities (الجوهر). Maturidi begins by stating that prophethood in general and Muhammad's message in particular are established by three means: the essence (الجوهر), sensory and rational signs, and the correspondence of his character to the need for a prophet. Here he focuses on the first means, the essence, which refers to his physical and moral perfection. He lists several attributes: his face was more beautiful than the full moon, his smell better than musk, his body softer than silk, his sweat was used as perfume. His creation was described with unparalleled beauty. These physical perfections, being free from any defect, indicate that he was given the highest rank in creation and the best of destinies. Then Maturidi moves to moral perfection: he was never known to lie, never made a mistake, never fled from enemies, and had no evil in his character. He did not flatter, did not engage in futile argument, did not use foul language, and did not seek revenge for himself. He was so compassionate that Allah rebuked him for it in the Quranic verse 'So do not let yourself be consumed' (referring to his grief over the disbelief of his people). These combined perfections serve as a direct proof of his prophethood, because such a person cannot be a false prophet; rather, his excellent qualities confirm his truthfulness and mission.

Key Terms
نبوة (prophethood)
الرسالة (message/mission)
الجوهر (essence)
أيات حسية وعقلية (sensory and rational signs)
الحسن والجمال (beauty and handsomeness)
الصدق والبراءة (truthfulness and innocence)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that Maturidi is relying solely on physical beauty as proof, but he combines it with moral perfection and the consistency of his life, making a cumulative argument.
Correction: The passage explicitly links physical perfection with moral impeccability, presenting a holistic argument from intrinsic qualities.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what foundational means validates Muhammad's prophethood in this passage?
A) Only sensory miracles like the splitting of the moon.
B) His intrinsic qualities (الجوهر), supported by his physical and moral perfection.
C) The consensus of all scholars.
D) The agreement of previous scriptures.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi demonstrates that Muhammad's impeccable physical and moral character constitutes a rational proof of his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet was never caught in a lie. When was the last time you lied, even a small one? What does your willingness to lie say about your relationship with the One who sent the truthful Prophet?
?
Muhammad's compassion was so intense that Allah had to tell him not to be consumed with grief for others. Do you grieve for those who are lost in disbelief? Or do you feel indifferent?
?
If his perfect character is a proof of his prophethood, what does your imperfect character say about your claim to follow him? What specific trait do you need to change today to better reflect his example?

The Threefold Proof of Prophethood
Maturidi introduces the triple proof of prophethood and elaborates on the proof from essence (جوهر).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam Maturidi's threefold proof of prophethood and how the Prophet's essential nature (جوهر) serves as the primary evidence.

Core Idea
Prophethood is proven by essence, signs, and circumstances—beginning with the Prophet's perfect nature.

Imam Maturidi begins by establishing a clear framework for proving prophethood. He identifies three distinct sources of evidence: the Prophet's innate essence (جوهر), sensory and rational signs, and the agreement of contingent circumstances. This lesson focuses on the first and most foundational proof—the extraordinary nature of the Prophet himself.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening statement
Read the first sentence which outlines the triple proof. Notice the order: essence first, then signs, then circumstances.
2
Understand the proof from essence
Maturidi then elaborates on the Prophet's physical beauty and perfection. Compare his description to the full moon and musk.
This is not mere praise but a rational argument for prophethood.
3
Reflect on the implication
The passage concludes that his innocence from defects and adornment with perfections indicate the highest ranks. Ask: Why does physical perfection point to prophethood?
In Islamic theology, prophets are protected from major sins and defects.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم القول في نبوة الأنبياء وبخاصة في رسالة محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم ثبت بالجوهر ثم بأيات حسية وعقلية ثم بموافقة ظهور الأحوال التي هي أحوال الحاجة إليه . فأما أمر الجوهر فقد بينا ابتداءه ، مع ما ذكر فيه أنه نظر إلى وجهه وإلى البدر فكان هو أحسن منه ، وأنه كان أطيب ريحا من المسك ، وألين من الحرير ، وكان يُؤخذ بعرقه فيُنقع به فى الطيب ، وقد وصفت خلقته بما لا يعرف أحد يوصف بمثله حسنا وجمالا ، وجل العين تراها تهيج في الحيرة بذى آفات في الخلقة ، فدل براءته عن كل الآفات ، وزينه بكل زين ، على استجابة أعلى الدرجات فى الخلق وأفضل الأقدار، ويدل على ذلك أنه لم يؤخذ عليه كذب قط، ولا عرفت منه هفوة ، ولا منه عن أعدائه فرار ، ولا في أخلاقه سوء ، بل كان على ما وصف، لا يُدارى ولا يمارى ولا يعرف فحش ولا ينتصر لنفسه ، وكان فى الإشفاق بالمحل الذى عوتب عليه بقوله : " فَلَا تَذْهَبْ نَفْسُكَ عَلَيْهِمْ حَسَرَاتٍ " ، وقوله : " لَعَلَّكَ بَاخِعٌ نَفْسَكَ " ، وفى التحزن بما فيه ملاك الخلق ، كما وصفه الله وعصمه بقوله : " وَلَا تَحْزَنْ عَلَيْهِمْ " ، وقال : " عَزِيزٌ عَلَيْهِ مَا عَنِتُم " ، وكان بالكرم بحيث عوتب به ، فقال : " وَلَا تبْسُطْهَا كُلَّ البَسْطِ " ، وقيل : لم يكن يدخر شيئا لغد . وقد عرض عليه أعلا ما يرغب فيه من متاع الدنيا والرياسة بأن يداهن قليلا فما أجاب فيه ، بل عادى الله الأقوياء والملوك والسادات حتى أكرمه الله بالرعب في قلوب الخلق ، فلم يكن يقصد إليهم في الحرب إلا خافوه ، وقيل : والله يعصمك من الناس فلم يخفهم بعد ذلك ، ولا أذكر أنه ولاهم ذلك ، على ما أصاب أتباعه النكبات والشدائد ، و وعد أن يبلغ ملك أمته ما دوى له من الأرض من المشارق والمغارب ، وما روى ما ذكر من أنواع الفزع فى قلوب أعدائه ، والحفظ عنه عما راموا به ، على موالاة أقربائه الأبعدين فى ذلك ، وما اجتمعت آرائهم على إطفاء نوره وطمس أثره ، فما ازداد إلا ظهورا ، ولا قوة إلا بالله .
Then the statement concerning the prophethood of the prophets, and especially concerning the message of Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, is established by essence, then by sensory and rational signs, and then by the agreement of the emergence of states which are states of need for him. As for the matter of essence, we have already explained its beginning, along with what was mentioned about it: that he looked at his face and at the full moon, and he was more beautiful than it; and that he was more fragrant than musk, and softer than silk; and his sweat was taken and soaked in perfume; and his creation was described in a way that no one is known to be described with similar beauty and handsomeness; and the eye of the great sees that it becomes agitated in bewilderment at one with defects in creation. So his innocence from every defect, and his adornment with every adornment, indicated his attaining the highest ranks in creation and the best of destinies. And that is indicated by the fact that he was never caught in a lie, nor was any lapse known from him, nor flight from his enemies, nor any evil in his morals; rather, he was as described: he did not flatter nor dispute, nor did he know obscenity, nor did he avenge himself. And he was in compassion to the extent that he was reproached for it in His saying: 'So do not let your soul be wasted in regrets over them,' and His saying: 'Perhaps you will kill yourself.' And in grief for what sustains creation, as God described him and protected him by His saying: 'And do not grieve over them,' and He said: 'Grievous to him is your suffering.' And he was so generous that he was reproached for it, and He said: 'And do not stretch your hand completely [in generosity].' And it is said: he did not store anything for tomorrow. And the highest of worldly goods and leadership were offered to him to compromise a little, but he did not respond; rather, he opposed the powerful, the kings, and the leaders for God, until God honored him with terror in the hearts of people, so they did not confront him in war without fearing him. And it is said: 'God will protect you from the people,' so he did not fear them after that. And I do not recall that he entrusted that to them, despite the afflictions and hardships that befell his followers. And he promised that the dominion of his nation would reach what his call had spread over the earth from east to west. And what was narrated about the types of fear in the hearts of his enemies, and the protection of him from what they plotted, despite the allegiance of his distant relatives in that. And their opinions did not unite to extinguish his light and obliterate his trace; rather, he only increased in prominence. And there is no power except through God.
Source pages p. 801

Commentary
This passage presents a multi-layered proof of prophethood. Maturidi states that prophethood is established by three means: essence (innate disposition), sensory and rational signs, and the agreement of contingent circumstances. He then focuses on the first: the Prophet's essence. He describes his physical perfection (superior to the moon, fragrant, soft) and his moral perfection (truthful, without fault, courageous, forgiving, generous, ascetic, fearless). These qualities indicate a divinely favored rank. The Prophet's character is further evidenced by Quranic verses reproaching his compassion and generosity, showing his extreme selflessness. His rejection of worldly offers in favor of divine mission, the terror instilled in enemies, and divine protection despite persecution all corroborate his prophethood. The conclusion: his light only increased, and all power is from God.

أيات حسية وعقلية

زين

Maturidi's first proof of prophethood is the Prophet's flawless essence, demonstrated through his physical and moral perfection.

?

?
If the Prophet's essence was free from every defect, what defects in your character must you remove to draw closer to him? Name one concrete step you will take this week to purify your heart.

The Prophet's Moral Perfection and Quranic Witness
Maturidi presents the Prophet's moral virtues and Quranic testimonies as further proof of prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's moral virtues, as attested by Quranic verses, serve as proof of his prophethood.

Core Idea
The Prophet's truthfulness, compassion, and generosity are themselves divine signs.

Having established the Prophet's physical perfection, Maturidi now turns to his moral character. He lists specific virtues—truthfulness, courage, forgiveness, compassion, generosity—and supports them with Quranic verses that both praise and gently reproach the Prophet for his extreme selflessness. This moral perfection is not coincidental but points to divine selection.

Guided Path
1
Read the list of moral virtues
Maturidi states that the Prophet was never caught lying, never fled from enemies, and had no evil in his character. Identify each virtue mentioned.
2
Understand the use of Quranic reproaches
The Quran reproaches the Prophet for excessive compassion and generosity. These reproaches actually highlight his perfect moral state. Match each Quranic verse to the virtue it illustrates.
For example, 'So do not let your soul go in regrets' shows his compassion.
3
Reflect on why moral perfection is a proof
Consider why a person with such perfect morals would not lie about prophethood. Maturidi implies that perfect character is incompatible with false claims.
This is a form of argument from integrity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم القول في نبوة الأنبياء وبخاصة في رسالة محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم ثبت بالجوهر ثم بأيات حسية وعقلية ثم بموافقة ظهور الأحوال التي هي أحوال الحاجة إليه . فأما أمر الجوهر فقد بينا ابتداءه ، مع ما ذكر فيه أنه نظر إلى وجهه وإلى البدر فكان هو أحسن منه ، وأنه كان أطيب ريحا من المسك ، وألين من الحرير ، وكان يُؤخذ بعرقه فيُنقع به فى الطيب ، وقد وصفت خلقته بما لا يعرف أحد يوصف بمثله حسنا وجمالا ، وجل العين تراها تهيج في الحيرة بذى آفات في الخلقة ، فدل براءته عن كل الآفات ، وزينه بكل زين ، على استجابة أعلى الدرجات فى الخلق وأفضل الأقدار، ويدل على ذلك أنه لم يؤخذ عليه كذب قط، ولا عرفت منه هفوة ، ولا منه عن أعدائه فرار ، ولا في أخلاقه سوء ، بل كان على ما وصف، لا يُدارى ولا يمارى ولا يعرف فحش ولا ينتصر لنفسه ، وكان فى الإشفاق بالمحل الذى عوتب عليه بقوله : " فَلَا تَذْهَبْ نَفْسُكَ عَلَيْهِمْ حَسَرَاتٍ " ، وقوله : " لَعَلَّكَ بَاخِعٌ نَفْسَكَ " ، وفى التحزن بما فيه ملاك الخلق ، كما وصفه الله وعصمه بقوله : " وَلَا تَحْزَنْ عَلَيْهِمْ " ، وقال : " عَزِيزٌ عَلَيْهِ مَا عَنِتُم " ، وكان بالكرم بحيث عوتب به ، فقال : " وَلَا تبْسُطْهَا كُلَّ البَسْطِ " ، وقيل : لم يكن يدخر شيئا لغد . وقد عرض عليه أعلا ما يرغب فيه من متاع الدنيا والرياسة بأن يداهن قليلا فما أجاب فيه ، بل عادى الله الأقوياء والملوك والسادات حتى أكرمه الله بالرعب في قلوب الخلق ، فلم يكن يقصد إليهم في الحرب إلا خافوه ، وقيل : والله يعصمك من الناس فلم يخفهم بعد ذلك ، ولا أذكر أنه ولاهم ذلك ، على ما أصاب أتباعه النكبات والشدائد ، و وعد أن يبلغ ملك أمته ما دوى له من الأرض من المشارق والمغارب ، وما روى ما ذكر من أنواع الفزع فى قلوب أعدائه ، والحفظ عنه عما راموا به ، على موالاة أقربائه الأبعدين فى ذلك ، وما اجتمعت آرائهم على إطفاء نوره وطمس أثره ، فما ازداد إلا ظهورا ، ولا قوة إلا بالله .
Then the statement concerning the prophethood of the prophets, and especially concerning the message of Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, is established by essence, then by sensory and rational signs, and then by the agreement of the emergence of states which are states of need for him. As for the matter of essence, we have already explained its beginning, along with what was mentioned about it: that he looked at his face and at the full moon, and he was more beautiful than it; and that he was more fragrant than musk, and softer than silk; and his sweat was taken and soaked in perfume; and his creation was described in a way that no one is known to be described with similar beauty and handsomeness; and the eye of the great sees that it becomes agitated in bewilderment at one with defects in creation. So his innocence from every defect, and his adornment with every adornment, indicated his attaining the highest ranks in creation and the best of destinies. And that is indicated by the fact that he was never caught in a lie, nor was any lapse known from him, nor flight from his enemies, nor any evil in his morals; rather, he was as described: he did not flatter nor dispute, nor did he know obscenity, nor did he avenge himself. And he was in compassion to the extent that he was reproached for it in His saying: 'So do not let your soul be wasted in regrets over them,' and His saying: 'Perhaps you will kill yourself.' And in grief for what sustains creation, as God described him and protected him by His saying: 'And do not grieve over them,' and He said: 'Grievous to him is your suffering.' And he was so generous that he was reproached for it, and He said: 'And do not stretch your hand completely [in generosity].' And it is said: he did not store anything for tomorrow. And the highest of worldly goods and leadership were offered to him to compromise a little, but he did not respond; rather, he opposed the powerful, the kings, and the leaders for God, until God honored him with terror in the hearts of people, so they did not confront him in war without fearing him. And it is said: 'God will protect you from the people,' so he did not fear them after that. And I do not recall that he entrusted that to them, despite the afflictions and hardships that befell his followers. And he promised that the dominion of his nation would reach what his call had spread over the earth from east to west. And what was narrated about the types of fear in the hearts of his enemies, and the protection of him from what they plotted, despite the allegiance of his distant relatives in that. And their opinions did not unite to extinguish his light and obliterate his trace; rather, he only increased in prominence. And there is no power except through God.

This passage presents a multi-layered proof of prophethood. Maturidi states that prophethood is established by three means: essence (innate disposition), sensory and rational signs, and the agreement of contingent circumstances. He then focuses on the first: the Prophet's essence. He describes his physical perfection (superior to the moon, fragrant, soft) and his moral perfection (truthful, without fault, courageous, forgiving, generous, ascetic, fearless). The Prophet's Steadfastness and Divine Victory
Maturidi recounts the Prophet's rejection of worldly offers, divine protection, and the triumph of his mission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's rejection of worldly offers and his ultimate success against all odds confirm his prophethood.

Core Idea
The Prophet's steadfastness and divine protection prove his prophethood beyond doubt.

Maturidi now turns to the Prophet's interaction with the world. He describes how the Prophet was offered the best of this world—wealth and leadership—in exchange for compromising his message, but he refused. Instead, he opposed the powerful and kings for the sake of Allah. Allah then granted him victory through the terror placed in enemies' hearts and divine protection. Despite persecution, his mission only grew stronger, fulfilling the promise that his message would spread east and west.

Guided Path
1
Read about the offer of worldly goods
The Prophet was offered the highest worldly pleasures and leadership if he would compromise just a little. Note his refusal.
This shows his sincerity.
2
Understand divine protection and victory
Allah made the Prophet's enemies fear him even before battle and protected him from their plots. This is a clear sign of divine support.
3
Reflect on the ultimate success
Despite the efforts of his enemies, his message spread and his followers endured hardships. The promise of global reach indicates divine plan.
This is a cumulative argument from historical outcome.

Miraculous Proofs of Prophethood
Maturidi enumerates miraculous proofs of the Prophet's truthfulness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Maturidi uses specific historical events and prophecies as sensory proofs to confirm the truthfulness of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him).

Core Idea
Sensory miracles and fulfilled prophecies are tangible proofs of prophethood.

Imam Maturidi presents a series of concrete events from the life of the Prophet that serve as sensory proofs of his prophethood. These are not abstract rational arguments but observable facts that were witnessed by both believers and enemies. This passage demonstrates that miracles are not limited to physical wonders but include fulfilled predictions and divine protection.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation slowly. Notice the list of events Maturidi mentions. Try to identify each example as a sensory miracle or fulfilled prophecy.
The passage begins with a possibly unclear phrase; focus on the clear examples.
2
Identify the types of proofs
Maturidi lists several categories: spread of followers, revealing hidden schemes, predictions about individuals (Ali, Ammar), promises of conquests. Group them mentally.
These are all sensory proofs because they were observed or historically verified.
3
Reflect on the purpose
Ask yourself why Maturidi enumerates these specific examples. He is showing that prophethood is supported by multiple layers of evidence, not just one type.
4
Connect to previous scriptures
Notice that Maturidi mentions these events were also foretold in previous scriptures. This adds a layer of corroboration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإمام أبو منصور الماتريدي بفرس من اتبعه الأرض، ثم ما أخبر من قوله ولا يتمنونه وكان كذلك، ثم بما قال: ادعوا شركاءكم ثم كيدونى ولا تنظرون ما قدروا عليه، ثم بكثرة ما يمكرونه حتى خلصه الله من ذلك، ولعظيم ما يضمر أهل النفاق في أنفسهم فأطلعه الله حتى كانوا شدة يحذرون نزول سورة تنبئهم بما كان تعنتهم منهم، وأظهرهم على ما قالوا فيه وفى متبعيه، وما قال في أبي بكر وأصحابه من قوله: أَفَإِنْ مَاتَ أَوْ قُتِلَ انْقَلَبْتُمْ عَلَى أَعْقَابِكُم، وكذلك في قوله: وَمَنْ يَرْتَدِدْ مِنْكُمْ عَنْ دِينِهِ وما أعلم عليا أنه يقتل الناكبين المشارفين، وكان كذلك، وما قال لعمار تقتلك الفئة الباغية، وما وعد من الفتوح وسعة الدنيا على المؤمنين، وغير ذلك مما يكثر ذكره، لو استقصى فيه دواة نجباء أمته، ثم عامة ذلك مما كان ظاهرا عند أعدائه ما كان فى الكتب المنزلة بعثه، وعلى ألسن الرسل، مع جرت البشارة وأخذ العهد عليهم، ولا قوة إلا بالله.
Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi: By the spread of his followers on the earth, then what he informed of His saying 'and they do not wish for it' and it was so, then by His saying 'Call your partners then plot against me and give me no respite' and they could not do it, then by the abundance of their plotting until God delivered him from that, and by the greatness of what the hypocrites concealed in themselves and God revealed it to him until they were intensely fearing the revelation of a sura informing them of their obstinacy, and He exposed them regarding what they said about him and his followers, and what He said about Abu Bakr and his companions in His saying 'If he dies or is killed, will you turn back on your heels', and likewise in His saying 'And whoever among you apostatizes from his religion', and what he informed that Ali would kill the deviant aggressors, and it was so, and what he said to Ammar 'The rebellious group will kill you', and what he promised of conquests and abundance of the world for the believers, and other things too numerous to mention; if one were to exhaust them, he would need the inkwells of the elite of his nation. Then all of that was apparent to his enemies, and it was in the revealed scriptures concerning his mission, and on the tongues of the messengers, along with the glad tidings and the covenant taken upon them. There is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 803

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of miraculous and prophetic proofs of the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him). Maturidi lists several examples: the spread of his followers, the fulfillment of his information (such as the hypocrites' secrets and the prediction that people would not wish for death), the challenge to call upon partners, the failure of plots, the revelation of secrets, the verses about apostasy, the prediction that Ali would kill the deviators, the saying to Ammar, and the promise of conquests. All these were witnessed and confirmed, and they were also foretold in previous scriptures. Maturidi emphasizes that these signs were evident even to enemies and serve as sensory (ḥissī) proofs of prophethood.

Key Terms
نبوة
معجزات
أدلة حسية
بشارات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only rational proofs are valid for establishing prophethood.
Correction: Maturidi demonstrates that sensory miracles and fulfilled prophecies are also strong, tangible proofs that were witnessed by contemporaries.

Checkpoint
What type of proof does Maturidi primarily present in this passage?
A) Rational proofs from the Quran
B) Sensory/miraculous proofs from events and prophecies
C) Philosophical arguments
D) Consensus of scholars

Key Takeaway
Sensory miracles and fulfilled prophecies provide concrete, observable evidence that supports the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet's prophecies came true precisely. Are you living as if you truly believe that what he foretold about the afterlife will also come true with the same certainty? What is one specific change you need to make today to align your life with that certainty?
?
The enemies of the Prophet witnessed these miracles yet denied. What evidence from Allah do you tend to overlook or explain away because it is inconvenient for your desires? How will you stop doing that from today?
?
The Prophet promised the believers abundance and conquests. Do you trust Allah's promises even when they are delayed in your life? What promise are you waiting for, and how can you strengthen your trust now?

Five Rational Proofs for Prophethood
Al-Maturidi enumerates five rational proofs for the truth of prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the five rational proofs that al-Maturidi presents to establish the truth of prophethood.

Core Idea
Prophethood is rationally established through five observable patterns.

Al-Maturidi distinguishes between sensible signs and rational proofs. While sensible signs are instruments, rational proofs provide the logical foundation. In this passage, he enumerates five arguments, each grounded in divine custom and human need, supported by Quranic verses. These proofs collectively demonstrate that prophethood is neither unprecedented nor arbitrary.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish sensible from rational proofs
Notice that al-Maturidi begins by setting apart the sensible (al-hissiyya) from the rational (al-'aqliyya). Understand why rational proofs are the focus here.
This frames the discussion.
2
Identify the first two proofs
Read the first proof about the continuous custom of sending messengers, and the second about the timing during a period of intermission. See how each is supported by a Quranic verse.
These address the pattern and need.
3
Identify the next two proofs
The third proof focuses on the unlettered recipients, and the fourth on the prominent location of the mission. Note how these show the suitability of the Prophet.
These highlight the audience and place.
4
Understand the fifth proof and conclusion
The fifth proof involves the people's prior oaths and desire for a warner, removing any excuse. Then read the concluding remark about their need.
This completes the five.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذكر أبو زيد أن الحسية من الآلات فما جاءت الآثار كافية. وأما العقلية فهي على وجوه: أحدها أن أمره لم يكن مستغربا، بل كان مستمرا على العادة بوجود مثله في الأمم، فلذلك يبطل وجه الرد عليه في أول وهله. قال الله تعالى: وَإِنْ مِنْ أُمَّةٍ إِلَّا خَلَا فِيهَا نَذِيرٌ، وقال: ثُمَّ أَرْسَلْنَا رُسُلَنَا تَتْرَى. والثاني موافقة مجيئه وقت الحاجة إليه؛ إذ كان زمان فترة ودروس العلم، مع جري عادة الله بمعاقبة أسباب الهداية عند زوال أهله عن الهدى. قال الله تعالى: قَدْ جَاءَكُمْ رَسُولُنَا يُبَيِّنُ لَكُمْ. والثالث كون المبعوث فيهم بموضع الحاجة إليه والخلاء جنسه عن أسباب العلم بقوله: هُوَ الَّذِي بَعَثَ فِي الأُمِّيِّينَ رَسُولًا مِنْهُم وغيره. والرابع كونه في أظهر الأماكن للخلق؛ إذ هو معالم أهل الآفاق في الدنيا، وقال الله تعالى: وَكَذَلِكَ أَوْحَيْنَا إِلَيْكَ. والخامس منى القوم ذلك وإظهار الرغبة في ذلك، وإذا اقترح مقترح على ربه إزالة حماته لم يكن تعجب قطع معذرته، قال الله تعالى: وَلَوْ أَنَّا أَهْلَكْنَاكُم بِعَذَابٍ مِنْ قَبْلِهِ، قال: وَأَقْسَمُوا بِاللَّهِ جَهْدَ أَيْمَانِهِمْ لَئِنْ جَاءَهُمْ نَذِيرٌ. فهذه الخمسة ثم حاجتهم به في أحوالهم ثم ما حاجتهم بما في أحوال النبي
And Abu Zayd mentioned that the sensible (signs) are instruments, so the transmitted reports are sufficient. As for the rational (proofs), they are of several aspects: First, that his matter was not unprecedented, but was continuous according to custom in the existence of its like among the nations, therefore the basis for rejecting him is nullified from the outset. Allah Almighty said: 'And there was no nation but that a warner had passed within it' (35:24), and He said: 'Then We sent Our messengers in succession' (23:44). Second, the accordance of his coming at the time of need for him, since it was a time of intermission (fatrah) and the effacement of knowledge, along with Allah's established custom of requiting the means of guidance when its people depart from guidance. Allah said: 'Our messenger has come to you to make clear to you' (5:15). Third, that the one sent among them was in a position of need for him and the emptiness of his kind from the means of knowledge, by His saying: 'It is He who sent among the unlettered a messenger from among them' (62:2) and others. Fourth, his being in the most apparent places for creation, since he is a landmark for the people of the regions in the world, and Allah said: 'And thus We have revealed to you' (42:7). Fifth, the people's wish for that and their showing desire for it, and if a proposer (of an objection) were to propose to his Lord the removal of His proofs, it would not be surprising to cut off his excuse. Allah said: 'And if We had destroyed them with a punishment before it' (20:134), He said: 'And they swore by Allah their strongest oaths that if a warner came to them' (35:42). These five concern their need for him in their circumstances, then their need concerning the circumstances of the Prophet.
Source pages p. 804

Commentary
This passage presents five rational proofs for the truth of prophethood, each supported by Quranic verses. The author begins by distinguishing between sensible signs and rational proofs, then enumerates five aspects. The first proof argues that the coming of prophets is not unprecedented but follows a continuous pattern of sending warners to every nation, so rejecting the Prophet is baseless. The second proof emphasizes the timing of his mission during a period of religious decline and loss of knowledge, fulfilling the need for guidance. The third proof notes that the Prophet was sent to a people lacking scriptural knowledge (the unlettered), so his message was necessary. The fourth proof highlights that his mission occurred in the most prominent region (Mecca), making it universally accessible. The fifth proof refers to the people's prior oaths and desire for a warner, so when he came, they had no excuse. The author concludes that these five aspects address the people's need in their external circumstances, while further proofs relate to the Prophet's personal attributes.

Key Terms
العقلية
الوجوه
الأمم
النذير
الفترة
الأميون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that prophethood is a new or unprecedented event that can be rejected as strange.
Correction: Al-Maturidi's first proof shows that sending prophets is a continuous custom of Allah throughout nations, so it is not unprecedented.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the five rational proofs mentioned by al-Maturidi?
A) The continuous custom of sending messengers to nations.
B) The timing of the Prophet's mission during a period of ignorance.
C) The Prophet's ability to perform miracles like splitting the moon.
D) The people's prior oath that they would follow a warner if he came.

Key Takeaway
Al-Maturidi establishes prophethood through five observable rational proofs: continuous divine custom, timely need, unlettered recipients, prominent location, and prior human desire – leaving no excuse for disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider that Allah's custom is to send warners to every nation, do you truly feel the weight of the Prophet's mission in your life, or do you take it for granted as just a historical fact? How can you live today as if he were sent for you personally?
?
The proofs show that the people had no excuse—they had even sworn oaths to follow a warner. Have you ever made a promise to Allah to follow guidance if it became clear, only to ignore that same guidance when it came? What will you do today to honour that promise?
?
If you were among the unlettered recipients who needed a messenger to explain divine truth, would you have recognized him when he came? What prevents you now from fully submitting to the guidance he brought, as if you were hearing it for the first time?

The Prophet's Illiteracy and Divine Revelation
Al-Maturidi argues from the Prophet's illiteracy and Quranic preservation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's illiteracy and his preservation of the Quran serve as rational proofs for the divine origin of his message.

Core Idea
The Prophet's illiteracy proves his knowledge came from Allah, not human learning.

One of the strongest signs of prophethood is that Muhammad ﷺ grew up in an unlettered environment and never studied books, yet he delivered the Quran with perfect preservation. This lesson examines Al-Maturidi's argument that his illiteracy is not a weakness but a divine proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on illiteracy
Read the Arabic passage and translation, focusing on how Al-Maturidi describes the Prophet's upbringing and his unlettered nature.
Notice the verses cited: 'Do they not recognize their messenger?' and 'These are from the news of the unseen.'
2
Understand the preservation proof
Al-Maturidi argues that the Prophet's extraordinary retention of the Quran, despite being unlettered, is evidence of divine intervention.
He cites 'We will make you recite, and you will not forget' (87:6) and 'Move not your tongue with it' (75:16).
3
Connect to the overarching argument
Reflect on how this proof fits into the broader case for prophethood: only a prophet could have such knowledge without human instruction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
منها أنه نشأ في قوم لم يكن لهم كتب ولا دراسة، مع ما لم يفارق قومه، وما كان لهم كتب قد سبق له الارتياض في دراستها كان في ضمن تلك: لو طرأ عليهم طارئ لا يجها مكانه، وذلك قوله: أَمْ لَمْ يَعْرِفُوا رَسُولَهُمْ، وقوله: تِلْكَ مِنْ أَنْبَاءِ الْغَيْبِ نُوحِيهَا. وقد نشأ أميا، والأمي لا يأخذ عن الكتب ولا يستطيع التحفظ من الأفواه غاية الحفظ، إنما يكون ضبطه بصور معقولة روحانية يرتفع بها عن المهم، دليله ما لا يوجد عن مثله رواية الأشعار مخافة الغلط وغيرها، ولذلك اشتد تعجبهم من حفظ القرآن وقال الله تعالى: سَنُقْرِئُكَ فَلَا تَنْسَى، وقال: لَا تُحَرُّكَ بِهِ لِسَانَكَ، ولذلك قال الموصوف بالحفظ إنه لأشد تعصبا من قلوب الرجال من النعم من عقلها، قال الله تعالى: وَمَا كُنْتَ تَتْلُو مِنْ قَبْلِهِ مِنْ كِتَابٍ. وأيضا أنه لم يذكر عنه في سالف عمره التشاغل بنظم الكلام وتعاطي ضروبه، ثم يمتنع عن مثله أن يتهيأ له ما يعجز عنه المعروفين برياضته، دليله أنه لم يطعن بشيء من ذلك بل لما قيل بقوله: لهم: فَأْتُوا بِسُورَةٍ مِثْلِهِ سكتوا ولم يدعوا عليه إظهاره فيه، قال الله تعالى: قُلْ لَوْ شَاءَ اللهُ مَا تَلَوْتُهُ عَلَيْكُم. وأيضا أن الله تعالى أمرهم بتأمل أحواله، هل يجدون ما يعذرهم في ترك الاكتراث إليه، فلم يجدوا، قال الله تعالى: قُلْ إِنَّمَا أَعِظُكُم بِوَاحِدَة. وأيضا مما دعاهم إلى النظر في أموره أن هل يجدون فيه ما وجدوا في المتسمين بصنعة الكلام من التصدى لله فلوك لنيل الدنيا، بل عُرضت عليه المطامع من الثروة والرياسة ليرجع عن دينه مما لديه يعز البشر، فلم يجب إلى ذلك ليعلم بالطبيعة المستمرة على ما فيه مخالفة الهوى وكفّ النفس عن الملاذ، إنه على ما راضه الله وأكرمه لدار كرامته، دون الميل إلى شيء من حطام الدنيا، وقال: قُلْ مَا أَسْأَلُكُمْ عَلَيْهِ مِنْ أَجْرٍ وَمَا أَنَا مِنَ المُتَكَلِّفِينَ. وأيضا ما حاجهم بالدعاء إلى النظر في الأديان ليعلموا تمسكه بأحسن ما في العقول مما فيه لزوم اختيار مثله فقال: قُلْ أَوَ لَوْ جِئْتُكُم
Among them is that he grew up among a people who had no books nor study, and he never left his people, and they had no books in which he had previously trained himself in their study, so that if a newcomer came to them, they would not know his place. That is His saying: 'Do they not recognize their messenger?' (23:69) and His saying: 'These are from the news of the unseen which We reveal' (11:49). He grew up unlettered, and the unlettered one does not learn from books nor can he memorize from speech to the fullest extent; rather his retention is by spiritual intelligible forms by which he rises above the lowly. The evidence for this is that there is not transmitted from his like the narration of poetry for fear of error and other things, and therefore their amazement at the preservation of the Quran increased, and Allah said: 'We will make you recite, and you will not forget' (87:6), and He said: 'Move not your tongue with it' (75:16). And therefore the one described with preservation said that it is stronger than the hearts of men from that which He [؟] has given them. Allah said: 'And you did not recite before it any scripture' (29:48). Also, there was not mentioned about him in his past life that he occupied himself with composing speech and practicing its various forms, and it is impossible for someone like him to be able to do what those known for training in it are incapable of. The evidence is that they did not criticize him in anything from that, but rather when it was said by his saying to them: 'Bring a surah like it' (10:38), they were silent and did not claim that he had shown it in him. Allah said: 'Say: If Allah had willed, I would not have recited it to you' (10:16). Also, Allah commanded them to ponder his condition, whether they find an excuse for turning away from him, and they did not find one. Allah said: 'Say: I only advise you with one thing' (34:46). Also, among what called them to examine his affairs is whether they find in him what they found in those who claim the art of speech (rhetoric) of striving for worldly gain. Rather, worldly desires of wealth and leadership were presented to him to turn him away from his religion, from that which [؟] people are incapable, but he did not respond to that, so that it would be known by his continuous nature that opposes desire and restrains the soul from pleasures that he is upon what Allah has trained him and honored him for the abode of His generosity, without inclination to anything from the rubble of the world. And He said: 'Say: I do not ask you for any reward for it, nor am I of those who pretend' (38:86). Also, he challenged them to examine the religions so that they would know his adherence to the best of that which is in the intellects, which necessitates the choice of his like, as he said: 'Say: Even if I bring you...' (incomplete).
Source pages p. 805

Commentary
This passage continues the rational proofs for prophethood by examining the Prophet's personal qualities. The author presents several arguments: (1) The Prophet grew up among an unlettered people with no books, and he never left them, so he could not have acquired prior knowledge. This is supported by Quranic verses about his recognition and the unseen news he revealed. (2) He was unlettered (ummi), meaning he did not learn from books and could not perfectly memorize from speech; his retention was by spiritual understanding. The evidence is that no one else like him could narrate poetry without error, yet he preserved the Quran perfectly, as Allah promised. (3) He never trained in composing poetry or rhetoric in his youth, yet produced speech that the most skilled orators could not match, as proven by the challenge to produce a surah, which people failed to meet. (4) Allah commanded people to examine his life for any excuse to reject him, and they found none. (5) Unlike false claimants who seek worldly gain, the Prophet rejected offers of wealth and leadership, showing his sincerity. (6) He challenged people to compare his message with other religions, implying that his teachings represent the best of reason. These proofs collectively establish the divine origin of his message.

Key Terms
أمي
التحفظ
حفظ القرآن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet's illiteracy was a weakness that discredits his prophethood.
Correction: On the contrary, his illiteracy shows that the Quran could not be from human learning; it is a sign of divine revelation.

Checkpoint
What evidence does Al-Maturidi give to show that the Prophet could not have learned the Quran from prior books?
A) The Prophet traveled widely and studied with Jewish scholars.
B) The Prophet grew up among a people with many books.
C) The Prophet never left his unlettered people and had no prior scripture.
D) The Prophet memorized poetry as a child.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's illiteracy and the Quran's preservation are intertwined proofs that his message is from Allah, not human invention.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Prophet's illiteracy is a sign that his knowledge came from Allah, how much do you rely on human credentials and degrees versus the divine truth revealed in the Quran? Are you willing to humble your pride in education before Allah's word?
?
The Quran was preserved flawlessly despite the Prophet being unlettered. Your own memorization of Quran—is it accompanied by the same reverence and perfection? Or do you treat it casually, forgetting that it is a miracle that challenges your complacency?
?
The Prophet's tribe had no books, yet he brought a book that changed the world. You have access to countless books and scholars—what is your excuse for not immersing yourself in the Quran? What are you afraid of finding?

The Inimitable Speech and Command to Reflect
Al-Maturidi argues from lack of training and the challenge to produce a surah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's lack of training in poetry and rhetoric, combined with the Quran's inimitability, proves his prophethood.

Core Idea
The untaught Prophet produced speech that experts could not match, confirming divine origin.

Al-Maturidi continues the proofs by noting that before prophethood, the Prophet never practiced composing poetry or rhetoric. Yet the Quran challenged the most skilled orators to produce its like, and they failed. This lesson also highlights the divine command to ponder the Prophet's life for any excuse to reject him.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on rhetorical training
Read the Arabic and translation, focusing on the argument that the Prophet never occupied himself with speechcraft.
The phrase 'ضروب الكلام' refers to the various forms of eloquent speech.
2
Understand the challenge and outcome
Al-Maturidi cites the Quranic challenge 'Bring a surah like it' and notes that the disbelievers remained silent, unable to match it.
This silence is evidence of inimitability.
3
Ponder the command to reflect
The passage also mentions Allah commanding people to examine the Prophet's circumstances, yet they found no valid excuse to reject him.
The verse 'Say: I only advise you with one thing' (34:46) calls for sincere reflection.

Commentary

The author presents several arguments: (1) The Prophet grew up among an unlettered people with no books, and he never left them, so he could not have acquired prior knowledge. This is supported by Quranic verses about his recognition and the unseen news he revealed. (2) He was unlettered (ummi), meaning he did not learn from books and could not perfectly memorize from speech; his retention was by spiritual understanding. The evidence is that no one else like him could narrate poetry without error, yet he preserved the Quran perfectly, as Allah promised. (3) He never trained in composing poetry or rhetoric in his youth, yet produced speech that the most skilled orators could not match, as proven by the challenge to produce a surah, which people failed to meet. (4) Allah commanded people to examine his life for any excuse to reject him, and they found none. (5) Unlike false claimants who seek worldly gain, the Prophet rejected offers of wealth and leadership, showing his sincerity. (6) He challenged people to compare his message with other religions, implying that his teachings represent the best of reason. These proofs collectively establish the divine origin of his message.

Key Terms
ضروب الكلام
التكلف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Quran could have been composed by the Prophet himself because he was eloquent.
Correction: The Prophet never trained in eloquence, yet produced speech that even the most eloquent failed to imitate, proving divine origin.

Checkpoint
What was the response of the disbelievers when challenged to produce a surah like the Quran?
A) They produced many similar verses.
B) They accused the Prophet of copying ancient texts.
C) They remained silent and could not match it.
D) They claimed the Prophet had studied poetry.

Key Takeaway
The Quran's inimitability, combined with the Prophet's lack of training, is a compelling proof that it is from Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The disbelievers were commanded to reflect on the Prophet’s life to find an excuse to reject him, but they could not find one. Have you ever honestly examined your own life to see if your hesitation to submit fully to Allah is based on a real excuse or just stubbornness? Will you commit to removing that excuse today?
?
The Prophet had no training in eloquence, yet he produced speech that leaves experts silent. This proves the Quran is from Allah. When you read the Quran, do you treat it as the very words of your Creator, or do you sometimes regard it as just another book? How will you change your approach to recitation and reflection starting this week?
?
The disbelievers' silence in the face of the challenge was a confession that they could not produce something like the Quran. But their hearts remained hardened. Is there an area in your life where you have evidence of Allah's truth but have chosen to ignore it? What will it take for you to let that knowledge transform into action?

Rejection of Worldly Gain and the Final Challenge
Al-Maturidi argues from the Prophet's rejection of worldly gain and challenge to compare religions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's rejection of wealth and leadership, and his challenge to compare religions, serve as moral proofs for his prophethood.

Core Idea
The Prophet's sincere rejection of worldly gain shows his message is from Allah, not self-interest.

Al-Maturidi presents a moral proof: the Prophet was offered wealth and power to abandon his mission, yet he refused. Unlike false claimants who seek worldly benefit, the Prophet remained steadfast. Additionally, he challenged the people to compare his teachings with other religions, implying that his message aligns with the best of reason.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on worldly temptations
Read the Arabic and translation, noting how the Prophet rejected offers of wealth and leadership.
The verse 'Say: I do not ask you for any reward' (38:86) is cited.
2
Contrast with false claimants
Al-Maturidi compares the Prophet to those who seek worldly gain through rhetoric, showing his sincerity.
The phrase 'المتصدين لنيل الدنيا' refers to those who strive for worldly gain.
3
Reflect on the challenge to examine religions
The passage ends with the Prophet challenging people to examine his teachings against other religions, implying rational superiority.
The verse 'Say: Even if I bring you...' is incomplete but the point is clear.

منها أنه نشأ في قوم لم يكن لهم كتب ولا دراسة، مع ما لم يفارق قومه، وما كان لهم كتب قد سبق له الارتياض في دراستها كان في ضمن تلك: لو طرأ عليهم طارئ لا يجها مكانه، وذلك قوله: أَمْ لَمْ يَعْرِفُوا رَسُولَهُمْ، وقوله: تِلْكَ مِنْ أَنْبَاءِ الْغَيْبِ نُوحِيهَا. وقد نشأ أميا، والأمي لا يأخذ عن الكتب ولا يستطيع التحفظ من الأفواه غاية الحفظ، إنما يكون ضبطه بصور معقولة روحانية يرتفع بها عن المهم، دليله ما لا يوجد عن مثله رواية الأشعار مخافة الغلط وغيرها، ولذلك اشتد تعجبهم من حفظ القرآن وقال الله تعالى: سَنُقْرِئُكَ فَلَا تَنْسَى، وقال: لَا تُحَرُّكَ بِهِ لِسَانَكَ، ولذلك قال الموصوف بالحفظ إنه لأشد تعصبا من قلوب الرجال من النعم من عقلها، قال الله تعالى: وَمَا كُنْتَ تَتْلُو مِنْ قَبْلِهِ مِنْ كِتَابٍ. وأيضا أنه لم يذكر عنه في سالف عمره التشاغل بنظم الكلام وتعاطي ضروبه، ثم يمتنع عن مثله أن يتهيأ له ما يعجز عنه المعروفين برياضته، دليله أنه لم يطعن بشيء من ذلك بل لما قيل بقوله: لهم: فَأْتُوا بِسُورَةٍ مِثْلِهِ سكتوا ولم يدعوا عليه إظهاره فيه، قال الله تعالى: قُلْ لَوْ شَاءَ اللهُ مَا تَلَوْتُهُ عَلَيْكُم. وأيضا أن الله تعالى أمرهم بتأمل أحواله، هل يجدون ما يعذرهم في ترك الاكتراث إليه، فلم يجدوا، قال الله تعالى: قُلْ إِنَّمَا أَعِظُكُم بِوَاحِدَة. وأيضا مما دعاهم إلى النظر في أموره أن هل يجدون فيه ما وجدوا في المتسمين بصنعة الكلام من التصدى لله فلوك لنيل الدنيا، بل عُرضت عليه المطامع من الثروة والرياسة ليرجع عن دينه مما لديه يعز البشر، فلم يجب إلى ذلك ليعلم بالطبيعة المستمرة على ما فيه مخالفة الهوى وكفّ النفس عن الملاذ، إنه على ما راضه الله وأكرمه لدار كرامته، دون الميل إلى شيء من حطام الدنيا، وقال: قُلْ مَا أَسْأَلُكُمْ عَلَيْهِ مِنْ أَجْرٍ وَمَا أَنَا مِنَ المُتَكَلِّفِينَ. وأيضا ما حاجهم بالدعاء إلى النظر في الأديان ليعلموا تمسكه بأحسن ما في العقول مما فيه لزوم اختيار مثله فقال: قُلْ أَوَ لَوْ جِئْتُكُم
Among them is that he grew up among a people who had no books nor study, and he never left his people, and they had no books in which he had previously trained himself in their study, so that if a newcomer came to them, they would not know his place. That is His saying: 'Do they not recognize their messenger?' (23:69) and His saying: 'These are from the news of the unseen which We reveal' (11:49). He grew up unlettered, and the unlettered one does not learn from books nor can he memorize from speech to the fullest extent; rather his retention is by spiritual intelligible forms by which he rises above the lowly. The evidence for this is that there is not transmitted from his like the narration of poetry for fear of error and other things, and therefore their amazement at the preservation of the Quran increased, and Allah said: 'We will make you recite, and you will not forget' (87:6), and He said: 'Move not your tongue with it' (75:16). And therefore the one described with preservation said that it is stronger than the hearts of men from that which He [؟] has given them. Allah said: 'And you did not recite before it any scripture' (29:48). Also, there was not mentioned about him in his past life that he occupied himself with composing speech and practicing its various forms, and it is impossible for someone like him to be able to do what those known for training in it are incapable of. The evidence is that they did not criticize him in anything from that, but rather when it was said by his saying to them: 'Bring a surah like it' (10:38), they were silent and did not claim that he had shown it in him. Allah said: 'Say: If Allah had willed, I would not have recited it to you' (10:16). Also, Allah commanded them to ponder his condition, whether they find an excuse for turning away from him, and they did not find one. Allah said: 'Say: I only advise you with one thing' (34:46). Also, among what called them to examine his affairs is whether they find in him what they found in those who claim the art of speech (rhetoric) of striving for worldly gain. Rather, worldly desires of wealth and leadership were presented to him to turn him away from his religion, from that which [؟] people are incapable, but he did not respond to that, so that it would be known by his continuous nature that opposes desire and restrains the soul from pleasures that he is upon what Allah has trained him and honored him for the abode of His generosity, without inclination to anything from the rubble of the world. And He said: 'Say: I do not ask you for any reward for it, nor am I of those who pretend' (38:86). Also, he challenged them to examine the religions so that they would know his adherence to the best of that which is in the intellects, which necessitates the choice of his like, as he said: 'Say: Even if I bring you...' (incomplete).

Commentary
This passage continues the rational proofs for prophethood by examining the Prophet's personal qualities. The author presents several arguments: (1) The Prophet grew up among an unlettered people with no books, and he never left them, so he could not have acquired prior knowledge. This is supported by Quranic verses about his recognition and the unseen news he revealed. (2) He was unlettered (ummi), meaning he did not learn from books and could not perfectly memorize from speech; his retention was by spiritual understanding. The evidence is that no one else like him could narrate poetry without error, yet he preserved the Quran perfectly, as Allah promised. (3) He never trained in composing poetry or rhetoric in his youth, yet produced speech that the most skilled orators could not match, as proven by the challenge to produce a surah, which people failed to meet. (4) Allah commanded people to examine his life for any excuse to reject him, and they found none. (5) Unlike false claimants who seek worldly gain, the Prophet rejected offers of wealth and leadership, showing his sincerity. (6) He challenged people to compare his message with other religions, implying that his teachings represent the best of reason. These proofs collectively establish the divine origin of his message.

Argument from the Prophet's Life and Character
Maturidi argues from the Prophet's untaught eloquence and moral integrity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the Prophet's lack of prior training in eloquence and his moral integrity as a proof of his prophethood.

Core Idea
The Prophet's untaught eloquence and selfless character point to divine origin.

Maturidi begins by examining the Prophet Muhammad's life before revelation. He argues that the Prophet was never known to compose poetry or oratory, yet he produced the Qur'an which amazed even the experts. Moreover, the Prophet's refusal of worldly wealth and power shows his message was not self-serving. These facts together form a compelling proof that his prophethood is genuine.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the Prophet's prior life
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the references to the Prophet's lack of engagement with poetry and speech composition.
Maturidi uses these facts to set up the argument.
2
Identify the argument from lack of training
Maturidi states that the Prophet did not occupy himself with composing speech. Then he challenges the disbelievers to produce something similar, and they were silent. This shows the Qur'an is beyond human capacity.
The verse 'Say: If Allah had willed, I would not have recited it to you' confirms divine origin.
3
Reflect on the moral integrity argument
The Prophet was offered wealth and leadership to abandon his mission, but he refused. This proves he was not after worldly gains, unlike false claimants.
The verse 'Say: I ask of you no reward' reinforces his sincerity.
4
Understand the combined proof
Both his untaught eloquence and his moral integrity together make a strong case that his message is from Allah.

مثله رواية الأشعار مخافة الغلط وغيرها، ولذلك اشتد تعجبهم من حفظ القرآن وقال الله تعالى: سَنُقْرِئُكَ فَلَا تَنْسَى (1)، وقال: لَا تُحَرُّكَ بِهِ لِسَانَكَ (2)، ولذلك قال الموصوف بالحفظ إنه لأشد تعصبا المُتَكَلِّفِينَ (7). وأيضا ما حاجهم بالدعاء إلى النظر في الأديان ليعلموا تمسكه بأحسن ما في العقول مما فيه لزوم اختيار مثله فقال: "قُلْ أَوَ لَوْ جِئْتُكُم بِأَهْدَى مِمَّا وَجَدْتُمْ عَلَيْهِ آبَاءَ كُم" (8)، وقال: تَعَالَوْا إِلَى كَلِمَةٍ سَوَاءٍ (9). وأيضا تحداهم بالعجز عما أتى به من القرآن ليكون حجة له عند امتناعه عن وسع البشر، مع ما وجدت الصناعة التي بها نباهة ورفعة من الكلام نوعان: أحدهما صناعة الشعر بالنظم الرائع والتأليف المؤنق، والثانى صناعة الكهانة بافادة المعاني العربية من تقدمه القول على الأشياء الكائنة، ثم وجد القرآن بنظمه مستعليا على ما جاء به الشعراء، وبمعانيه على ما جاء به الكهنة، فوجب أنه ليس من كلام البشر. وفى مثله احتجاج الله تعالى: "قُلْ لَئِنْ اجْتَمَعَت الإِنس والجن عَلَى أَنْ يَأْتُوا بِمِثْلِ هَذَا القُرْآن" (10)، وقوله: وَمَا هُو بِقَوْلِ شَاعِرٍ (11)، وقوله: أَوْ لَمْ تَأْتِهِمْ بَيِّنَةٌ (12)، [وقوله]: كِتَابٌ أَنْزَلْنَاهُ إِلَيْكَ مُبَارَكٌ (13)، وقوله: قُلْ فَأْتُوا بِكِتَابِ مِنْ عِنْدِ اللهِ (14). وأيضا ما أشار من التأييد الذي يظهر دعوتها و يفلح حجته بما يبصره على من شاقه وحاده؛ إذ الله تعالى بعثه في أوان طموس من أعلام الهدى ودروس من آثار الدين إلى العباد لينقذهم من الردى، ثم لما أقامه هذا المقام الجليل والخطب الجسيم لم يُخله عن نصره والتمكين [له] ليقوى منه عليه بما أكرمه من المقام بقوله: (إِنَّا لِنَنْصُرُ رُسُلَنَا) (15)، وقوله: كَتَبَ الله (16).
Like him, the transmission of poems (ash‘ār) for fear of error and other things, and therefore their amazement at the preservation of the Qur'an intensified, and Allah Most High said: 'We will make you recite, so you shall not forget' (1), and He said: 'Do not move your tongue with it' (2), and therefore the one described as having preservation said that it is more firmly rooted than the hearts of men, among the blessings of its intellect. Allah Most High said: 'And you did not recite before it any book' (3). Also, it is not mentioned about him in his past life that he occupied himself with composing speech (naẓm al-kalām) and practicing its varieties, then it is impossible that he would be able to produce what those known for its practice are incapable of. Its proof is that they did not criticize anything of that, but when it was said by his saying: to them: 'Then bring a surah like it' (4), they were silent and did not claim that he showed it from within himself. Allah Most High said: 'Say: If Allah had willed, I would not have recited it to you' (5). Also, Allah Most High commanded them to reflect on his states: would they find an excuse for not paying attention to him? They did not find any. Allah Most High said: 'Say: I only admonish you with one thing' (6). Also, among what called them to consider his affairs is whether they find in him what they found in those who claim the craft of speech (ṣinā‘at al-kalām) of striving for the sake of gaining the world. Rather, inducements of wealth and leadership were presented to him to turn him away from his religion, from that which he had of what humans hold dear, but he did not respond to that, so that it may be known by the continuous nature (al-ṭabī‘a al-mustamirra) upon what opposes desire and restraining the soul from pleasures, that he is upon what Allah trained him and honored him for the abode of His nobility, without inclining to any of the temporal goods. And he said: 'Say: I ask of you no reward for it, nor am I of those who pretend' (7). Also, he argued with them by calling them to consider religions, so that they might know his adherence to the best of what is in intellects, which requires choosing the like of him. He said: 'Say: Even if I bring you better than what you found your fathers upon?' (8), and He said: 'Come to a common word' (9). Also, he challenged them to be unable to produce what he brought of the Qur'an, so that it would be a proof for him, given its being beyond human capacity, along with the fact that the craft (al-ṣinā‘a) by which there is distinction and elevation is of two types: one is the craft of poetry with splendid composition and elegant arrangement, and the second is the craft of soothsaying (kihāna) by conveying Arabic meanings through prior prediction of things that come to be. Then the Qur'an was found with its composition surpassing what the poets brought, and with its meanings surpassing what the soothsayers brought. So it is necessary that it is not from human speech. And in like manner is the argument of Allah Most High: 'Say: If mankind and jinn were to gather together to produce the like of this Qur'an' (10), and His saying: 'And it is not the saying of a poet' (11), and His saying: 'Or has there not come to them a clear proof?' (12), [and His saying]: 'A Book which We have sent down to you, blessed' (13), and His saying: 'Say: Then bring a book from Allah' (14). Also, the support which manifests his call and perfects his argument by granting him insight against those who oppose and contend with him; for Allah Most High sent him at a time of effacement of guidance's signs and decay of religion's traces to the servants to save them from destruction. Then when He established him in this noble station and great matter, He did not leave him without His victory and empowerment, to strengthen him thereby at that station with which He honored him, by His saying: 'Indeed, We will support Our messengers' (15), and His saying: 'Allah has written' (16).
Source pages p. 805

Commentary
This passage presents a series of arguments proving the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him) by examining his life and the nature of the Qur'an. It begins by noting that the Prophet was not previously engaged in poetry or oratory, so his inability to produce such speech naturally made people amazed at the Qur'an's preservation. Allah's promise 'We will make you recite, so you shall not forget' and the command 'Do not move your tongue with it' show divine safeguarding. The author then argues that the Prophet's lack of prior training in composing eloquent speech means he could not have produced what even skilled poets and orators are incapable of. The proof is that when challenged to bring a surah like the Qur'an, the disbelievers were silent and could not claim that the Prophet had shown his ability before. Allah's statement 'Say: If Allah had willed, I would not have recited it to you' confirms that the Qur'an is from Him. Next, the author highlights the Prophet's moral integrity: despite being offered wealth and leadership to abandon his message, he refused, demonstrating that he was not after worldly gain. His call to 'Come to a common word' shows his reliance on reason and fairness. The most powerful argument is the Qur'an's inimitability (i‘jāz). The author divides eloquent speech into two crafts: poetry (with beautiful composition) and soothsaying (with predictive meanings). The Qur'an excels both in composition and meaning, proving it is beyond human capacity. Allah's challenge to produce a similar book confirms this. Finally, the author points to divine support and victory granted to the Prophet, fulfilling Allah's promise to support His messengers, which further authenticates his prophethood.

Key Terms
نظم
صنعة الكلام
برهان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet's lack of prior education alone proves his prophethood.
Correction: Maturidi argues that both his untaught eloquence and his moral integrity are needed together as proof; one without the other is insufficient.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did the Prophet not do in his past life that supports his prophethood?
A) Recite the Qur'an
B) Compose poetry and speech
C) Trade
D) Seek knowledge

Key Takeaway
Maturidi establishes the Prophet's prophethood through his untaught eloquence and his unblemished moral character.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the Qur'an, do you ever pause to consider that it came through an unlettered man? How does that truth affect the weight you give to its words in your daily decisions? Will you let that awe change how you approach your next recitation?
?
The Prophet refused wealth and leadership to remain on the truth. Is there any worldly gain—a promotion, a relationship, a comfort—that you are holding onto even though it conflicts with your faith? Are you willing to name it and release it today?
?
You have been commanded to reflect on the Prophet's life (Q 34:46). When was the last time you studied his character as proof of his prophethood—not just as a historical figure, but as a living witness to the truth? What step will you take this week to know him more personally?
