Prophethood
beginner
5 min
The Qur'an's Inimitability and Divine Support
Maturidi argues from the Qur'an's inimitability and divine support.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the Qur'an's surpassing of poetry and soothsaying, along with divine support, as proof of prophethood.

Core Idea
The Qur'an's unmatched composition and meaning, plus God's victory, prove its divine origin.

Maturidi continues his proofs by focusing on the Qur'an itself. He argues that the Qur'an surpasses both poetry and soothsaying in its composition and meaning, demonstrating it is beyond human capacity. He also points to the divine support and victory granted to the Prophet as further evidence that his mission was from Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the Qur'an's challenge
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note how Maturidi divides eloquent speech into two crafts and shows the Qur'an's superiority.
The challenge to produce a similar book is a key proof of inimitability.
2
Understand the two crafts
Maturidi identifies poetry (splendid composition) and soothsaying (predictive meanings). The Qur'an excels both, so it is not human speech.
This argument addresses both the form and content.
3
Consider the divine support argument
The Prophet was sent in a time of spiritual darkness, yet God supported him and gave him victory, fulfilling His promise.
This shows that his success was not by his own power but by Allah's will.
4
Connect to the overall proof
Together, the inimitability of the Qur'an and the divine support confirm that Muhammad is a true prophet.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مثله رواية الأشعار مخافة الغلط وغيرها، ولذلك اشتد تعجبهم من حفظ القرآن وقال الله تعالى: سَنُقْرِئُكَ فَلَا تَنْسَى (1)، وقال: لَا تُحَرُّكَ بِهِ لِسَانَكَ (2)، ولذلك قال الموصوف بالحفظ إنه لأشد تعصبا من قلوب الرجال من النعم من عقلها، قال الله تعالى: "وَمَا كُنْتَ تَتْلُو مِنْ قَبْلِهِ مِنْ كِتَابٍ" (3). وأيضا أنه لم يذكر عنه في سالف عمره التشاغل بنظم الكلام وتعاطي ضروبه، ثم يمتنع عن مثله أن يتهيأ له ما يعجز عنه المعروفين بارتياضه، دليله أنه لم يطعن بشيء من ذلك بل لما قيل بقوله: ال لهم: "فَأْتُوا بِسُورَةٍ مِثْلِهِ" (4) سكتوا ولم يدعوا عليه إظهاره فيه، قال الله تعالى: "قُلْ لَوْ شَاءَ اللهُ مَا تَلَوْتُه عَلَيْكُم" (5). وأيضا أن الله تعالى أمرهم بتأمل أحواله، هل يجدون ما يعذرهم في ترك الاكتراث إليه، فلم يجدوا، قال الله تعالى: قُلْ إِنَّمَا أَعِظُكُم بِوَاحِدَة (6). وأيضا مما دعاهم إلى النظر في أموره أن هل يجدون فيه ما وجدوا فى المتسمين بصنعة الكلام من التصدى لله فلوك لنيل الدنيا، بل عُرضت عليه المطامع من الثروة والرياسة ليرجع عن دينه مما لديه يعز البشر، فلم يجب إلى ذلك ليعلم بالطبيعة المستمرة على ما فيه مخالفة الهوى وكفّ النفس عن الملاذ، إنه على ما راضه الله وأكرمه لدار كرامته، دون الميل إلى شيء من حطام الدنيا، وقال: قُلْ مَا أَسْأَلُكُمْ عَلَيْهِ مِنْ أَجْرٍ وَمَا أَنَا مِنَ المُتَكَلِّفِينَ (7). وأيضا ما حاجهم بالدعاء إلى النظر في الأديان ليعلموا تمسكه بأحسن ما في العقول مما فيه لزوم اختيار مثله فقال: "قُلْ أَوَ لَوْ جِئْتُكُم بِأَهْدَى مِمَّا وَجَدْتُمْ عَلَيْهِ آبَاءَ كُم" (8)، وقال: تَعَالَوْا إِلَى كَلِمَةٍ سَوَاءٍ (9). وأيضا تحداهم بالعجز عما أتى به من القرآن ليكون حجة له عند امتناعه عن وسع البشر، مع ما وجدت الصناعة التي بها نباهة ورفعة من الكلام نوعان: أحدهما صناعة الشعر بالنظم الرائع والتأليف المؤنق، والثانى صناعة الكهانة بافادة المعاني العربية من تقدمه القول على الأشياء الكائنة، ثم وجد القرآن بنظمه مستعليا على ما جاء به الشعراء، وبمعانيه على ما جاء به الكهنة، فوجب أنه ليس من كلام البشر. وفى مثله احتجاج الله تعالى: "قُلْ لَئِنْ اجْتَمَعَت الإِنس والجن عَلَى أَنْ يَأْتُوا بِمِثْلِ هَذَا القُرْآن" (10)، وقوله: وَمَا هُو بِقَوْلِ شَاعِرٍ (11)، وقوله: أَوْ لَمْ تَأْتِهِمْ بَيِّنَةٌ (12)، [وقوله]: كِتَابٌ أَنْزَلْنَاهُ إِلَيْكَ مُبَارَكٌ (13)، وقوله: قُلْ فَأْتُوا بِكِتَابِ مِنْ عِنْدِ اللهِ (14). وأيضا ما أشار من التأييد الذي يظهر دعوتها و يفلح حجته بما يبصره على من شاقه وحاده؛ إذ الله تعالى بعثه في أوان طموس من أعلام الهدى ودروس من آثار الدين إلى العباد لينقذهم من الردى، ثم لما أقامه هذا المقام الجليل والخطب الجسيم لم يُخله عن نصره والتمكين [له] ليقوى منه عليه بما أكرمه من المقام بقوله: (إِنَّا لِنَنْصُرُ رُسُلَنَا) (15)، وقوله: كَتَبَ الله (16).
Like him, the transmission of poems (ash‘ār) for fear of error and other things, and therefore their amazement at the preservation of the Qur'an intensified, and Allah Most High said: 'We will make you recite, so you shall not forget' (1), and He said: 'Do not move your tongue with it' (2), and therefore the one described as having preservation said that it is more firmly rooted than the hearts of men, among the blessings of its intellect. Allah Most High said: 'And you did not recite before it any book' (3). Also, it is not mentioned about him in his past life that he occupied himself with composing speech (naẓm al-kalām) and practicing its varieties, then it is impossible that he would be able to produce what those known for its practice are incapable of. Its proof is that they did not criticize anything of that, but when it was said by his saying: to them: 'Then bring a surah like it' (4), they were silent and did not claim that he showed it from within himself. Allah Most High said: 'Say: If Allah had willed, I would not have recited it to you' (5). Also, Allah Most High commanded them to reflect on his states: would they find an excuse for not paying attention to him? They did not find any. Allah Most High said: 'Say: I only admonish you with one thing' (6). Also, among what called them to consider his affairs is whether they find in him what they found in those who claim the craft of speech (ṣinā‘at al-kalām) of striving for the sake of gaining the world. Rather, inducements of wealth and leadership were presented to him to turn him away from his religion, from that which he had of what humans hold dear, but he did not respond to that, so that it may be known by the continuous nature (al-ṭabī‘a al-mustamirra) upon what opposes desire and restraining the soul from pleasures, that he is upon what Allah trained him and honored him for the abode of His nobility, without inclining to any of the temporal goods. And he said: 'Say: I ask of you no reward for it, nor am I of those who pretend' (7). Also, he argued with them by calling them to consider religions, so that they might know his adherence to the best of what is in intellects, which requires choosing the like of him. He said: 'Say: Even if I bring you better than what you found your fathers upon?' (8), and He said: 'Come to a common word' (9). Also, he challenged them to be unable to produce what he brought of the Qur'an, so that it would be a proof for him, given its being beyond human capacity, along with the fact that the craft (al-ṣinā‘a) by which there is distinction and elevation is of two types: one is the craft of poetry with splendid composition and elegant arrangement, and the second is the craft of soothsaying (kihāna) by conveying Arabic meanings through prior prediction of things that come to be. Then the Qur'an was found with its composition surpassing what the poets brought, and with its meanings surpassing what the soothsayers brought. So it is necessary that it is not from human speech. And in like manner is the argument of Allah Most High: 'Say: If mankind and jinn were to gather together to produce the like of this Qur'an' (10), and His saying: 'And it is not the saying of a poet' (11), and His saying: 'Or has there not come to them a clear proof?' (12), [and His saying]: 'A Book which We have sent down to you, blessed' (13), and His saying: 'Say: Then bring a book from Allah' (14). Also, the support which manifests his call and perfects his argument by granting him insight against those who oppose and contend with him; for Allah Most High sent him at a time of effacement of guidance's signs and decay of religion's traces to the servants to save them from destruction. Then when He established him in this noble station and great matter, He did not leave him without His victory and empowerment, to strengthen him thereby at that station with which He honored him, by His saying: 'Indeed, We will support Our messengers' (15), and His saying: 'Allah has written' (16).
Source pages p. 805

Commentary
This passage presents a series of arguments proving the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him) by examining his life and the nature of the Qur'an. It begins by noting that the Prophet was not previously engaged in poetry or oratory, so his inability to produce such speech naturally made people amazed at the Qur'an's preservation. Allah's promise 'We will make you recite, so you shall not forget' and the command 'Do not move your tongue with it' show divine safeguarding. The author then argues that the Prophet's lack of prior training in composing eloquent speech means he could not have produced what even skilled poets and orators are incapable of. The proof is that when challenged to bring a surah like the Qur'an, the disbelievers were silent and could not claim that the Prophet had shown his ability before. Allah's statement 'Say: If Allah had willed, I would not have recited it to you' confirms that the Qur'an is from Him. Next, the author highlights the Prophet's moral integrity: despite being offered wealth and leadership to abandon his message, he refused, demonstrating that he was not after worldly gain. His call to 'Come to a common word' shows his reliance on reason and fairness. The most powerful argument is the Qur'an's inimitability (i‘jāz). The author divides eloquent speech into two crafts: poetry (with beautiful composition) and soothsaying (with predictive meanings). The Qur'an excels both in composition and meaning, proving it is beyond human capacity. Allah's challenge to produce a similar book confirms this. Finally, the author points to divine support and victory granted to the Prophet, fulfilling Allah's promise to support His messengers, which further authenticates his prophethood.

Key Terms
إعجاز
تحدي
صنعة الكلام
نظم
كهانة
برهان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Qur'an is simply a form of excellent poetry.
Correction: Maturidi argues that the Qur'an surpasses both poetry (in composition) and soothsaying (in meaning), making it distinct from human speech.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what two types of eloquent speech did the Qur'an surpass?
A) Poetry and philosophy
B) Poetry and soothsaying
C) Oratory and rhetoric
D) Prose and verse

Key Takeaway
The Qur'an's superiority over poetry and soothsaying, combined with divine support, confirms Muhammad's prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Qur'an, do you truly recognize that no human effort could produce its words? How does that understanding affect your reverence for it? Commit to reading one verse today with the awareness that it is beyond human capacity.
?
This lesson shows that God supported His Prophet even when guidance seemed lost. In what area of your life do you feel spiritually lost or unsupported? Are you willing to trust that God's support will come even when you cannot see it? Surrender that area to Him now.
?
The Prophet called people to use their intellects to examine religions. Have you ever used your own reason to verify the truth of Islam, or do you rely on upbringing? What would it take for you to personally affirm that the Qur'an is from God? Take a step today to study a proof of prophethood seriously.

Prophethood
beginner
5 min
The Quran's Inimitability: Surpassing Poetry and Soothsaying
Maturidi argues the Quran surpasses poetry and soothsaying.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that the Quran's superiority over all human speech forms—specifically poetry and soothsaying—demonstrates its divine origin.

Core Idea
The Quran exceeds all human rhetorical arts, proving it is not from humans.

Maturidi presents a clear logical proof for the Quran's divine origin: if it were human speech, it would fit within known human crafts of elevated speech. He identifies two such crafts—poetry and soothsaying—and shows how the Quran surpasses both. This passage lays the foundation for the doctrine of i'jaz (inimitability).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the English translation. Let Maturidi's argument flow naturally.
2
Identify the two crafts of elevated speech
Notice that Maturidi categorizes human eloquence into two types: poetry (shi'r) with its fine composition, and soothsaying (kihana) with its meaningful utterances about future events.
This classification is key to his argument.
3
See how the Quran excels both
Maturidi asserts that the Quran surpasses poetry in composition (nazm) and soothsaying in meaning (ma'ani). Ask yourself: why does this superiority prove it is not human?
The conclusion is that it must be divine speech.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بِأَهْدَى مِمَّا وَجَدْتُمْ عَلَيْهِ آبَاءَ كُم، وقال: تَعَالَوْا إِلَى كَلِمَةٍ سَوَاءٍ. وأيضا تحداهم بالعجز عما أتى به من القرآن ليكون حجة له عند امتناعه عن وسع البشر، مع ما وجدت الصناعة التي بها نباهة ورفعة من الكلام نوعان: أحدهما صناعة الشعر بالنظم الرائع والتأليف المؤنق، والثانى صناعة الكهانة بإفادة المعاني العربية من تقدمه القول على الأشياء الكائنة، ثم وجد القرآن بنظمه مستعليا على ما جاء به الشعراء، وبمعانيه على ما جاء به الكهنة، فوجب أنه ليس من كلام البشر. وفى مثله احتجاج الله تعالى: قُلْ لَئِنْ اجْتَمَعَتِ الإِنسُ وَالْجِنُ عَلَى أَنْ يَأْتُوا بِمِثْلِ هَذَا الْقُرْآنِ، وقوله: وَمَا هُوَ بِقَوْلِ شَاعِرٍ، وقوله: أَوَ لَمْ تَأْتِهِمْ بَيْنَةٌ، وقوله: كِتَابٌ أَنْزَلْنَاهُ إِلَيْكَ مُبَارَكٌ، وقوله: قُلْ فَأْتُوا بِكِتَابٍ مِنْ عِنْدِ اللهِ.
By that which is more guided than what you found your fathers upon, and He said: Come to a word of equality. And also He challenged them with inability regarding what he brought of the Quran to be a proof for him, given its being beyond the capacity of humans, along with what was found of the craft by which there is eminence and elevation of speech: two types: one is the craft of poetry with splendid composition and harmonious arrangement, and the second is the craft of soothsaying by conveying Arabic meanings from his antecedent utterance about future things. Then the Quran was found, in its composition, excelling what the poets brought, and in its meanings excelling what the soothsayers brought, so it is necessary that it is not from human speech. And in like manner is God's argument: 'Say: If mankind and jinn gathered to produce the like of this Quran...' and His saying: 'And it is not the saying of a poet,' and His saying: 'Or has there not come to them a clear proof,' and His saying: 'A Book We have sent down to you, blessed,' and His saying: 'Say: Bring a book from God...'
Source pages p. 806

Commentary
This passage presents a proof for the divine origin of the Quran based on its inimitability (i'jaz). Maturidi begins by noting that God challenged the disbelievers to produce something like the Quran, and they were unable. He then identifies two types of elevated human speech: poetry, characterized by fine composition and pleasing arrangement, and soothsaying, which claims to convey meaning about future events. The Quran, however, surpasses poetry in its composition (nazm) and surpasses soothsaying in its meanings (ma'ani). Therefore, it cannot be human speech. To support this, Maturidi cites several Quranic verses that argue for the Quran's uniqueness, such as the challenge to produce a similar book and the denial that it is the speech of a poet. The argument follows a clear logical sequence: the Quran is either human or divine; it exceeds all known human rhetorical arts; therefore, it must be divine.

Key Terms
إعجاز (i'jaz)
نظم (nazm)
شعر (shi'r)
كهانة (kihana)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Quran's inimitability is only about its stylistic beauty.
Correction: Maturidi also emphasizes superiority in meaning over soothsaying, showing i'jaz encompasses both form and content.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what two types of elevated speech does the Quran surpass?
A) Poetry and prose
B) Poetry and soothsaying
C) Soothsaying and rhetoric
D) Rhetoric and prose

Key Takeaway
Maturidi proves the Quran is divine by showing it exceeds all human rhetorical arts—both poetry and soothsaying—in composition and meaning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the Quran, do you feel you are encountering something utterly beyond human capacity, or has familiarity dulled your sense of its miraculous nature? What would change if you approached it with the awe it deserves?
?
Maturidi argues the Quran surpasses poetry and soothsaying. Which of these two—beauty of style or depth of meaning—do you tend to appreciate more in the Quran? Are you neglecting the other, and how can you cultivate both?
?
The Quran challenges you to produce something like it. If you truly believe it is from God, does it bother you that you spend more time on human-made content than on His speech? What would it look like to let the Quran's superiority reshape your daily priorities?

Prophethood

Divine Support: The Unseen Hand Behind the Prophets
Maturidi states the general principle of divine support for messengers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how divine support (ta'yid) serves as a rational proof of prophethood, as explained by Imam Maturidi.

Core Idea
Prophets succeed not by human power but by Allah's direct support.

Imam Maturidi presents a powerful argument: the success of prophets despite overwhelming odds points to divine backing. This lesson examines the general principle that Allah supports His messengers, a truth affirmed by Quranic promises.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage about divine support
Focus on the verses quoted: إنا لننصر رسلنا and كتب الله لأغلبن أنا ورسلي. Notice how Maturidi uses them as proof.
2
Understand the proof structure
Maturidi argues that God promised victory to messengers, and that promise is fulfilled. This shows the truth of their prophethood.
3
Reflect on the implications
Why is this a strong argument? Because it shows that prophethood is not based on worldly power but on divine will.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضا ما أشار من التأييد الذي يظهر دعوتها و يفلح حجته بما يبصره على من شاقه وحاده؛ إذ الله تعالى بعثه في أوان طموس من أعلام الهدى ودروس من آثار الدين إلى العباد لينقذهم من الردى، ثم لما أقامه هذا المقام الجليل والخطب الجسيم لم يُخله عن نصره والتمكين له ليقوى منه عليه بما أكرمه من المقام بقوله: إِنَّا لَنَنْصُرُ رُسُلَنَا، وقوله: كَتَبَ اللهُ لَأَغْلِبَنَّ أَنَا وَرُسُلِي، وبمثله سبقت كلمته لعباده المرسلين. ثم كان له أيضا من خصوص حال أن بعث إلى الناس كافة، ووعد له الغلبة والنصر ليعلم أنه لم يرجع قوته إلى معونة بشرية يتوصل بها طلاب دول الدنيا إلى بغياتهم من إرث ملك فى حسبه أو قنية مال يستمتع بها، كان كما قال الله: وَوَجَدَكَ عَائِلًا فَأَغْنَى، ولا عشيرة، بل كانوا أشد الناس عليه وأجهدهم في إطفاء نوره حتى قد أخرجوه من بين أظهرهم طريدا وحيدا، ثم مع ذلك لم يدعو شيئا مما تسره إليه النفس إلا أتوه، فلم يمل إليهم، بل صبر على كل أذى واحتمل كل أمر صعب، إلا بالإجابة له في الحق، قال الله تعالى: لَقَدْ جَاءَكُمْ رَسُولٌ مِنْ أَنْفُسِكُمْ، وقال: إِلَّا تَنْصُرُوهُ فَقَدْ نَصَرَهُ اللهُ، وقال: وَيَوْمَ حُنَيْنٍ إِذْ أَعْجَبَتْكُمْ كَثْرَتُكُمْ، وقال: وَمَا أَفَاءَ اللهُ، وغير ذلك من الآيات والأدلة الصادقة أنه بالله قام وبه انتصر.
And also what is indicated of the support that makes his call manifest and his argument succeed, by which He gives him insight against whoever opposes him; for God sent him in a time of obliteration of the beacons of guidance and effacement of the traces of religion to the servants to rescue them from destruction. Then when He established him in this lofty station and great matter, He did not leave him without His help and empowerment to strengthen him, by the station with which He honored him, by His saying: 'Indeed We support Our messengers,' and His saying: 'God has written: I will prevail, I and My messengers,' and similarly His word preceded for His sent servants. Then also it was from his particular situation that he was sent to all people, and he was promised victory and triumph, so that it be known that his strength did not rely on human assistance through which seekers of worldly kingdoms attain their desires of inheriting a kingdom or acquiring wealth to enjoy. He was as God said: 'And He found you needy and enriched you,' with no clan, rather they were the most severe people against him and the most diligent in extinguishing his light until they expelled him from among them, driven out and alone. Yet despite that, they offered him everything that the soul desires, but he did not incline to them; rather he endured every harm and bore every difficult matter, except by responding to him in truth. God said: 'There has come to you a messenger from among yourselves,' and He said: 'If you do not support him, God has supported him,' and He said: 'And on the day of Hunayn when your multitude impressed you,' and He said: 'And what God gave as spoils,' and other verses and truthful evidences that he stood by God and by Him he triumphed.
Source pages p. 806

Commentary
This passage presents a second proof of prophethood: the divine support (ta'yid) granted to the Prophet Muhammad. Maturidi argues that God sent the Prophet at a time when guidance was scarce and religion was fading. Despite the Prophet's lack of worldly power—no wealth, no clan—he was promised victory and indeed succeeded. Maturidi highlights that the Prophet could have been swayed by offers of worldly goods but remained steadfast. The Quranic verses cited demonstrate that God supported him even when his followers were few, such as at the Battle of Hunayn. This support, not reliant on human means, shows that his mission was from God. The argument follows: if the Prophet had relied on human support, he would have failed; but he succeeded through God alone, proving divine backing.

Key Terms
تأييد
نصر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the Prophet's success was due to his own political skill or military strategy.
Correction: Maturidi emphasizes that the support was from God, not human means.

Checkpoint
What does the verse 'إنا لننصر رسلنا' indicate?
A) Prophets support themselves
B) God supports His messengers
C) The Prophet had a large army
D) The Prophet was wealthy

Key Takeaway
Divine support, promised in the Quran, is a key proof that the Prophet's mission was from Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet was sent in a time of 'obliteration of the beacons of guidance.' Look at your own life—what spiritual darkness surrounds you? Are you a beacon of guidance in that darkness, or have you let it overwhelm you? What concrete step will you take this week to actively manifest the truth you believe, trusting Allah's support?
?
Maturidi argues that the Prophet's success came not from personal ability but from Allah's direct help. In what areas of your life do you rely on your own skill rather than crying out to Allah for His support? Will you today sincerely ask Allah to empower you in a specific struggle you are facing?
?
Divine support for the Prophet was promised in the Quran and fulfilled. Do you live with the certainty that Allah's promises are true, even when you see no evidence of victory? Where in your life are you wavering in that trust? Commit to memorizing one of the two verses from this lesson and repeating it whenever doubt creeps in.

The Prophet's Unique Journey: From Poverty to Triumph
Maturidi details the Prophet's poor start and ultimate triumph.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's lack of worldly resources and his eventual victory demonstrate divine support.

Core Idea
The Prophet's poverty and persecution make his success a clear miracle.

Maturidi now focuses on the Prophet's personal circumstances: he had no wealth, no clan, and was expelled from Mecca. Yet he persevered and succeeded. This lesson explores how these facts strengthen the proof of prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the second part of the passage
Notice the description of the Prophet's poverty (عائل) and lack of clan, and how he was expelled.
2
Contrast with worldly kings
Maturidi contrasts the Prophet with seekers of worldly power who rely on wealth and clan.
3
See how God fulfilled His promise
Despite all odds, the Prophet succeeded, as shown in verses like 'If you do not support him, God has supported him' and the battle of Hunayn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضا ما أشار من التأييد الذي يظهر دعوتها و يفلح حجته بما يبصره على من شاقه وحاده؛ إذ الله تعالى بعثه في أوان طموس من أعلام الهدى ودروس من آثار الدين إلى العباد لينقذهم من الردى، ثم لما أقامه هذا المقام الجليل والخطب الجسيم لم يُخله عن نصره والتمكين له ليقوى منه عليه بما أكرمه من المقام بقوله: إِنَّا لَنَنْصُرُ رُسُلَنَا، وقوله: كَتَبَ اللهُ لَأَغْلِبَنَّ أَنَا وَرُسُلِي، وبمثله سبقت كلمته لعباده المرسلين. ثم كان له أيضا من خصوص حال أن بعث إلى الناس كافة، ووعد له الغلبة والنصر ليعلم أنه لم يرجع قوته إلى معونة بشرية يتوصل بها طلاب دول الدنيا إلى بغياتهم من إرث ملك فى حسبه أو قنية مال يستمتع بها، كان كما قال الله: وَوَجَدَكَ عَائِلًا فَأَغْنَى، ولا عشيرة، بل كانوا أشد الناس عليه وأجهدهم في إطفاء نوره حتى قد أخرجوه من بين أظهرهم طريدا وحيدا، ثم مع ذلك لم يدعو شيئا مما تسره إليه النفس إلا أتوه، فلم يمل إليهم، بل صبر على كل أذى واحتمل كل أمر صعب، إلا بالإجابة له في الحق، قال الله تعالى: لَقَدْ جَاءَكُمْ رَسُولٌ مِنْ أَنْفُسِكُمْ، وقال: إِلَّا تَنْصُرُوهُ فَقَدْ نَصَرَهُ اللهُ، وقال: وَيَوْمَ حُنَيْنٍ إِذْ أَعْجَبَتْكُمْ كَثْرَتُكُمْ، وقال: وَمَا أَفَاءَ اللهُ، وغير ذلك من الآيات والأدلة الصادقة أنه بالله قام وبه انتصر.
And also what is indicated of the support that makes his call manifest and his argument succeed, by which He gives him insight against whoever opposes him; for God sent him in a time of obliteration of the beacons of guidance and effacement of the traces of religion to the servants to rescue them from destruction. Then when He established him in this lofty station and great matter, He did not leave him without His help and empowerment to strengthen him, by the station with which He honored him, by His saying: 'Indeed We support Our messengers,' and His saying: 'God has written: I will prevail, I and My messengers,' and similarly His word preceded for His sent servants. Then also it was from his particular situation that he was sent to all people, and he was promised victory and triumph, so that it be known that his strength did not rely on human assistance through which seekers of worldly kingdoms attain their desires of inheriting a kingdom or acquiring wealth to enjoy. He was as God said: 'And He found you needy and enriched you,' with no clan, rather they were the most severe people against him and the most diligent in extinguishing his light until they expelled him from among them, driven out and alone. Yet despite that, they offered him everything that the soul desires, but he did not incline to them; rather he endured every harm and bore every difficult matter, except by responding to him in truth. God said: 'There has come to you a messenger from among yourselves,' and He said: 'If you do not support him, God has supported him,' and He said: 'And on the day of Hunayn when your multitude impressed you,' and He said: 'And what God gave as spoils,' and other verses and truthful evidences that he stood by God and by Him he triumphed.
Source pages p. 806

Commentary
This passage presents a second proof of prophethood: the divine support (ta'yid) granted to the Prophet Muhammad. Maturidi argues that God sent the Prophet at a time when guidance was scarce and religion was fading. Despite the Prophet's lack of worldly power—no wealth, no clan—he was promised victory and indeed succeeded. Maturidi highlights that the Prophet could have been swayed by offers of worldly goods but remained steadfast. The Quranic verses cited demonstrate that God supported him even when his followers were few, such as at the Battle of Hunayn. This support, not reliant on human means, shows that his mission was from God. The argument follows: if the Prophet had relied on human support, he would have failed; but he succeeded through God alone, proving divine backing.

Key Terms
تأييد
نصر
عائل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the Prophet's eventual military success was due to his strategic alliances.
Correction: Maturidi shows that his initial weakness and divine intervention prove the source was God.

Checkpoint
What was the Prophet's condition before his mission?
A) He was wealthy with a large tribe
B) He was poor and without clan
C) He was a king
D) He had many followers

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's poverty and perseverance, followed by divine victory, confirm that his success was a miracle from Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a situation where you are weak, alone, or opposed, do you genuinely trust that Allah's support is enough, or do you immediately scramble for human solutions? What would it look like for you to 'stand by God' in that situation today?
?
The Prophet refused worldly offers despite extreme poverty. Is there a comfort, status, or relationship you cling to that you know compromises your commitment to Allah? What is one concrete step you can take this week to detach from it and rely on Allah alone?
?
If you truly believed that 'if you do not support Him, Allah will support His Prophet,' how would it change the way you participate in acts of da'wah or service? Are you trying to be indispensable, and what would it mean for you to step back and let Allah's support manifest?

Prophethood
intermediate

Fulfillment of Prophecies as Proof of Prophethood
Maturidi presents fulfilled prophecies as evidence of divine knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the consistent fulfillment of prophecies serves as a distinct proof of prophethood, differentiating the Prophet from soothsayers who rely on devilish whispers.

Core Idea
Perfectly fulfilled prophecies signal divine knowledge, not human trickery.

Imam Maturidi presents a third argument for prophethood: the Prophet foretold events of the unseen, and they came true without fail. This cannot be achieved by human means, whereas soothsayers only mix snatches of truth with lies. Let's examine his reasoning and the Quranic evidence he cites.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice how Maturidi contrasts the Prophet's truthfulness with the deception of soothsayers.
2
Identify the two groups compared
The passage compares the Prophet (who fulfills promises of unseen knowledge) and soothsayers (who receive devilish whispers). Focus on the difference.
Maturidi quotes Quran 26:221-222 to support his point.
3
Analyze the Quranic evidence
Look at the verse quoted: 'Shall I inform you upon whom the devils descend?' How does this reinforce Maturidi's argument about the source of soothsayers' knowledge?
The devils provide only fragments of truth mixed with lies.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
What does the consistent fulfillment of prophecies imply about the Prophet's source of knowledge? Contrast this with human attempts to predict the unseen.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضا مما حاجتهم به ما ظهر من إنجاز الموعود في كل ما نطق به مما هو علم الغيب الذي لا يعلمه إلا الله، ومن رام التوصل إليه ببعض حيل الإنسانية يضل حق ما جاء به فى باطله وصدقه فى كذبه ويحصل أمره على تمويه ومخادعة. قال الله تعالى: هَلْ أُنَبِّئُكُمْ عَلَى مَنْ تَنَزَّلُ الشَّيَاطِينُ، فأخبر أن الكهنة يلقون ذلك من إفك الشياطين مما يختطفون فيحلون على اللمحة من لمح الحق أكاذيب القول.
And also among what he argued against them is what appeared of the fulfillment of the promise in everything he spoke of which is knowledge of the unseen that none knows except God. Whoever seeks to attain it through some human tricks will make the truth of what he brought false in his falsehood, and his truthfulness in his lie, and his affair becomes a matter of obfuscation and deception. God said: 'Shall I inform you upon whom the devils descend?' So He informed that the soothsayers receive that from the lies of the devils which they snatch, and they place upon the flash of a glimpse of truth lies of speech.
Source pages p. 807

Commentary
This passage presents a third proof: the fulfillment of prophecies. Maturidi argues that the Prophet foretold future events (knowledge of the unseen) and they came true. This cannot be achieved by human means; those who attempt it through tricks end up mixing truth with falsehood. In contrast, the Prophet's predictions were consistently accurate. Maturidi contrasts this with soothsayers (kuhhan), who receive some truths from devils but mix them with lies, as indicated by the Quranic verse: 'Shall I inform you upon whom the devils descend?' The soothsayers' knowledge is incomplete and deceptive. Thus, the Prophet's perfect fulfillment of prophecies, without any deception, proves his source is divine revelation, not devils or human guesswork.

Key Terms
إنجاز الموعود (injaz al-maw'ud)
علم الغيب ('ilm al-ghayb)
كهانة (kihana)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think soothsayers have genuine occult knowledge, but Maturidi clarifies they rely on devilish whispers mixed with lies.
Correction: The Prophet's knowledge is complete and true, while soothsayers only snatch fragments of truth from devils and corrupt them with lies.

Checkpoint
How does Maturidi differentiate the Prophet's knowledge of the unseen from that of soothsayers?
A) Soothsayers have more accurate predictions
B) The Prophet's predictions are completely truthful and consistent
C) Soothsayers get knowledge from angels
D) The Prophet used human tricks

Key Takeaway
The perfect and consistent fulfillment of prophecies distinguishes the Prophet from soothsayers and proves his knowledge comes from Allah alone.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet's prophecies were perfectly fulfilled because they came from Allah. In your own life, what are you placing your trust in that may be a mix of truth and deception? Are there 'soothsayers'—people, ideologies, or your own desires—that you follow even partially? What would it mean for you to commit fully to the truth of revelation instead?
?
Maturidi argues that anyone who seeks knowledge of the unseen through human tricks ends up in obfuscation. When you are anxious about the future, where do you turn? Do you resort to human strategies like excessive planning, superstitions, or hoping in your own efforts? How can the Prophet's certainty in Allah's revelation transform your own response to uncertainty?
?
The soothsayers mixed truth with lies, yet people still followed them. In what areas of your faith or practice have you accepted a mixture of truth and falsehood—thinking a little compromise is harmless? How does the purity of the Prophet's message call you to purge any deception from your worship and character, starting today?

Proof from the Prophet's Life and God's Promise
Maturidi presents rational proof from the Prophet's life circumstances.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's lack of worldly support and his eventual victory serve as a rational proof of his prophethood.

Core Idea
The Prophet's triumph without human power proves his mission is from God.

Maturidi begins by citing God's promise 'I will surely prevail, I and My messengers' to establish that the Prophet's victory is divine. He then contrasts the Prophet's poverty, lack of clan support, and initial persecution with his eventual success, showing that his strength came from God alone. This lesson examines that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the Prophet's situation
Read the Arabic and translation to understand the details of the Prophet's circumstances.
Notice the contrast between his lack of means and his ultimate triumph.
2
Identify the obstacles the Prophet faced
List the hindrances: poverty (found poor), no clan support, expulsion, solitary state.
3
See how God's promise is fulfilled
Observe how Quranic verses (e.g., 'And He found you poor and made you rich') show divine intervention.
4
Reflect on the rational implication
Ask: why does this prove prophethood? Because his success cannot be from human means, so it must be from God.
This is a core rational argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لَأَغْلِبَنَّ أَنَا وَرُسُلِي وَبِمِثْلِهِ سَبَقَتْ كَلِمَتُهُ لِعِبَادِهِ الْمُرْسَلِينَ. ثُمَّ كَانَ لَهُ أَيْضًا مِنْ خُصُوصِ حَالٍ أَنْ بُعِثَ إِلَى النَّاسِ كَافَّةً، وَوُعِدَ لَهُ الْغَلَبَةَ وَالنَّصْرَ لِيَعْلَمَ أَنَّهُ لَمْ يَرْجِعْ قُوَّتَهُ إِلَى مَعُونَةٍ بَشَرِيَّةٍ يَتَوَصَّلُ بِهَا طُلَابُ دُوَلِ الدُّنْيَا إِلَى بَغْيَاتِهِمْ مِنْ إِرْثِ مُلْكٍ فِي حَسَبِهِ أَوْ قِنْيَةِ مَالٍ يَسْتَمْتِعُ بِهَا، كَانَ كَمَا قَالَ اللَّهُ: {وَوَجَدَكَ عَائِلًا فَأَغْنَى}. وَلَا عَشِيرَةَ، بَلْ كَانُوا أَشَدَّ النَّاسِ عَلَيْهِ وَأَجْهَدَهُمْ فِي إِطْفَاءِ نُورِهِ حَتَّى قَدْ أَخْرَجُوهُ مِنْ بَيْنِ أَظْهُرِهِمْ طَرِيدًا وَحِيدًا، ثُمَّ مَعَ ذَلِكَ لَمْ يَدْعُوا شَيْئًا مِمَّا تَسُرُّهُ إِلَيْهِ النَّفْسُ إِلَّا أَتَوْهُ، فَلَمْ يَمِلْ إِلَيْهِمْ، بَلْ صَبَرَ عَلَى كُلِّ أَذًى وَاحْتَمَلَ كُلَّ أَمْرٍ صَعْبٍ، إِلَّا بِالْإِجَابَةِ لَهُ فِي الْحَقِّ. قَالَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى: {لَقَدْ جَاءَكُمْ رَسُولٌ مِنْ أَنْفُسِكُمْ}، وَقَالَ: {إِلَّا تَنْصُرُوهُ فَقَدْ نَصَرَهُ اللَّهُ}، وَقَالَ: {وَيَوْمَ حُنَيْنٍ إِذْ أَعْجَبَتْكُمْ كَثْرَتُكُمْ}، وَقَالَ: {وَمَا أَفَاءَ اللَّهُ}، وَغَيْرُ ذَلِكَ مِنَ الْآيَاتِ وَالْأَدِلَّةِ الصَّادِقَةِ أَنَّهُ بِاللَّهِ قَامَ وَبِهِ انْتَصَرَ. وَأَيْضًا مِمَّا حَاجَّهُمْ بِهِ مَا ظَهَرَ مِنْ إِنْجَازِ الْمَوْعُودِ فِي كُلِّ مَا نَطَقَ بِهِ مِمَّا هُوَ عِلْمُ الْغَيْبِ الَّذِي لَا يَعْلَمُهُ إِلَّا اللَّهُ، وَمَنْ رَامَ التَّوَصُّلَ إِلَيْهِ بِبَعْضِ حِيَلِ الْإِنْسَانِيَّةِ يَضِلُّ حَقَّ مَا جَاءَ بِهِ فِي بَاطِلِهِ وَصِدْقَهُ فِي كَذِبِهِ وَيَحْصُلُ أَمْرُهُ عَلَى تَمْوِيهٍ وَمُخَادَعَةٍ. قَالَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى: {هَلْ أُنَبِّئُكُمْ عَلَى مَنْ تَنَزَّلُ الشَّيَاطِينُ}، فَأَخْبَرَ أَنَّ الْكَهَنَةَ يُلْقُونَ ذَلِكَ مِنْ إِفْكِ الشَّيَاطِينِ مِمَّا يَخْتَطِفُونَ فَيَحِلُّونَ عَلَى اللَّمْحَةِ مِنْ لَمْحِ الْحَقِّ أَكَاذِيبَ الْقَوْلِ وَأَبَاطِيلَ الدَّعْوَى. وَالْأَصْلُ أَنَّ الْكِهَانَةَ مَحْمُولٌ أَكْثَرُهَا عَلَى الْكَذِبِ وَالْمُخَادَعَةِ وَالسِّحْرَ عَلَى الشَّبَهِ وَالتَّخْيِيلِ، وَمَا يَأْخُذُ الْأَنْبِيَاءُ يَأْخُذُونَهُ عَلَى أَلْسُنِ الْمَلَائِكَةِ الْبَرَرَةِ مِمَّا لَا يُوجَدُ فِيهَا غَيْرُ الصِّدْقِ وَالْحَقِّ عَلَى التَّجْرِبَةِ وَالِامْتِحَانِ، وَفِعْلُهُمْ حَقٌّ ثَابِتٌ عَلَى مَرِّ الْأَيَّامِ وَالزَّمَانِ. وَلَمَّا كَانَ ذَلِكَ كَذَلِكَ، ثُمَّ وُجِدَ كِتَابُ اللَّهِ نَاطِقًا بِإِظْهَارِ دِينِهِ عَلَى كُلِّ الْأَدْيَانِ، مَا أَخْبَرَ مِنَ الْحَوَادِثِ وَالْأَكْوَانِ مِثْلَ قَوْلِهِ: {هُوَ الَّذِي أَرْسَلَ رَسُولَهُ بِالْهُدَى}، وَقَوْلِهِ: {يُرِيدُونَ أَنْ يُطْفِئُوا نُورَ اللَّهِ بِأَفْوَاهِهِمْ}، وَقَوْلِهِ: {أَمْ يَقُولُونَ نَحْنُ جَمِيعٌ مُنْتَصِرٌ}، وَقَوْلِهِ: {إِنَّا كَفَيْنَاكَ الْمُسْتَهْزِئِينَ}، وَقَوْلِهِ: {قَاتِلُوهُمْ يُعَذِّبْهُمُ اللَّهُ بِأَيْدِيكُمْ}، وَقَوْلِهِ: {أَوَلَمْ يَرَوْا أَنَّا نَأْتِي الْأَرْضَ نَنْقُصُهَا مِنْ أَطْرَافِهَا}، وَقَوْلِهِ: {وَلَا يَزَالُ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا تُصِيبُهُمْ}، وَقَوْلِهِ: {وَإِذْ يَعِدُكُمُ اللَّهُ}، وَقَوْلِهِ: {وَلَقَدْ صَدَقَكُمُ اللَّهُ وَعْدَهُ}. وَمَا جَاءَ مِنَ التَّخْصِيصِ فِي أَقْوَامٍ أَنَّهُمْ لَا يُؤْمِنُونَ وَأَنَّهُمْ أَصْحَابُ الْجَحِيمِ، ثُمَّ مَاتُوا عَلَى الْكُفْرِ، وَغَيْرُ ذَلِكَ مِمَّا فِي كُلٍّ مِنَ الْأَنْبَاءِ الْفَانِيَةِ الَّذِي عِنْدَ التَّدْبِيرِ فِيهَا يُعْلَمُ أَنَّهُ بِاللَّهِ. فَمَنْ تَأَمَّلَ مَا عَدَدْنَا مِنْ أَحْوَالِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ عَلِمَ أَنَّهُ قَدِ انْتَظَمَتْ جَمِيعُ الْبَرَاهِينِ الْعَقْلِيَّةِ الدَّالَّةِ عَلَى نُبُوَّتِهِ، وَصَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَى خَيْرِ الْبَرِيَّةِ.
I will surely prevail, I and My messengers, and similarly His word preceded for His servants, the messengers. Then also from his particular situation was that he was sent to all people, and victory and triumph were promised to him, so that it may be known that his strength was not reliant on human assistance by which seekers of worldly states attain their desires of inherited kingship in his lineage or acquisition of wealth for enjoyment. He was as God said: {And He found you poor and made you rich}. And he had no clan; rather, they were the most severe people against him and the most strenuous in extinguishing his light until they expelled him from among them, driven out and alone. Then despite that, they did not offer him anything that the soul desires except that they brought it to him, but he did not incline to them. Rather, he endured every harm and bore every difficult matter, except for responding to him in truth. God Most High said: {Indeed, a messenger has come to you from among yourselves}, and He said: {If you do not support him, God has certainly supported him}, and He said: {And on the Day of Hunayn, when your great number pleased you}, and He said: {And what God restored}, and other such verses and truthful proofs that by God he stood and through Him he triumphed. Also among what he argued them with was the fulfillment of promises in everything he spoke regarding the knowledge of the unseen, which none knows except God. Whoever seeks to attain it through some human tricks misplaces the truth of what he brought in his falsehood and his truthfulness in his lie, and his affair results in obfuscation and deception. God Most High said: {Shall I inform you upon whom the devils descend?} Thus He informed that the soothsayers receive that from the falsehood of devils from what they eavesdrop upon, and they weave upon the hint of truth lies of speech and falsehoods of claims. The principle is that soothsaying is mostly based on lying and deception, and sorcery on ambiguity and illusion. What the prophets receive, they receive upon the tongues of the righteous angels, in which there is nothing but truth and right, upon experience and examination, and their action is a constant truth over the course of days and time. And since that is so, then God's Book was found to be speaking for the manifestation of His religion over all religions. What He reported of events and occurrences, such as His saying: {He is the One who sent His Messenger with guidance}, and His saying: {They want to extinguish the light of God with their mouths}, and His saying: {Or do they say, 'We are an assembly that is victorious'}, and His saying: {Indeed, We have sufficed you against the mockers}, and His saying: {Fight them; God will punish them by your hands}, and His saying: {Do they not see that We come to the land, diminishing it from its borders?}, and His saying: {And those who disbelieve will not cease to be afflicted}, and His saying: {And when God promised you}, and His saying: {And God certainly fulfilled His promise to you}. And what came of specification concerning groups that they would not believe and that they are companions of Hellfire, then they died in disbelief, and other such matters in each of the [fulfilled] prophecies, through reflection on which it is known that it is from God. So whoever ponders what we have enumerated of the conditions of the Prophet, peace be upon him, knows that all the rational proofs of his prophethood have been gathered together. And may God bless the best of creation.
Source pages p. 807

Commentary
This passage is a composite argument for the prophethood of Muhammad. It begins by citing God's promise 'I will surely prevail, I and My messengers' to establish that the Prophet's victory is divine. Maturidi then contrasts the Prophet's lack of worldly resources—poverty, absence of clan, and initial rejection—with his eventual triumph, proving it is from God. He quotes Quranic verses as evidence. Next, he addresses a potential objection: that prophethood might be confused with soothsaying or sorcery. He distinguishes them by noting that prophets fulfill what they foretell (knowledge of the unseen) without human trickery, whereas soothsayers rely on eavesdropping from devils and mix truth with lies. Sorcery is based on illusion. Prophets receive revelation through angels who convey pure truth, and their actions remain consistent over time. Finally, Maturidi lists many Quranic verses that predicted future events—such as the spread of Islam, victory over enemies, and the fate of disbelievers—all of which were fulfilled. He concludes that for anyone who reflects on these signs, all rational proofs of prophethood are manifest. The passage thus combines logical reasoning from the Prophet's biography and fulfilled prophecies to argue for his divine mission.

Key Terms
نبوة
براهين عقلية
غلبة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what shows that the Prophet's strength was not from human assistance?
A) His miracles
B) His poverty and lack of clan support
C) His many followers
D) His eloquent speech

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's triumph despite lacking worldly means proves his prophethood is from God, not human power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a situation where you have no resources, no support, and are alone, do you trust in God's promise of victory or do you despair? What would it take for you to have the Prophet's certainty?
?
The Prophet was offered everything the soul desires if he would compromise on truth. What desires are you tempted to compromise your faith for today? Will you stand firm like him?
?
In which areas of your life do you rely on your wealth, family, or status rather than on God's direct support? Could you let go of those crutches and depend entirely on Him, as the Prophet did?

Prophethood
intermediate

Distinguishing Prophethood from Soothsaying and Sorcery
Maturidi distinguishes prophethood from soothsaying and sorcery.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi distinguishes genuine prophethood from soothsaying and sorcery, emphasizing the source of knowledge.

Core Idea
Prophets receive pure truth from angels, soothsayers from devils who mix truth with lies.

Maturidi addresses a potential confusion: how can we be sure that prophethood is not like soothsaying or sorcery? He argues that the source of their knowledge is fundamentally different. Prophets receive revelation through righteous angels, while soothsayers get their information from devils who eavesdrop and mix falsehood with a hint of truth. This lesson examines that distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on soothsaying and sorcery
Read the Arabic and translation to understand the definitions and contrasts.
Pay attention to the specific terms used.
2
Identify the key differences
List differences: source (angels vs devils), method, truthfulness.
Prophets: pure truth; soothsayers: lies mixed with truth; sorcery: illusion.
3
Note the consistency of prophethood
Observe that prophets' actions remain true over time, unlike sorcery's fleeting illusions.
4
Reflect on the protective function of this argument
Understand that this distinction safeguards belief in prophethood by removing confusion with similar phenomena.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لَأَغْلِبَنَّ أَنَا وَرُسُلِي وَبِمِثْلِهِ سَبَقَتْ كَلِمَتُهُ لِعِبَادِهِ الْمُرْسَلِينَ. ثُمَّ كَانَ لَهُ أَيْضًا مِنْ خُصُوصِ حَالٍ أَنْ بُعِثَ إِلَى النَّاسِ كَافَّةً، وَوُعِدَ لَهُ الْغَلَبَةَ وَالنَّصْرَ لِيَعْلَمَ أَنَّهُ لَمْ يَرْجِعْ قُوَّتَهُ إِلَى مَعُونَةٍ بَشَرِيَّةٍ يَتَوَصَّلُ بِهَا طُلَابُ دُوَلِ الدُّنْيَا إِلَى بَغْيَاتِهِمْ مِنْ إِرْثِ مُلْكٍ فِي حَسَبِهِ أَوْ قِنْيَةِ مَالٍ يَسْتَمْتِعُ بِهَا، كَانَ كَمَا قَالَ اللَّهُ: {وَوَجَدَكَ عَائِلًا فَأَغْنَى}. وَلَا عَشِيرَةَ، بَلْ كَانُوا أَشَدَّ النَّاسِ عَلَيْهِ وَأَجْهَدَهُمْ فِي إِطْفَاءِ نُورِهِ حَتَّى قَدْ أَخْرَجُوهُ مِنْ بَيْنِ أَظْهُرِهِمْ طَرِيدًا وَحِيدًا، ثُمَّ مَعَ ذَلِكَ لَمْ يَدْعُوا شَيْئًا مِمَّا تَسُرُّهُ إِلَيْهِ النَّفْسُ إِلَّا أَتَوْهُ، فَلَمْ يَمِلْ إِلَيْهِمْ، بَلْ صَبَرَ عَلَى كُلِّ أَذًى وَاحْتَمَلَ كُلَّ أَمْرٍ صَعْبٍ، إِلَّا بِالْإِجَابَةِ لَهُ فِي الْحَقِّ. قَالَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى: {لَقَدْ جَاءَكُمْ رَسُولٌ مِنْ أَنْفُسِكُمْ}، وَقَالَ: {إِلَّا تَنْصُرُوهُ فَقَدْ نَصَرَهُ اللَّهُ}، وَقَالَ: {وَيَوْمَ حُنَيْنٍ إِذْ أَعْجَبَتْكُمْ كَثْرَتُكُمْ}، وَقَالَ: {وَمَا أَفَاءَ اللَّهُ}، وَغَيْرُ ذَلِكَ مِنَ الْآيَاتِ وَالْأَدِلَّةِ الصَّادِقَةِ أَنَّهُ بِاللَّهِ قَامَ وَبِهِ انْتَصَرَ. وَأَيْضًا مِمَّا حَاجَّهُمْ بِهِ مَا ظَهَرَ مِنْ إِنْجَازِ الْمَوْعُودِ فِي كُلِّ مَا نَطَقَ بِهِ مِمَّا هُوَ عِلْمُ الْغَيْبِ الَّذِي لَا يَعْلَمُهُ إِلَّا اللَّهُ، وَمَنْ رَامَ التَّوَصُّلَ إِلَيْهِ بِبَعْضِ حِيَلِ الْإِنْسَانِيَّةِ يَضِلُّ حَقَّ مَا جَاءَ بِهِ فِي بَاطِلِهِ وَصِدْقَهُ فِي كَذِبِهِ وَيَحْصُلُ أَمْرُهُ عَلَى تَمْوِيهٍ وَمُخَادَعَةٍ. قَالَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى: {هَلْ أُنَبِّئُكُمْ عَلَى مَنْ تَنَزَّلُ الشَّيَاطِينُ}، فَأَخْبَرَ أَنَّ الْكَهَنَةَ يُلْقُونَ ذَلِكَ مِنْ إِفْكِ الشَّيَاطِينِ مِمَّا يَخْتَطِفُونَ فَيَحِلُّونَ عَلَى اللَّمْحَةِ مِنْ لَمْحِ الْحَقِّ أَكَاذِيبَ الْقَوْلِ وَأَبَاطِيلَ الدَّعْوَى. وَالْأَصْلُ أَنَّ الْكِهَانَةَ مَحْمُولٌ أَكْثَرُهَا عَلَى الْكَذِبِ وَالْمُخَادَعَةِ وَالسِّحْرَ عَلَى الشَّبَهِ وَالتَّخْيِيلِ، وَمَا يَأْخُذُ الْأَنْبِيَاءُ يَأْخُذُونَهُ عَلَى أَلْسُنِ الْمَلَائِكَةِ الْبَرَرَةِ مِمَّا لَا يُوجَدُ فِيهَا غَيْرُ الصِّدْقِ وَالْحَقِّ عَلَى التَّجْرِبَةِ وَالِامْتِحَانِ، وَفِعْلُهُمْ حَقٌّ ثَابِتٌ عَلَى مَرِّ الْأَيَّامِ وَالزَّمَانِ. وَلَمَّا كَانَ ذَلِكَ كَذَلِكَ، ثُمَّ وُجِدَ كِتَابُ اللَّهِ نَاطِقًا بِإِظْهَارِ دِينِهِ عَلَى كُلِّ الْأَدْيَانِ، مَا أَخْبَرَ مِنَ الْحَوَادِثِ وَالْأَكْوَانِ مِثْلَ قَوْلِهِ: {هُوَ الَّذِي أَرْسَلَ رَسُولَهُ بِالْهُدَى}، وَقَوْلِهِ: {يُرِيدُونَ أَنْ يُطْفِئُوا نُورَ اللَّهِ بِأَفْوَاهِهِمْ}، وَقَوْلِهِ: {أَمْ يَقُولُونَ نَحْنُ جَمِيعٌ مُنْتَصِرٌ}، وَقَوْلِهِ: {إِنَّا كَفَيْنَاكَ الْمُسْتَهْزِئِينَ}، وَقَوْلِهِ: {قَاتِلُوهُمْ يُعَذِّبْهُمُ اللَّهُ بِأَيْدِيكُمْ}، وَقَوْلِهِ: {أَوَلَمْ يَرَوْا أَنَّا نَأْتِي الْأَرْضَ نَنْقُصُهَا مِنْ أَطْرَافِهَا}، وَقَوْلِهِ: {وَلَا يَزَالُ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا تُصِيبُهُمْ}، وَقَوْلِهِ: {وَإِذْ يَعِدُكُمُ اللَّهُ}، وَقَوْلِهِ: {وَلَقَدْ صَدَقَكُمُ اللَّهُ وَعْدَهُ}. وَمَا جَاءَ مِنَ التَّخْصِيصِ فِي أَقْوَامٍ أَنَّهُمْ لَا يُؤْمِنُونَ وَأَنَّهُمْ أَصْحَابُ الْجَحِيمِ، ثُمَّ مَاتُوا عَلَى الْكُفْرِ، وَغَيْرُ ذَلِكَ مِمَّا فِي كُلٍّ مِنَ الْأَنْبَاءِ الْفَانِيَةِ الَّذِي عِنْدَ التَّدْبِيرِ فِيهَا يُعْلَمُ أَنَّهُ بِاللَّهِ. فَمَنْ تَأَمَّلَ مَا عَدَدْنَا مِنْ أَحْوَالِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ عَلِمَ أَنَّهُ قَدِ انْتَظَمَتْ جَمِيعُ الْبَرَاهِينِ الْعَقْلِيَّةِ الدَّالَّةِ عَلَى نُبُوَّتِهِ، وَصَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَى خَيْرِ الْبَرِيَّةِ.
I will surely prevail, I and My messengers, and similarly His word preceded for His servants, the messengers. Then also from his particular situation was that he was sent to all people, and victory and triumph were promised to him, so that it may be known that his strength was not reliant on human assistance by which seekers of worldly states attain their desires of inherited kingship in his lineage or acquisition of wealth for enjoyment. He was as God said: {And He found you poor and made you rich}. And he had no clan; rather, they were the most severe people against him and the most strenuous in extinguishing his light until they expelled him from among them, driven out and alone. Then despite that, they did not offer him anything that the soul desires except that they brought it to him, but he did not incline to them. Rather, he endured every harm and bore every difficult matter, except for responding to him in truth. God Most High said: {Indeed, a messenger has come to you from among yourselves}, and He said: {If you do not support him, God has certainly supported him}, and He said: {And on the Day of Hunayn, when your great number pleased you}, and He said: {And what God restored}, and other such verses and truthful proofs that by God he stood and through Him he triumphed. Also among what he argued them with was the fulfillment of promises in everything he spoke regarding the knowledge of the unseen, which none knows except God. Whoever seeks to attain it through some human tricks misplaces the truth of what he brought in his falsehood and his truthfulness in his lie, and his affair results in obfuscation and deception. God Most High said: {Shall I inform you upon whom the devils descend?} Thus He informed that the soothsayers receive that from the falsehood of devils from what they eavesdrop upon, and they weave upon the hint of truth lies of speech and falsehoods of claims. The principle is that soothsaying is mostly based on lying and deception, and sorcery on ambiguity and illusion. What the prophets receive, they receive upon the tongues of the righteous angels, in which there is nothing but truth and right, upon experience and examination, and their action is a constant truth over the course of days and time. And since that is so, then God's Book was found to be speaking for the manifestation of His religion over all religions. What He reported of events and occurrences, such as His saying: {He is the One who sent His Messenger with guidance}, and His saying: {They want to extinguish the light of God with their mouths}, and His saying: {Or do they say, 'We are an assembly that is victorious'}, and His saying: {Indeed, We have sufficed you against the mockers}, and His saying: {Fight them; God will punish them by your hands}, and His saying: {Do they not see that We come to the land, diminishing it from its borders?}, and His saying: {And those who disbelieve will not cease to be afflicted}, and His saying: {And when God promised you}, and His saying: {And God certainly fulfilled His promise to you}. And what came of specification concerning groups that they would not believe and that they are companions of Hellfire, then they died in disbelief, and other such matters in each of the [fulfilled] prophecies, through reflection on which it is known that it is from God. So whoever ponders what we have enumerated of the conditions of the Prophet, peace be upon him, knows that all the rational proofs of his prophethood have been gathered together. And may God bless the best of creation.
Source pages p. 807

Commentary
This passage is a composite argument for the prophethood of Muhammad. It begins by citing God's promise 'I will surely prevail, I and My messengers' to establish that the Prophet's victory is divine. Maturidi then contrasts the Prophet's lack of worldly resources—poverty, absence of clan, and initial rejection—with his eventual triumph, proving it is from God. He quotes Quranic verses as evidence. Next, he addresses a potential objection: that prophethood might be confused with soothsaying or sorcery. He distinguishes them by noting that prophets fulfill what they foretell (knowledge of the unseen) without human trickery, whereas soothsayers rely on eavesdropping from devils and mix truth with lies. Sorcery is based on illusion. Prophets receive revelation through angels who convey pure truth, and their actions remain consistent over time. Finally, Maturidi lists many Quranic verses that predicted future events—such as the spread of Islam, victory over enemies, and the fate of disbelievers—all of which were fulfilled. He concludes that for anyone who reflects on these signs, all rational proofs of prophethood are manifest. The passage thus combines logical reasoning from the Prophet's biography and fulfilled prophecies to argue for his divine mission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophethood is similar to soothsaying or sorcery, as both involve knowledge of the unseen.
Correction: Maturidi explains that prophethood receives pure truth from angels, while soothsaying mixes truth with lies from devils, and sorcery is based on illusion.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the difference between prophets and soothsayers in receiving knowledge?
A) Prophets receive from angels; soothsayers from devils
B) Both receive from angels but prophets receive more
C) Soothsayers receive from God
D) There is no difference

Key Takeaway
Prophethood is distinct from soothsaying and sorcery because prophets receive pure truth from angels, while others rely on devils or illusions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face uncertainty about the future, do you instinctively turn to trustworthy sources (like the Quran and scholars) or do you find yourself attracted to soothsayers, horoscopes, or 'hidden knowledge'? How can you anchor your heart to the truth that only God knows the unseen?
?
The passage says soothsayers mix truth with lies. Examine the conversations you engage in daily—do you ever pass along information that sounds true but might be mixed with falsehood? What would it take for you to only speak what is consistently truthful, like the prophets?
?
Prophets' actions are 'constant truth over time.' Reflect on your own commitments: Are there areas in your life where your actions and words fluctuate with convenience? How can you seek to be as reliable and truthful as the prophets in your small daily affairs?

Prophethood

Fulfilled Prophecies as Proof of Prophethood
Maturidi enumerates fulfilled Quranic prophecies as proof of prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses fulfilled Quranic prophecies as rational proof of Muhammad's prophethood.

Core Idea
The Quran's accurate predictions about future events confirm it is from God.

Maturidi now turns to the Quran itself as evidence. He lists numerous verses that foretold specific events—such as the spread of Islam, victory over enemies, and the fate of disbelievers—all of which came true. This lesson explores how these fulfilled prophecies, when combined with the previous arguments, form a comprehensive rational proof.

Guided Path
1
Scan the list of Quranic verses cited
Read through the verses Maturidi quotes; note the variety of predictions.
Verses cover triumph, defeat of enemies, fate of individuals.
2
Recognize that these predictions were fulfilled
Recall historical outcomes: Islam spread, enemies were defeated, certain individuals died in disbelief.
3
Understand why this proves divine origin
Consider human limitations: no person can consistently predict specific future events; therefore, this is divine.
4
Reflect on the overall rational proof
Combine this with the earlier arguments to see the full picture of rational proofs for prophethood.

Source Text

لَأَغْلِبَنَّ أَنَا وَرُسُلِي وَبِمِثْلِهِ سَبَقَتْ كَلِمَتُهُ لِعِبَادِهِ الْمُرْسَلِينَ. ثُمَّ كَانَ لَهُ أَيْضًا مِنْ خُصُوصِ حَالٍ أَنْ بُعِثَ إِلَى النَّاسِ كَافَّةً، وَوُعِدَ لَهُ الْغَلَبَةَ وَالنَّصْرَ لِيَعْلَمَ أَنَّهُ لَمْ يَرْجِعْ قُوَّتَهُ إِلَى مَعُونَةٍ بَشَرِيَّةٍ يَتَوَصَّلُ بِهَا طُلَابُ دُوَلِ الدُّنْيَا إِلَى بَغْيَاتِهِمْ مِنْ إِرْثِ مُلْكٍ فِي حَسَبِهِ أَوْ قِنْيَةِ مَالٍ يَسْتَمْتِعُ بِهَا، كَانَ كَمَا قَالَ اللَّهُ: {وَوَجَدَكَ عَائِلًا فَأَغْنَى}. وَلَا عَشِيرَةَ، بَلْ كَانُوا أَشَدَّ النَّاسِ عَلَيْهِ وَأَجْهَدَهُمْ فِي إِطْفَاءِ نُورِهِ حَتَّى قَدْ أَخْرَجُوهُ مِنْ بَيْنِ أَظْهُرِهِمْ طَرِيدًا وَحِيدًا، ثُمَّ مَعَ ذَلِكَ لَمْ يَدْعُوا شَيْئًا مِمَّا تَسُرُّهُ إِلَيْهِ النَّفْسُ إِلَّا أَتَوْهُ، فَلَمْ يَمِلْ إِلَيْهِمْ، بَلْ صَبَرَ عَلَى كُلِّ أَذًى وَاحْتَمَلَ كُلَّ أَمْرٍ صَعْبٍ، إِلَّا بِالْإِجَابَةِ لَهُ فِي الْحَقِّ. قَالَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى: {لَقَدْ جَاءَكُمْ رَسُولٌ مِنْ أَنْفُسِكُمْ}، وَقَالَ: {إِلَّا تَنْصُرُوهُ فَقَدْ نَصَرَهُ اللَّهُ}، وَقَالَ: {وَيَوْمَ حُنَيْنٍ إِذْ أَعْجَبَتْكُمْ كَثْرَتُكُمْ}، وَقَالَ: {وَمَا أَفَاءَ اللَّهُ}، وَغَيْرُ ذَلِكَ مِنَ الْآيَاتِ وَالْأَدِلَّةِ الصَّادِقَةِ أَنَّهُ بِاللَّهِ قَامَ وَبِهِ انْتَصَرَ. وَأَيْضًا مِمَّا حَاجَّهُمْ بِهِ مَا ظَهَرَ مِنْ إِنْجَازِ الْمَوْعُودِ فِي كُلِّ مَا نَطَقَ بِهِ مِمَّا هُوَ عِلْمُ الْغَيْبِ الَّذِي لَا يَعْلَمُهُ إِلَّا اللَّهُ، وَمَنْ رَامَ التَّوَصُّلَ إِلَيْهِ بِبَعْضِ حِيَلِ الْإِنْسَانِيَّةِ يَضِلُّ حَقَّ مَا جَاءَ بِهِ فِي بَاطِلِهِ وَصِدْقَهُ فِي كَذِبِهِ وَيَحْصُلُ أَمْرُهُ عَلَى تَمْوِيهٍ وَمُخَادَعَةٍ. قَالَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى: {هَلْ أُنَبِّئُكُمْ عَلَى مَنْ تَنَزَّلُ الشَّيَاطِينُ}، فَأَخْبَرَ أَنَّ الْكَهَنَةَ يُلْقُونَ ذَلِكَ مِنْ إِفْكِ الشَّيَاطِينِ مِمَّا يَخْتَطِفُونَ فَيَحِلُّونَ عَلَى اللَّمْحَةِ مِنْ لَمْحِ الْحَقِّ أَكَاذِيبَ الْقَوْلِ وَأَبَاطِيلَ الدَّعْوَى. وَالْأَصْلُ أَنَّ الْكِهَانَةَ مَحْمُولٌ أَكْثَرُهَا عَلَى الْكَذِبِ وَالْمُخَادَعَةِ وَالسِّحْرَ عَلَى الشَّبَهِ وَالتَّخْيِيلِ، وَمَا يَأْخُذُ الْأَنْبِيَاءُ يَأْخُذُونَهُ عَلَى أَلْسُنِ الْمَلَائِكَةِ الْبَرَرَةِ مِمَّا لَا يُوجَدُ فِيهَا غَيْرُ الصِّدْقِ وَالْحَقِّ عَلَى التَّجْرِبَةِ وَالِامْتِحَانِ، وَفِعْلُهُمْ حَقٌّ ثَابِتٌ عَلَى مَرِّ الْأَيَّامِ وَالزَّمَانِ. وَلَمَّا كَانَ ذَلِكَ كَذَلِكَ، ثُمَّ وُجِدَ كِتَابُ اللَّهِ نَاطِقًا بِإِظْهَارِ دِينِهِ عَلَى كُلِّ الْأَدْيَانِ، مَا أَخْبَرَ مِنَ الْحَوَادِثِ وَالْأَكْوَانِ مِثْلَ قَوْلِهِ: {هُوَ الَّذِي أَرْسَلَ رَسُولَهُ بِالْهُدَى}، وَقَوْلِهِ: {يُرِيدُونَ أَنْ يُطْفِئُوا نُورَ اللَّهِ بِأَفْوَاهِهِمْ}، وَقَوْلِهِ: {أَمْ يَقُولُونَ نَحْنُ جَمِيعٌ مُنْتَصِرٌ}، وَقَوْلِهِ: {إِنَّا كَفَيْنَاكَ الْمُسْتَهْزِئِينَ}، وَقَوْلِهِ: {قَاتِلُوهُمْ يُعَذِّبْهُمُ اللَّهُ بِأَيْدِيكُمْ}، وَقَوْلِهِ: {أَوَلَمْ يَرَوْا أَنَّا نَأْتِي الْأَرْضَ نَنْقُصُهَا مِنْ أَطْرَافِهَا}، وَقَوْلِهِ: {وَلَا يَزَالُ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا تُصِيبُهُمْ}، وَقَوْلِهِ: {وَإِذْ يَعِدُكُمُ اللَّهُ}، وَقَوْلِهِ: {وَلَقَدْ صَدَقَكُمُ اللَّهُ وَعْدَهُ}. وَمَا جَاءَ مِنَ التَّخْصِيصِ فِي أَقْوَامٍ أَنَّهُمْ لَا يُؤْمِنُونَ وَأَنَّهُمْ أَصْحَابُ الْجَحِيمِ، ثُمَّ مَاتُوا عَلَى الْكُفْرِ، وَغَيْرُ ذَلِكَ مِمَّا فِي كُلٍّ مِنَ الْأَنْبَاءِ الْفَانِيَةِ الَّذِي عِنْدَ التَّدْبِيرِ فِيهَا يُعْلَمُ أَنَّهُ بِاللَّهِ. فَمَنْ تَأَمَّلَ مَا عَدَدْنَا مِنْ أَحْوَالِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ عَلِمَ أَنَّهُ قَدِ انْتَظَمَتْ جَمِيعُ الْبَرَاهِينِ الْعَقْلِيَّةِ الدَّالَّةِ عَلَى نُبُوَّتِهِ، وَصَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَى خَيْرِ الْبَرِيَّةِ.
I will surely prevail, I and My messengers, and similarly His word preceded for His servants, the messengers. Then also from his particular situation was that he was sent to all people, and victory and triumph were promised to him, so that it may be known that his strength was not reliant on human assistance by which seekers of worldly states attain their desires of inherited kingship in his lineage or acquisition of wealth for enjoyment. He was as God said: {And He found you poor and made you rich}. And he had no clan; rather, they were the most severe people against him and the most strenuous in extinguishing his light until they expelled him from among them, driven out and alone. Then despite that, they did not offer him anything that the soul desires except that they brought it to him, but he did not incline to them. Rather, he endured every harm and bore every difficult matter, except for responding to him in truth. God Most High said: {Indeed, a messenger has come to you from among yourselves}, and He said: {If you do not support him, God has certainly supported him}, and He said: {And on the Day of Hunayn, when your great number pleased you}, and He said: {And what God restored}, and other such verses and truthful proofs that by God he stood and through Him he triumphed. Also among what he argued them with was the fulfillment of promises in everything he spoke regarding the knowledge of the unseen, which none knows except God. Whoever seeks to attain it through some human tricks misplaces the truth of what he brought in his falsehood and his truthfulness in his lie, and his affair results in obfuscation and deception. God Most High said: {Shall I inform you upon whom the devils descend?} Thus He informed that the soothsayers receive that from the falsehood of devils from what they eavesdrop upon, and they weave upon the hint of truth lies of speech and falsehoods of claims. The principle is that soothsaying is mostly based on lying and deception, and sorcery on ambiguity and illusion. What the prophets receive, they receive upon the tongues of the righteous angels, in which there is nothing but truth and right, upon experience and examination, and their action is a constant truth over the course of days and time. And since that is so, then God's Book was found to be speaking for the manifestation of His religion over all religions. What He reported of events and occurrences, such as His saying: {He is the One who sent His Messenger with guidance}, and His saying: {They want to extinguish the light of God with their mouths}, and His saying: {Or do they say, 'We are an assembly that is victorious'}, and His saying: {Indeed, We have sufficed you against the mockers}, and His saying: {Fight them; God will punish them by your hands}, and His saying: {Do they not see that We come to the land, diminishing it from its borders?}, and His saying: {And those who disbelieve will not cease to be afflicted}, and His saying: {And when God promised you}, and His saying: {And God certainly fulfilled His promise to you}. And what came of specification concerning groups that they would not believe and that they are companions of Hellfire, then they died in disbelief, and other such matters in each of the [fulfilled] prophecies, through reflection on which it is known that it is from God. So whoever ponders what we have enumerated of the conditions of the Prophet, peace be upon him, knows that all the rational proofs of his prophethood have been gathered together. And may God bless the best of creation.
Source pages p. 807

Commentary
This passage is a composite argument for the prophethood of Muhammad. It begins by citing God's promise 'I will surely prevail, I and My messengers' to establish that the Prophet's victory is divine. Maturidi then contrasts the Prophet's lack of worldly resources—poverty, absence of clan, and initial rejection—with his eventual triumph, proving it is from God. He quotes Quranic verses as evidence. Next, he addresses a potential objection: that prophethood might be confused with soothsaying or sorcery. He distinguishes them by noting that prophets fulfill what they foretell (knowledge of the unseen) without human trickery, whereas soothsayers rely on eavesdropping from devils and mix truth with lies. Sorcery is based on illusion. Prophets receive revelation through angels who convey pure truth, and their actions remain consistent over time. Finally, Maturidi lists many Quranic verses that predicted future events—such as the spread of Islam, victory over enemies, and the fate of disbelievers—all of which were fulfilled. He concludes that for anyone who reflects on these signs, all rational proofs of prophethood are manifest. The passage thus combines logical reasoning from the Prophet's biography and fulfilled prophecies to argue for his divine mission.

Key Terms
إنجاز الموعود
آيات
علم الغيب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Fulfilled prophecies are not strong evidence because anyone can make vague predictions.
Correction: Maturidi cites specific, detailed Quranic predictions that were historically fulfilled, proving divine origin.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what do the fulfilled prophecies in the Quran prove?
A) That Muhammad was a great leader
B) That the Quran is inarticulate
C) That the prophethood is from God
D) That Arabs were skilled poets

Key Takeaway
The Quran's fulfilled prophecies about future events demonstrate that it is from God, confirming Muhammad's prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider a specific prophecy from the list that directly relates to your life today. How does the certainty of God's promises affect your trust in Him for your future?
?
If the Quran's prophecies are so accurate, why do you still struggle to fully trust its guidance in your daily choices?
?
Which of these fulfilled prophecies challenges your own doubts or hesitations about Islam? What would change if you truly believed every word of the Quran as coming from God?

The Method of Arguing Against Selective Belief in Prophets
Maturidi outlines the method to argue with those who accept some prophets but reject others.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's methodological approach to arguing against those who accept some prophets but reject others, particularly the Jews and Christians who denied Muhammad.

Core Idea
Consistency in criteria exposes selective belief in prophets as irrational.

Maturidi now turns to a practical challenge: how to engage with people who accept some prophets (e.g., Moses and Jesus) but reject Muhammad. Rather than simply quoting scripture, he proposes a rational method: ask them for the criterion they used to accept the prophets they do accept. Once they give that criterion, it can be tested against Muhammad's prophethood. This passage sets up that logical move.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Note that the passage is incomplete; it sets up a key question.
2
Identify the two groups mentioned
The passage distinguishes between 'those who affirm the messengers in general' (Muslims) and 'those who deny some of them' (Jews and Christians). Recognize the context.
3
Understand the strategic question
Maturidi suggests asking the deniers about the 'meaning' (criterion) by which they accepted the prophets they do accept. This question forces them to articulate a standard that can then be examined.
This is a rational approach, not merely traditional.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ الْقَوْلُ فِيمَا بَيْنَ الْمُقِرِّينَ بِالرُّسُلِ جُمْلَةً وَالْمُنْكِرِينَ لِبَعْضِهِمْ عَلَى الْإِشَارَةِ أَنْ نَسْأَلَهُمْ عَنِ الْمَعْنَى الَّذِي لَهُ أَقَرُّوا بِهِ أَوْ أَقَرَّ بِهِ سَلَفُهُمْ، فَإِنْ أَشَارُوا إِلَى مَعْنًى عَلَى
Then the discourse concerning what is between those who affirm the messengers in general and those who deny some of them is the suggestion that we ask them about the meaning [criterion] by which they affirmed them or by which their predecessors affirmed. For if they point to a meaning upon...
Source pages p. 808

Commentary
This passage is a methodological statement. Maturidi shifts to a new topic: how to engage with people who accept some prophets (presumably the Jews and Christians who accept Moses and Jesus but deny Muhammad) but reject others. The approach is to ask them for the criterion (al-maʿnā) by which they accepted the prophets they do accept, or that their forefathers used. The sentence is incomplete, but it suggests that once they provide a criterion, the argument can proceed (likely showing that Muhammad meets that same criterion). The passage thus sets up a logical refutation of selective belief in prophets.

Key Terms
مقرّون بالرسل (affirmers of messengers)
منكرون (deniers)
معنى (meaning/criterion)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that accepting some prophets is based on rational criteria, but Maturidi demands consistency: if a criterion is used, it must apply to all prophets including Muhammad.
Correction: Maturidi's method shows that selective belief is arbitrary unless a consistent criterion is applied. By asking for that criterion, he forces the opponent to either apply it uniformly or abandon it.

Checkpoint
What method does Maturidi propose to argue with those who accept some prophets but deny others?
A) Recite Quranic verses to them.
B) Ask them about the criterion by which they accepted the prophets they do accept.
C) Accuse them of ignorance.
D) Present miracles of Muhammad.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi's method shows that selective belief in prophets is based on an inconsistent criterion, and asking for that criterion exposes the arbitrariness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever accepted a belief about religion simply because you inherited it from your parents, without examining whether that same criterion would apply to other truths? What would it cost you to apply the same standard to all claims?
?
Think of a person or group you reject as false. What is your criterion for rejection? If you were forced to state it aloud and apply it to yourself, would you still accept it?
?
This lesson exposes selective belief as irrational. Where in your own life are you being selectively consistent — accepting some truths because they are comfortable and rejecting others because they are costly?

Distinction between Prophethood and Soothsaying with Quranic Evidence
Maturidi distinguishes prophethood from soothsaying and cites Quranic prophecies as proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Maturidi distinguishes prophethood from soothsaying and magic, and how Quranic prophecies serve as rational proofs for prophethood.

Core Idea
Prophethood is verified truth from angels; soothsaying is rooted in deception.

Imam Maturidi begins by contrasting the foundations of prophethood and soothsaying. While soothsaying relies on lies and magic on illusion, prophethood is based on truth received from angels. He then presents Quranic prophecies as concrete evidence that only God could know, demonstrating that Muhammad's prophethood is supported by rational proofs.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the English translation to grasp the overall argument.
Pay attention to the contrast at the beginning.
2
Identify the contrast
Notice how Maturidi contrasts soothsaying and magic with prophethood. What are the characteristics of each?
3
Examine the Quranic verses
The author lists several Quranic verses as prophecies. Reflect on how these predictions serve as evidence for prophethood.
These verses are presented as examples of fulfilled prophecies.
4
Understand the conclusion
See how Maturidi concludes that all rational proofs of prophethood are combined in the Prophet. Why does he say this?
The conclusion ties the evidence together.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأباطيل الدعوى . والأصل أن الكهانة محمول أكثرها على الكذب والمخادعة والسحر على الشبه والتخييل ، وما اختار الأنبياء يأخذونها على ألسن الملائكة البررة مما لا يوجد فيها غير الصدق والحق على التجربة والامتحان ، وفعلهم حق ثابت على مر الأيام والزمان ، ولما أن كان كذلك . ثم وجد كتاب الله ناطقا باظهار دينه على كل الأديان ، ما أخبر من الحوادث والأكوان مثل قوله : هُوَ الَّذِي أَرْسَلَ رَسُولَهُ بِالهُدَى ، وقوله : يُرِيدُونَ أَنْ يُطْفِئُوا نُورَ اللهِ بِأَفْوَاهِهِمْ ، وقوله : أَمْ يَقُولُونَ نَحْنُ جَميعٌ مُنْتَصِرُ ، وقوله : إِنَّا كَفَيْنَاكَ المُسْتَهْزِئِينَ ، وقوله : قَاتِلُوهُم يُعَذِّبُهُمُ اللهُ بِأَيْدِيكُم ، وقوله : أَوَلَمْ يَرَوْا أَنَّا نَأْتِي الأَرْضَ نَنْقُصُها مِنْ أَطْرَافِهَا ، وقوله : وَلَا يَزَالُ الدِّينَ كَفَرُوا تُصِيبُهُم ، وقوله : وَإِذْ يَعِدُكُم يَعِدُكُم الله ، وقوله : وَلَقَدْ صَدَقَكُمُ اللَّهُ وَعْدَهُ ، وما جاء من التخصيص في أقوام أنهم لا يؤمنون وأنهم أصحاب الجحيم ، ثم ماتوا على الكفر وغير ذلك مما في كل من الأنباء الفانية الذي عند التدبير فيها يعلم أنه بالله علمها لتكون آيات له فمن تأمل ما عددنا من أحوال النبي عليه السلام علم أنه قد انتظمت جميع البراهين العقلية الدالة على نبوته ، وصلى الله على خير البرية .
And the falsehoods of the claim. The principle is that soothsaying is mostly based on lies and deception, and magic on ambiguity and illusion. What the prophets bring, they receive from the tongues of the pious angels, in which there is nothing but truth and right verified by experience and testing, and their action is a constant truth over the course of days and time. Since that is so, then the Book of God was found speaking to manifest His religion over all religions, informing of events and existences such as His saying: 'He it is Who sent His Messenger with guidance,' and His saying: 'They want to extinguish the light of God with their mouths,' and His saying: 'Or do they say: We are a victorious multitude?' and His saying: 'Indeed, We have sufficed you the mockers,' and His saying: 'Fight them; God will punish them by your hands,' and His saying: 'Do they not see that We come to the land, reducing it from its borders?' and His saying: 'And those who disbelieved will not cease to be struck,' and His saying: 'And when God promised you,' and His saying: 'And God certainly fulfilled His promise to you.' And what came of specification concerning peoples that they would not believe and that they are the companions of Hellfire, then they died in unbelief, and other such things among the prophecies that pass away, upon reflection of which it is known that they are from God, He taught them to be signs for him. So whoever contemplates what we have enumerated of the states of the Prophet, peace be upon him, knows that all the rational proofs indicating his prophethood are combined. And blessings of God be upon the best of creation.
Source pages p. 808

Commentary
This passage is a proof for prophethood by contrasting it with soothsaying and magic, and by citing Quranic prophecies that were fulfilled. The author begins by stating that soothsaying is mostly lies and deception, while magic relies on ambiguity and illusion. In contrast, prophets receive their messages from pious angels, and their teachings are pure truth verified through experience and consistent over time. Then the author points to the Quran as a book that manifests the religion of God over all religions, and lists several verses that contain prophecies about future events, such as the victory of truth, the protection of the Prophet, and the punishment of disbelievers. These prophecies, along with specific predictions about individuals who would die in unbelief, are evidence that only God could know. Therefore, anyone who examines the conditions of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) will find that all rational proofs of his prophethood are present. The passage concludes with a prayer for the Prophet.

Key Terms
كهانة
نبوة
آيات
براهين عقلية

Key Terms from Source Passage
